%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{K2A: Kinetic Gram Matrix on the Common Left-Handed Family Space}

\section{Goal}

From \(K1\), the common physical left-handed family space has already been isolated as
\[
\mathcal H_L=\operatorname{Ran}(P_L),
\qquad
\dim \mathcal H_L=3.
\]
Moreover, the sector-reduced low-energy dynamics is already known to be a finite Hermitian problem on this same \(\mathcal H_L\).

The next task in \(K2\) is therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{define the kinetic form on }\mathcal H_L,
\text{ prove positive-definiteness,
and canonically normalize it.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Setup}

Choose any basis
\[
\{\phi_A\}_{A=1}^3
\]
of \(\mathcal H_L\).
For each sector \(f\), let \(\mathcal K_f\) denote the projected kinetic operator on \(\mathcal H_L\).
Define the kinetic Gram matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z^{(f)}_{AB}:=\langle \phi_A,\mathcal K_f\,\phi_B\rangle.
}
\label{eq:K2A_Zdef}
\end{equation}

Likewise, let the finite sector-reduced Hermitian family operator be represented by
\begin{equation}
Y^{(f)}_{AB}:=\langle \phi_A,\mathcal Y_f\,\phi_B\rangle.
\label{eq:K2A_Ydef}
\end{equation}

If a family field is expanded as
\begin{equation}
\Psi_f=\sum_{A=1}^3 c_A^{(f)}\,\phi_A,
\label{eq:K2A_family_expand}
\end{equation}
then the quadratic low-energy family action has the generic form
\begin{equation}
L_f^{\mathrm{fam}}
=
i\,c^{(f)\dagger} Z^{(f)} \dot c^{(f)}
-
c^{(f)\dagger} Y^{(f)} c^{(f)},
\label{eq:K2A_family_lagrangian}
\end{equation}
or, equivalently, the generalized eigenvalue problem
\begin{equation}
Y^{(f)}u = E\, Z^{(f)}u.
\label{eq:K2A_generalized_evp}
\end{equation}

Thus the physical meaning of \(K2\) is:
before any sectoral splitting or mixing is interpreted, the metric \(Z^{(f)}\) on family space must first be reduced to the identity.

\section{Theorem 1: Hermiticity of the kinetic Gram matrix}


Assume that \(\mathcal K_f\) is self-adjoint on \(\mathcal H_L\). Then
\[
Z^{(f)\dagger}=Z^{(f)}.
\]



By definition,
\[
Z^{(f)}_{AB}=\langle \phi_A,\mathcal K_f\phi_B\rangle.
\]
Since \(\mathcal K_f\) is self-adjoint,
\[
\overline{Z^{(f)}_{BA}}
=
\overline{\langle \phi_B,\mathcal K_f\phi_A\rangle}
=
\langle \mathcal K_f\phi_A,\phi_B\rangle
=
\langle \phi_A,\mathcal K_f\phi_B\rangle
=
Z^{(f)}_{AB}.
\]
Hence \(Z^{(f)}\) is Hermitian.


\section{Theorem 2: Positivity criterion}

\begin{theorem}[Exact positivity criterion]
Let \(Z^{(f)}\) be defined by \eqref{eq:K2A_Zdef}. Then the following are equivalent:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(Z^{(f)}\) is positive definite;
\item
\[
\langle \psi,\mathcal K_f\psi\rangle>0
\qquad
\forall\,\psi\in\mathcal H_L\setminus\{0\};
\]
\item
\[
\lambda_{\min}\bigl(Z^{(f)}\bigr)>0.
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}


Let
\[
\psi=\sum_{A=1}^3 x_A\phi_A,
\qquad
x\in\mathbb C^3.
\]
Then
\[
\langle \psi,\mathcal K_f\psi\rangle
=
\sum_{A,B}\overline{x_A}\,
\langle \phi_A,\mathcal K_f\phi_B\rangle
x_B
=
x^\dagger Z^{(f)} x.
\]
Therefore positivity of the quadratic form on \(\mathcal H_L\) is exactly positivity of the matrix \(Z^{(f)}\).
For a finite Hermitian matrix, positive-definiteness is equivalent to positivity of its smallest eigenvalue.


\section{Practical sufficient criteria for positivity}

The exact criterion is \(\lambda_{\min}(Z^{(f)})>0\).
For concrete calculations, the following sufficient conditions are useful.

\subsection{Criterion A: perturbation of the identity}

If
\begin{equation}
Z^{(f)}=\mathbf 1_3+\Delta Z^{(f)},
\label{eq:K2A_identity_perturb}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\|\Delta Z^{(f)}\|<1
\label{eq:K2A_norm_small}
\end{equation}
in operator norm, then \(Z^{(f)}\) is positive definite.

\begin{proof}
For any unit vector \(x\),
\[
x^\dagger Z^{(f)}x
=
1+x^\dagger \Delta Z^{(f)}x
\ge
1-\|\Delta Z^{(f)}\|
>0.
\]
Thus \(Z^{(f)}>0\).
\end{proof}

\subsection{Criterion B: strict diagonal dominance}

If
\begin{equation}
Z^{(f)}_{AA}
>
\sum_{B\neq A}|Z^{(f)}_{AB}|
\qquad
\text{for each }A=1,2,3,
\label{eq:K2A_diag_dom}
\end{equation}
and \(Z^{(f)}_{AA}>0\), then \(Z^{(f)}\) is positive definite.

\begin{proof}
Since \(Z^{(f)}\) is Hermitian, Gershgorin's theorem implies that every eigenvalue lies in the union of intervals
\[
\Bigl[
Z^{(f)}_{AA}-\sum_{B\neq A}|Z^{(f)}_{AB}|,
\ 
Z^{(f)}_{AA}+\sum_{B\neq A}|Z^{(f)}_{AB}|
\Bigr].
\]
Under \eqref{eq:K2A_diag_dom}, all such intervals lie strictly in \((0,\infty)\), hence every eigenvalue is positive.
\end{proof}

\section{Theorem 3: Canonical normalization}

\begin{theorem}[Canonical normalization on \(\mathcal H_L\)]
Assume \(Z^{(f)}\) is positive definite. Then:

\begin{enumerate}
\item there exists a unique positive Hermitian square root
\[
Z^{(f)1/2}>0;
\]

\item there exists a unique positive Hermitian inverse square root
\[
Z^{(f)-1/2}>0;
\]

\item after the field redefinition
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c^{(f)} = Z^{(f)-1/2}\,\chi^{(f)},
}
\label{eq:K2A_field_redef}
\end{equation}
the kinetic term becomes canonical:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
i\,c^{(f)\dagger} Z^{(f)} \dot c^{(f)}
=
i\,\chi^{(f)\dagger}\dot\chi^{(f)}.
}
\label{eq:K2A_kinetic_identity}
\end{equation}

\item the family operator becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat Y^{(f)}
=
Z^{(f)-1/2}Y^{(f)}Z^{(f)-1/2},
}
\label{eq:K2A_Yhat}
\end{equation}
so the generalized eigenvalue problem \eqref{eq:K2A_generalized_evp} is equivalent to the ordinary Hermitian eigenvalue problem
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat Y^{(f)}\,\widehat u = E\,\widehat u,
\qquad
\widehat u:=Z^{(f)1/2}u.
}
\label{eq:K2A_standard_evp}
\end{equation}
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Because \(Z^{(f)}\) is finite-dimensional Hermitian positive definite, the spectral theorem gives
\[
Z^{(f)} = U D U^\dagger,
\qquad
D=\operatorname{diag}(d_1,d_2,d_3),
\qquad
d_a>0.
\]
Define
\[
Z^{(f)1/2}=U D^{1/2}U^\dagger,
\qquad
Z^{(f)-1/2}=U D^{-1/2}U^\dagger.
\]
These are Hermitian, positive, and satisfy
\[
Z^{(f)-1/2}Z^{(f)}Z^{(f)-1/2}=\mathbf 1_3.
\]
Substituting \eqref{eq:K2A_field_redef} into \eqref{eq:K2A_family_lagrangian},
\[
L_f^{\mathrm{fam}}
=
i\,\chi^{(f)\dagger}\dot\chi^{(f)}
-
\chi^{(f)\dagger}
\Bigl(
Z^{(f)-1/2}Y^{(f)}Z^{(f)-1/2}
\Bigr)
\chi^{(f)}.
\]
This proves \eqref{eq:K2A_kinetic_identity} and \eqref{eq:K2A_Yhat}.

Finally, from
\[
Y^{(f)}u=E Z^{(f)}u,
\]
multiply by \(Z^{(f)-1/2}\) on the left and set \(\widehat u=Z^{(f)1/2}u\):
\[
Z^{(f)-1/2}Y^{(f)}Z^{(f)-1/2}\widehat u
=
E\widehat u.
\]
Hence \eqref{eq:K2A_standard_evp}.
\end{proof}

\section{Basis form of the normalization}

Equivalently, instead of redefining coefficients, one may define the canonically normalized basis
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde \phi_A
:=
\sum_{B=1}^3
\phi_B\,(Z^{(f)-1/2})_{BA}.
}
\label{eq:K2A_basis_redef}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\langle \widetilde\phi_A,\mathcal K_f\,\widetilde\phi_B\rangle
=
\delta_{AB}.
}
\label{eq:K2A_basis_orthonormal}
\end{equation}

\begin{proof}
By direct substitution,
\[
\langle \widetilde\phi_A,\mathcal K_f\,\widetilde\phi_B\rangle
=
(Z^{(f)-1/2})^\dagger Z^{(f)} Z^{(f)-1/2}
=
\mathbf 1_3.
\]
Since \(Z^{(f)-1/2}\) is Hermitian, this proves the claim.
\end{proof}

\section{Common normalization issue across sectors}

At the sectorwise level, the preceding theorem is complete:
for each \(f\), positivity of \(Z^{(f)}\) implies exact canonical normalization.

However, for a physically meaningful common left-handed flavor comparison across several sectors
(e.g. later up/down comparison), one needs one additional statement:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the compared sectors must share the same left-handed kinetic form}
}
\label{eq:K2A_common_metric_needed}
\end{equation}
or, equivalently, there must exist a common matrix \(Z_L>0\) on \(\mathcal H_L\) such that
\[
Z^{(f)}=Z_L
\]
for all compared left-handed sectors.

If such a common \(Z_L\) exists, then one single normalization
\[
Z_L^{-1/2}
\]
canonically normalizes all compared sectors simultaneously.
This is the physically clean form needed before \(K3\) and \(K4\).

If, by contrast, the sectoral \(Z^{(f)}\) differ, then sectorwise normalization is still mathematically possible,
but a common flavor comparison requires an additional matching theorem identifying the unique common left-handed kinetic metric.

\section{Practical K2A closure theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Practical \(K2A\) theorem]
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(K1\) is already closed at practical theorem level, so that
\[
\mathcal H_L=\operatorname{Ran}(P_L),\qquad \dim\mathcal H_L=3;
\]

\item for the sector \(f\), the projected kinetic operator \(\mathcal K_f\) is self-adjoint on \(\mathcal H_L\);

\item the finite kinetic Gram matrix
\[
Z^{(f)}_{AB}=\langle \phi_A,\mathcal K_f\phi_B\rangle
\]
is positive definite.
\end{enumerate}

Then the sectoral family dynamics admits an exact canonical normalization on \(\mathcal H_L\), given by
\[
Z^{(f)}\to \mathbf 1_3
\]
through the unique positive transformation \(Z^{(f)-1/2}\), and every reduced family operator must thereafter be replaced by
\[
\widehat Y^{(f)}=Z^{(f)-1/2}Y^{(f)}Z^{(f)-1/2}.
\]
Hence \(K2A\) is closed at practical theorem level once the sign of the finite \(3\times 3\) matrix \(Z^{(f)}\) is verified.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from Theorems 1--3.
\end{proof}

\section{Honest status}

What is now closed is the full structural reduction of \(K2A\):

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K2A
\text{ is exactly a finite }3\times3\text{ Hermitian positivity problem.}
}
\end{equation}

What is not yet inserted is the actual microscopic evaluation of the matrix elements
\[
\langle \phi_A,\mathcal K_f\phi_B\rangle.
\]
So, just as in late \(K1\), the remaining frontier is finite microscopic insertion,
not further structural reduction.

\section{Final Summary}

The common family space \(\mathcal H_L\) is already available from \(K1\).
The \(K2A\) task is to define the family kinetic Gram matrix
\[
Z^{(f)}_{AB}=\langle \phi_A,\mathcal K_f\phi_B\rangle
\]
on that space and prove \(Z^{(f)}>0\).

If \(Z^{(f)}>0\), then there exists a unique positive inverse square root \(Z^{(f)-1/2}\), and the family variables can be canonically normalized by
\[
c^{(f)}=Z^{(f)-1/2}\chi^{(f)},
\]
or equivalently the basis can be replaced by
\[
\widetilde\phi_A=\sum_B \phi_B (Z^{(f)-1/2})_{BA},
\]
so that
\[
\langle \widetilde\phi_A,\mathcal K_f\widetilde\phi_B\rangle=\delta_{AB}.
\]

After this normalization, the reduced family operator is not \(Y^{(f)}\) itself but
\[
\widehat Y^{(f)}=Z^{(f)-1/2}Y^{(f)}Z^{(f)-1/2}.
\]

Therefore \(K2A\) reduces completely to the finite check
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{\min}(Z^{(f)})>0.
}
\]

This is the correct next closure point before \(K3\).

\section{K2A Final Summary}

The current stage is \(K2\), and the first mandatory substep is \(K2A\):
construct the kinetic Gram matrix on the common family space
\[
Z_{AB}^{(f)}=\langle \phi_A,\mathcal K_f\phi_B\rangle.
\]

Since \(K1\) already provides the common rank-three left-handed family space
\[
\mathcal H_L=\operatorname{Ran}(P_L),\qquad \dim\mathcal H_L=3,
\]
\(K2A\) is a finite-dimensional problem.

If \(\mathcal K_f\) is self-adjoint, then \(Z^{(f)}\) is Hermitian.
If \(Z^{(f)}\) is positive definite, equivalently
\[
\lambda_{\min}(Z^{(f)})>0,
\]
then there exists a unique positive inverse square root \(Z^{(f)-1/2}\), and the family kinetic form can be reduced exactly to the identity:
\[
Z^{(f)}\to \mathbf 1_3.
\]

The canonically normalized family operator is therefore
\[
\widehat Y^{(f)}=Z^{(f)-1/2}Y^{(f)}Z^{(f)-1/2},
\]
and the generalized eigenvalue problem
\[
Y^{(f)}u=E Z^{(f)}u
\]
is equivalent to the ordinary Hermitian eigenvalue problem
\[
\widehat Y^{(f)}\widehat u=E\widehat u.
\]

Hence the exact mathematical content of \(K2A\) is:
\[
\boxed{
K2A
\text{ is fully reduced to a finite }3\times3\text{ positivity check.}
}
\]

What remains open is not structural reduction but actual microscopic insertion of the matrix elements
\[
\langle \phi_A,\mathcal K_f\phi_B\rangle
\]
on the intended TECT branch.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{K2B: Finite Positivity Criteria and the Common-Metric Obstruction}

\section{Goal}

At \(K2A\), the kinetic form on the common left-handed family space
\[
\mathcal H_L=\operatorname{Ran}(P_L),
\qquad
\dim\mathcal H_L=3,
\]
was reduced to the finite Hermitian Gram matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z^{(f)}_{AB}:=\langle \phi_A,\mathcal K_f\phi_B\rangle.
}
\label{eq:K2B_Z_def}
\end{equation}

The next task is twofold:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(i) give exact and practical positivity criteria for }Z^{(f)},
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(ii) determine when several sectors admit one common canonical normalization.}
}
\end{equation}

The first is a finite matrix question.
The second is the real structural obstruction for later sector comparison.

\section{1. Basis covariance of the kinetic Gram matrix}

Let
\[
\phi'_A=\sum_B \phi_B S_{BA},
\qquad
S\in GL(3,\mathbb C).
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z^{(f)}\mapsto Z'^{(f)}=S^\dagger Z^{(f)} S.
}
\label{eq:K2B_congruence}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Basis covariance and positivity invariance]
Under the change of basis \eqref{eq:K2B_congruence}, positive-definiteness is invariant:
\[
Z^{(f)}>0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
Z'^{(f)}>0.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
For any \(x\neq 0\), define \(y=Sx\neq 0\). Then
\[
x^\dagger Z'^{(f)}x
=
x^\dagger S^\dagger Z^{(f)}Sx
=
y^\dagger Z^{(f)}y.
\]
Hence the quadratic form is positive for all nonzero \(x\) iff it is positive for all nonzero \(y\).
\end{proof}

Thus positivity tests may be performed in any convenient basis on \(\mathcal H_L\).

\section{2. Exact finite positivity criteria}

Since \(Z^{(f)}\) is Hermitian, there are several equivalent exact criteria.

\subsection{Eigenvalue criterion}

\begin{theorem}[Exact eigenvalue criterion]
\[
Z^{(f)}>0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\lambda_{\min}(Z^{(f)})>0.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Standard spectral theorem for finite Hermitian matrices.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Sylvester criterion for the \(3\times3\) family problem}

Write
\[
Z^{(f)}=
\begin{pmatrix}
z_{11} & z_{12} & z_{13}\\
\bar z_{12} & z_{22} & z_{23}\\
\bar z_{13} & \bar z_{23} & z_{33}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

\begin{theorem}[Exact \(3\times3\) Sylvester criterion]
For Hermitian \(Z^{(f)}\), the following are equivalent:
\[
Z^{(f)}>0
\]
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z_{11}>0,
\qquad
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
z_{11}&z_{12}\\
\bar z_{12}&z_{22}
\end{pmatrix}>0,
\qquad
\det Z^{(f)}>0.
}
\label{eq:K2B_sylvester}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
This is the standard Sylvester criterion for Hermitian matrices.
\end{proof}

Therefore \(K2\) is already reduced to a finite scalar check even at the exact level.

\section{3. Practical sufficient criteria}

\subsection{Norm-small perturbation of a reference metric}

Assume a reference positive metric \(Z_\star>0\) is already chosen.
Write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z^{(f)}=Z_\star^{1/2}\bigl(\mathbf 1+\Delta^{(f)}\bigr)Z_\star^{1/2}.
}
\label{eq:K2B_reference_split}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Norm-small sufficient criterion]
If
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|\Delta^{(f)}\|<1,
}
\label{eq:K2B_norm_small}
\end{equation}
then \(Z^{(f)}>0\).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
For any \(x\neq 0\), let \(y=Z_\star^{1/2}x\neq 0\). Then
\[
x^\dagger Z^{(f)}x
=
y^\dagger (\mathbf 1+\Delta^{(f)}) y
\ge
(1-\|\Delta^{(f)}\|)\, \|y\|^2.
\]
If \(\|\Delta^{(f)}\|<1\), the right-hand side is strictly positive.
\end{proof}

In the special basis where \(Z_\star=\mathbf 1\), this becomes simply
\[
Z^{(f)}=\mathbf 1+\Delta^{(f)},
\qquad
\|\Delta^{(f)}\|<1
\Longrightarrow
Z^{(f)}>0.
\]

\subsection{Gershgorin / diagonal-dominance criterion}

\begin{theorem}[Strict diagonal dominance]
Assume \(Z^{(f)}\) is Hermitian and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z^{(f)}_{AA}
>
\sum_{B\neq A}|Z^{(f)}_{AB}|
\qquad
(A=1,2,3),
}
\label{eq:K2B_diagdom}
\end{equation}
with \(Z^{(f)}_{AA}>0\). Then \(Z^{(f)}>0\).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By Gershgorin's theorem, every eigenvalue lies in the union of intervals
\[
\Bigl[
Z^{(f)}_{AA}-\sum_{B\neq A}|Z^{(f)}_{AB}|,
\ 
Z^{(f)}_{AA}+\sum_{B\neq A}|Z^{(f)}_{AB}|
\Bigr].
\]
Under \eqref{eq:K2B_diagdom}, all such intervals lie strictly in \((0,\infty)\).
Hence all eigenvalues are positive.
\end{proof}

This is the most useful branch-level criterion when diagonal dominance comes from weak overlap and exponentially suppressed off-diagonal tails.

\section{4. General form of all canonical normalizations}

Fix one sector \(f\), and consider an invertible linear change
\[
c^{(f)}=N_f\,\chi^{(f)}.
\]
The kinetic form becomes canonical iff
\[
N_f^\dagger Z^{(f)} N_f=\mathbf 1.
\]

\begin{theorem}[Complete classification of sectorwise canonical normalizations]
Assume \(Z^{(f)}>0\). Then all solutions of
\[
N_f^\dagger Z^{(f)} N_f=\mathbf 1
\]
are exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
N_f=Z^{(f)-1/2}U_f,
\qquad
U_f\in U(3).
}
\label{eq:K2B_general_whitening}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
If \(N_f=Z^{(f)-1/2}U_f\) with \(U_f\) unitary, then
\[
N_f^\dagger Z^{(f)} N_f
=
U_f^\dagger Z^{(f)-1/2} Z^{(f)} Z^{(f)-1/2} U_f
=
U_f^\dagger U_f
=
\mathbf 1.
\]

Conversely, if \(N_f^\dagger Z^{(f)} N_f=\mathbf 1\), define
\[
U_f:=Z^{(f)1/2}N_f.
\]
Then
\[
U_f^\dagger U_f
=
N_f^\dagger Z^{(f)} N_f
=
\mathbf 1,
\]
so \(U_f\) is unitary and
\[
N_f=Z^{(f)-1/2}U_f.
\]
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Immediate consequence.}
Sectorwise canonical normalization is never unique.
It always carries an independent unitary ambiguity \(U_f\in U(3)\).

This is harmless inside one sector, but it becomes a genuine obstruction when comparing several sectors.

\section{5. Simultaneous common canonical normalization: exact obstruction}

Suppose we compare several sectors \(f\in\mathcal F\).
We ask whether there exists one single invertible matrix \(N\) such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
N^\dagger Z^{(f)} N=\mathbf 1
\qquad
\forall f\in\mathcal F.
}
\label{eq:K2B_common_whitening}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Exact simultaneous-normalization criterion]
A common canonical normalization \eqref{eq:K2B_common_whitening} exists
if and only if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z^{(f)}=Z^{(g)}
\qquad
\forall f,g\in\mathcal F.
}
\label{eq:K2B_common_equal}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
If \(N^\dagger Z^{(f)}N=\mathbf 1\) and \(N^\dagger Z^{(g)}N=\mathbf 1\), then
\[
N^\dagger (Z^{(f)}-Z^{(g)}) N=0.
\]
Since \(N\) is invertible, this implies
\[
Z^{(f)}-Z^{(g)}=0.
\]
So all \(Z^{(f)}\) must coincide.

Conversely, if all \(Z^{(f)}\) equal one common positive matrix \(Z_L\), choosing
\[
N=Z_L^{-1/2}
\]
gives
\[
N^\dagger Z^{(f)}N=\mathbf 1
\qquad
\forall f.
\]
\end{proof}

So the statement

\[
\text{“each sector is canonically normalizable”}
\]

is strictly weaker than

\[
\text{“all sectors share one common canonical family basis.”}
\]

The second is the one needed for later aligned sector comparison.

\section{6. Common-orientation theorem: scalar multiples are enough}

The previous theorem is exact but too strict if one only cares about a common \emph{basis orientation}.
Indeed, sector-dependent overall positive scalars are harmless.

\begin{theorem}[Common orientation up to sectorwise scalar rescaling]
The following are equivalent:

\begin{enumerate}
\item there exist one invertible \(N\) and positive scalars \(z_f>0\) such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
N^\dagger Z^{(f)}N=z_f\,\mathbf 1
\qquad
\forall f;
}
\label{eq:K2B_scalar_identity}
\end{equation}

\item there exists one positive matrix \(Z_L>0\) such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z^{(f)}=z_f\, Z_L
\qquad
\forall f
}
\label{eq:K2B_scalar_multiple}
\end{equation}
for some positive scalars \(z_f\).
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
If \eqref{eq:K2B_scalar_identity} holds, then
\[
Z^{(f)}=z_f\,(N^{-1})^\dagger N^{-1}.
\]
So all \(Z^{(f)}\) are positive scalar multiples of the common matrix
\[
Z_L:=(N^{-1})^\dagger N^{-1}.
\]

Conversely, if \(Z^{(f)}=z_f Z_L\), choosing
\[
N=Z_L^{-1/2}
\]
gives
\[
N^\dagger Z^{(f)}N=z_f\,\mathbf 1.
\]
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Physical meaning.}
If all sectoral kinetic metrics differ only by an overall scalar, then one common family basis exists.
The remaining sector dependence is only a scalar wavefunction renormalization, not a family-space rotation.

This is already enough to eliminate the dangerous independent \(U(3)\) ambiguities between sectors.

\section{7. Reference-metric reduction theorem}

Assume one sector-independent reference metric \(Z_L>0\) is given on \(\mathcal H_L\), and write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z^{(f)}=Z_L+\delta Z^{(f)}.
}
\label{eq:K2B_deltaZ}
\end{equation}
Conjugating by \(Z_L^{-1/2}\), define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat Z^{(f)}
:=
Z_L^{-1/2} Z^{(f)} Z_L^{-1/2}
=
\mathbf 1+\widehat{\delta Z}^{(f)},
}
\label{eq:K2B_hatZ}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\widehat{\delta Z}^{(f)}
=
Z_L^{-1/2}\delta Z^{(f)} Z_L^{-1/2}.
\]

\begin{theorem}[Reference-metric reduction]
If
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|\widehat{\delta Z}^{(f)}\|<1
\qquad
\forall f,
}
\label{eq:K2B_ref_small}
\end{equation}
then every \(Z^{(f)}\) is positive definite.

Moreover, if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\delta Z}^{(f)}=0
\qquad
\forall f,
}
\label{eq:K2B_exact_common}
\end{equation}
then one exact common canonical normalization exists.

If instead
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat{\delta Z}^{(f)}=\epsilon_f\,\mathbf 1
\qquad
\forall f,
}
\label{eq:K2B_scalar_common}
\end{equation}
then one common orientation exists, with only harmless sectorwise scalar renormalization remaining.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The positivity claim follows from the norm-small theorem applied to
\[
\widehat Z^{(f)}=\mathbf 1+\widehat{\delta Z}^{(f)}.
\]
The second statement is immediate from \eqref{eq:K2B_exact_common}.
The third follows from the common-orientation theorem, since
\[
Z^{(f)}=(1+\epsilon_f)\,Z_L.
\]
\end{proof}

\section{8. Practical K2B theorem}

We may now state the exact theorem-level closure of \(K2B\).

\begin{theorem}[Practical \(K2B\) theorem]
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(K1\) is already closed at practical theorem level, so
\[
\mathcal H_L=\operatorname{Ran}(P_L),
\qquad
\dim\mathcal H_L=3;
\]

\item for each relevant sector \(f\), the projected kinetic Gram matrix
\[
Z^{(f)}_{AB}=\langle \phi_A,\mathcal K_f\phi_B\rangle
\]
is Hermitian;

\item one of the finite positivity tests holds for each \(f\), e.g.
\[
\lambda_{\min}(Z^{(f)})>0,
\]
or the Sylvester test \eqref{eq:K2B_sylvester},
or the norm-small criterion \eqref{eq:K2B_norm_small},
or strict diagonal dominance \eqref{eq:K2B_diagdom}.

\end{enumerate}

Then:

\begin{enumerate}
\item each sector admits canonical normalization;
\item all sectorwise canonical normalizations are of the form
\[
N_f=Z^{(f)-1/2}U_f,
\qquad
U_f\in U(3);
\]
\item a single common canonical normalization exists iff all \(Z^{(f)}\) are equal;
\item a single common family orientation exists iff all \(Z^{(f)}\) are positive scalar multiples of one common matrix.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore \(K2B\) is structurally closed:
the remaining issue is no longer abstract linear algebra, but actual microscopic evaluation of the finite matrices \(Z^{(f)}\) and their mutual relations.
\end{theorem}

\section{9. Honest status}

What is now rigorously closed is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K2
\text{ is not merely “show }Z^{(f)}>0\text{”.}
}
\end{equation}
It splits sharply into two finite questions:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(A) positivity of each }Z^{(f)},
}
\qquad
\boxed{
\text{(B) common-metric relation among the }Z^{(f)}.
}
\end{equation}

Part (A) is completely reduced to finite \(3\times3\) criteria.

Part (B) is the true structural obstruction for later sector comparison:
without a common metric (or at least common orientation up to scalars),
independent sectorwise canonical normalizations leave an arbitrary \(U(3)\) freedom in each sector.

Hence the remaining frontier inside \(K2\) is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{determine whether the actual microscopic TECT branch gives }
Z^{(f)}=Z_L,
\text{ or at least }Z^{(f)}=z_f Z_L.
}
\end{equation}

\section{K2B Final Summary}

At stage \(K2\), the projected family kinetic data are the finite Hermitian matrices
\[
Z^{(f)}_{AB}=\langle \phi_A,\mathcal K_f\phi_B\rangle
\]
on the common three-dimensional left-handed family space
\[
\mathcal H_L=\operatorname{Ran}(P_L),
\qquad
\dim\mathcal H_L=3.
\]

The exact positivity problem is completely finite.
For each sector \(f\),
\[
Z^{(f)}>0
\]
is equivalent to
\[
\lambda_{\min}(Z^{(f)})>0,
\]
and for \(3\times3\) Hermitian matrices it is also equivalent to the Sylvester conditions
\[
z_{11}>0,
\qquad
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
z_{11}&z_{12}\\
\bar z_{12}&z_{22}
\end{pmatrix}>0,
\qquad
\det Z^{(f)}>0.
\]

Useful practical sufficient criteria are:
\[
Z^{(f)}=\mathbf 1+\Delta^{(f)},
\qquad
\|\Delta^{(f)}\|<1,
\]
or strict diagonal dominance.

For one fixed sector, all canonical normalizations are
\[
N_f=Z^{(f)-1/2}U_f,
\qquad
U_f\in U(3).
\]
Hence sectorwise canonical normalization is not unique.

The exact simultaneous-normalization criterion is:
there exists one single invertible matrix \(N\) such that
\[
N^\dagger Z^{(f)}N=\mathbf 1
\qquad
\forall f
\]
if and only if
\[
Z^{(f)}=Z^{(g)}
\qquad
\forall f,g.
\]

A weaker but physically still useful statement is:
there exists one common family orientation, with only sectorwise scalar normalization left, if and only if
\[
Z^{(f)}=z_f Z_L,
\qquad
z_f>0.
\]

Therefore \(K2B\) is structurally closed.
What remains is finite microscopic insertion:
to determine whether the actual TECT branch yields
\[
Z^{(f)}=Z_L
\quad\text{or at least}\quad
Z^{(f)}=z_f Z_L.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{K2C: Microscopic Sufficient Conditions for a Common Left-Handed Kinetic Metric}

\section{Goal}

At stage \(K2\), the kinetic Gram matrices on the common left-handed family space
\[
\mathcal H_L=\operatorname{Ran}(P_L),
\qquad
\dim \mathcal H_L=3
\]
are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z_{AB}^{(f)}=\langle \phi_A,\mathcal K_f\phi_B\rangle,
\qquad
\phi_A\in\mathcal H_L.
}
\label{eq:K2C_Zdef}
\end{equation}

The exact obstruction identified in \(K2B\) is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{a single common canonical normalization exists iff all }Z^{(f)}\text{ are equal,}
}
\end{equation}
and a common family orientation exists iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z^{(f)}=z_f Z_L
\qquad (z_f>0)
}
\end{equation}
for one common positive matrix \(Z_L\).

Thus the \(K2C\) task is to derive \emph{microscopic sufficient conditions} implying precisely this structure.

\section{1. Low--heavy block notation}

Let
\[
Q_H:=1-P_L.
\]
Since \(P_L\) projects onto the common low-energy left-handed family space obtained in \(K1\), every operator \(\mathcal K_f\) admits the block decomposition
\begin{equation}
\mathcal K_f
=
P_L\mathcal K_fP_L
+
P_L\mathcal K_fQ_H
+
Q_H\mathcal K_fP_L
+
Q_H\mathcal K_fQ_H.
\label{eq:K2C_full_block}
\end{equation}

Only the first block enters the family kinetic Gram matrix:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z_{AB}^{(f)}
=
\langle \phi_A,P_L\mathcal K_fP_L\,\phi_B\rangle.
}
\label{eq:K2C_lowblock_only}
\end{equation}

Therefore the exact microscopic question is not the full \(\mathcal K_f\), but only the low block \(P_L\mathcal K_fP_L\).

\section{2. Exact common-metric theorem from low-block factorization}

\begin{theorem}[Exact common metric]
Assume there exists one Hermitian operator \(\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}\) such that for every relevant sector \(f\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal K_f
=
\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}
+
P_L\mathcal R_fQ_H
+
Q_H\mathcal R_f^\dagger P_L
+
Q_H\mathcal S_fQ_H,
}
\label{eq:K2C_exact_common_ass}
\end{equation}
with arbitrary operators \(\mathcal R_f,\mathcal S_f\).

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_L\mathcal K_fP_L
=
P_L\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}P_L
}
\label{eq:K2C_exact_common_proj}
\end{equation}
for all \(f\), and hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z^{(f)}=Z_L
\qquad
\forall f,
}
\label{eq:K2C_exact_common_Z}
\end{equation}
where
\[
(Z_L)_{AB}:=\langle \phi_A,\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}\phi_B\rangle.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Sandwich \eqref{eq:K2C_exact_common_ass} between \(P_L\) on the left and right.
Because
\[
P_LQ_H=Q_HP_L=0,
\]
all terms containing \(Q_H\) on either side vanish after projection, and one gets
\[
P_L\mathcal K_fP_L=P_L\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}P_L.
\]
Taking matrix elements in the basis \(\{\phi_A\}\subset\mathcal H_L\) gives \eqref{eq:K2C_exact_common_Z}.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Meaning.}
This theorem says that \(K2\) does \emph{not} require the full microscopic kinetic operator to be sector-independent.
It is sufficient that all sector dependence sits outside the low--low block.

\section{3. Exact scalar-multiple theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Exact common orientation up to scalar wavefunction factors]
Assume there exists one Hermitian operator \(\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}\), and positive scalars \(z_f>0\), such that for every sector \(f\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal K_f
=
z_f\,\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}
+
P_L\mathcal R_fQ_H
+
Q_H\mathcal R_f^\dagger P_L
+
Q_H\mathcal S_fQ_H.
}
\label{eq:K2C_scalar_ass}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_L\mathcal K_fP_L
=
z_f\,P_L\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}P_L,
}
\label{eq:K2C_scalar_proj}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z^{(f)}=z_f\,Z_L,
\qquad
Z_L:=\bigl[\langle \phi_A,\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}\phi_B\rangle\bigr].
}
\label{eq:K2C_scalar_Z}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Exactly as in the previous theorem:
sandwich \eqref{eq:K2C_scalar_ass} between \(P_L\) and use \(P_LQ_H=0\).
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Meaning.}
This is the most useful exact \(K2C\) theorem.
It identifies the precise microscopic content needed for a common family orientation:
all sectoral differences may be present, but only as
\begin{itemize}
\item a positive scalar \(z_f\), and/or
\item terms that live wholly outside the low--low block.
\end{itemize}

\section{4. Approximate version with a controlled projected remainder}

In practice, one may only have
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal K_f=z_f\,\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}+\Delta_f,
}
\label{eq:K2C_approx_ass}
\end{equation}
where \(\Delta_f\) is not exactly projected away, but its low block is small:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_f:=\|P_L\Delta_fP_L\|.
}
\label{eq:K2C_epsf}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Controlled deviation from a scalar-multiple common metric]
Under \eqref{eq:K2C_approx_ass},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|Z^{(f)}-z_f Z_L\|\le \varepsilon_f.
}
\label{eq:K2C_eps_bound}
\end{equation}
In particular, if \(Z_L>0\) and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_f< z_f\,\lambda_{\min}(Z_L),
}
\label{eq:K2C_eps_small}
\end{equation}
then \(Z^{(f)}>0\).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
For \(x\in\mathbb C^3\), let
\[
\psi_x:=\sum_A x_A\phi_A\in\mathcal H_L.
\]
Then
\[
x^\dagger (Z^{(f)}-z_f Z_L)x
=
\langle \psi_x, P_L\Delta_fP_L\,\psi_x\rangle.
\]
Taking the operator norm on \(\mathcal H_L\) yields \eqref{eq:K2C_eps_bound}.
If \(Z_L>0\), then
\[
\lambda_{\min}(Z^{(f)})
\ge
z_f\lambda_{\min}(Z_L)-\varepsilon_f,
\]
so \eqref{eq:K2C_eps_small} implies positivity.
\end{proof}

\section{5. Localized three-defect criterion}

We now turn the exact block statement into a practical microscopic sufficient criterion adapted to the \(K1B\) geometry.

Let the \(K1B\) basis be chosen from the three localized defect modes:
\[
\phi_A\approx \psi_A,
\qquad
\psi_A(x)=\psi_\star(x-X_A),
\qquad
A=1,2,3,
\]
with pairwise separations
\[
R_{AB}=|X_A-X_B|,
\qquad
R_{\min}:=\min_{A\neq B}R_{AB}.
\]

Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the common operator \(\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}\) is defect-local and identical around each defect core;
\item the diagonal matrix elements are asymptotically the same:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bigl|
\langle \phi_A,\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}\phi_A\rangle-z_0
\bigr|
\le d_0\,e^{-\mu R_{\min}}
}
\label{eq:K2C_diag_bound}
\end{equation}
for all \(A\);
\item the off-diagonal matrix elements are tunneling-suppressed:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bigl|
\langle \phi_A,\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}\phi_B\rangle
\bigr|
\le t_0\,e^{-\mu R_{AB}}
\le
t_0\,e^{-\mu R_{\min}}
\qquad (A\neq B).
}
\label{eq:K2C_offdiag_bound}
\end{equation}
\end{enumerate}

\begin{theorem}[Common localized metric theorem]
Under \eqref{eq:K2C_diag_bound}--\eqref{eq:K2C_offdiag_bound},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z_L=z_0\,\mathbf 1_3+E_{\mathrm{geom}},
}
\label{eq:K2C_ZL_geom}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|E_{\mathrm{geom}}\|
\le
(d_0+2t_0)e^{-\mu R_{\min}}.
}
\label{eq:K2C_geom_bound}
\end{equation}
Hence, if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z_0>(d_0+2t_0)e^{-\mu R_{\min}},
}
\label{eq:K2C_geom_positive}
\end{equation}
then \(Z_L>0\).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Let
\[
E_{\mathrm{geom}}:=Z_L-z_0\mathbf 1_3.
\]
Then
\[
|(E_{\mathrm{geom}})_{AA}|
\le d_0 e^{-\mu R_{\min}},
\qquad
|(E_{\mathrm{geom}})_{AB}|
\le t_0 e^{-\mu R_{\min}}
\quad(A\neq B).
\]
Therefore each row sum obeys
\[
\sum_B |(E_{\mathrm{geom}})_{AB}|
\le
(d_0+2t_0)e^{-\mu R_{\min}}.
\]
Hence
\[
\|E_{\mathrm{geom}}\|
\le
\|E_{\mathrm{geom}}\|_\infty
\le
(d_0+2t_0)e^{-\mu R_{\min}}.
\]
The positivity criterion follows from
\[
\lambda_{\min}(Z_L)
\ge
z_0-\|E_{\mathrm{geom}}\|.
\]
\end{proof}

\section{6. Combined practical (K2C) theorem}

Combining the scalar-multiple reduction with the localized metric theorem gives the practical branch criterion.

\begin{theorem}[Practical \(K2C\) theorem]
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(K1\) is already closed at practical theorem level, so \(\mathcal H_L=\operatorname{Ran}(P_L)\) has dimension three;
\item for each sector \(f\),
\[
\mathcal K_f=z_f\,\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}+\Delta_f;
\]
\item the common operator \(\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}\) satisfies the localized identical-core bounds \eqref{eq:K2C_diag_bound}--\eqref{eq:K2C_offdiag_bound};
\item the projected remainder satisfies
\[
\varepsilon_f:=\|P_L\Delta_fP_L\|.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z^{(f)}
=
z_f z_0\,\mathbf 1_3+\widetilde E_f,
}
\label{eq:K2C_practical_form}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|\widetilde E_f\|
\le
|z_f|(d_0+2t_0)e^{-\mu R_{\min}}+\varepsilon_f.
}
\label{eq:K2C_practical_bound}
\end{equation}

In particular, if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|z_f|(d_0+2t_0)e^{-\mu R_{\min}}+\varepsilon_f
<
z_f z_0
\qquad
\forall f,
}
\label{eq:K2C_practical_positive}
\end{equation}
then every \(Z^{(f)}\) is positive definite.

Moreover, if \(\varepsilon_f=0\) for all \(f\), then
\[
Z^{(f)}=z_f Z_L
\]
with one common positive \(Z_L\), so a common family orientation exists exactly.
If in addition all \(z_f\) are equal, then one exact common canonical normalization exists.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
From the previous theorems,
\[
Z^{(f)}=z_f Z_L + R_f,
\qquad
\|R_f\|\le \varepsilon_f.
\]
Using
\[
Z_L=z_0\mathbf 1_3+E_{\mathrm{geom}},
\qquad
\|E_{\mathrm{geom}}\|\le (d_0+2t_0)e^{-\mu R_{\min}},
\]
one gets
\[
Z^{(f)}=z_f z_0\mathbf 1_3 + \bigl(z_f E_{\mathrm{geom}}+R_f\bigr).
\]
Hence
\[
\|\widetilde E_f\|
\le
|z_f|\|E_{\mathrm{geom}}\|+\|R_f\|
\le
|z_f|(d_0+2t_0)e^{-\mu R_{\min}}+\varepsilon_f.
\]
Positivity follows from the finite perturbation criterion.
The final statements are immediate from the exact/scalar-multiple theorems of Sections 2 and 3.
\end{proof}

\section{7. What this means microscopically}

The previous theorem identifies the actual microscopic content of \(K2C\).

To obtain
\[
Z^{(f)}=Z_L,
\]
it is sufficient that the sector dependence of \(\mathcal K_f\) vanish on the low block:
\[
P_L(\mathcal K_f-\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}})P_L=0.
\]

To obtain
\[
Z^{(f)}=z_f Z_L,
\]
it is sufficient that the only sector dependence surviving on the low block be an overall scalar wavefunction factor:
\[
P_L\mathcal K_fP_L=z_f\,P_L\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}P_L.
\]

In the three-defect localized branch, the natural microscopic mechanism is:
\begin{enumerate}
\item identical defect-core kinetic density,
\item exponentially small inter-defect tails,
\item sector-dependent corrections that either
\begin{itemize}
\item live outside the low block, or
\item are small after projection to \(\mathcal H_L\).
\end{itemize}
\end{enumerate}

Thus the true remaining frontier is not abstract linear algebra.
It is the explicit intended-branch evaluation of:
\[
z_0,\qquad
d_0,\qquad
t_0,\qquad
\varepsilon_f.
\]

\section{8. Honest status}

What is now closed at theorem level is the structural reduction of \(K2C\):

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K2C
\text{ reduces to a finite projected low-block audit.}
}
\end{equation}

No further conceptual obstruction remains inside \(K2\).
The only remaining work is finite microscopic insertion on the actual TECT branch, namely:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{compute the projected low-block part of }\mathcal K_f
\text{ and bound the projected remainder.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The family kinetic matrices are determined only by the low block \(P_L\mathcal K_fP_L\).
Therefore:

\begin{itemize}
\item if all sector dependence lies outside the low--low block, then
\[
Z^{(f)}=Z_L;
\]

\item if the low block differs only by a positive scalar \(z_f\), then
\[
Z^{(f)}=z_f Z_L;
\]

\item in the localized three-defect branch, identical defect cores and exponentially small tails imply
\[
Z_L=z_0\mathbf 1_3+O(e^{-\mu R_{\min}}),
\]
hence
\[
Z^{(f)}=z_f z_0\mathbf 1_3+\widetilde E_f,
\qquad
\|\widetilde E_f\|
\le
|z_f|(d_0+2t_0)e^{-\mu R_{\min}}+\varepsilon_f.
\]

\item if this error is smaller than \(z_f z_0\), every sector is positive definite;
\item if \(\varepsilon_f=0\), a common family orientation exists exactly;
\item if in addition all \(z_f\) are equal, then one exact common canonical normalization exists.
\end{itemize}

Hence \(K2C\) is structurally closed.
The remaining frontier is the finite microscopic evaluation of the projected kinetic low block on the intended TECT branch.

\section{K2C Final Summary}

At stage \(K2C\), the problem is to determine when the projected sectoral kinetic operators
\[
P_L\mathcal K_fP_L
\]
produce one common left-handed kinetic metric.

The exact microscopic sufficient conditions are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item If
\[
\mathcal K_f
=
\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}
+
P_L\mathcal R_fQ_H
+
Q_H\mathcal R_f^\dagger P_L
+
Q_H\mathcal S_fQ_H,
\]
then
\[
P_L\mathcal K_fP_L=P_L\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}P_L,
\]
hence
\[
Z^{(f)}=Z_L.
\]

\item If
\[
\mathcal K_f
=
z_f\,\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}
+
P_L\mathcal R_fQ_H
+
Q_H\mathcal R_f^\dagger P_L
+
Q_H\mathcal S_fQ_H,
\qquad
z_f>0,
\]
then
\[
P_L\mathcal K_fP_L
=
z_f\,P_L\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}P_L,
\]
hence
\[
Z^{(f)}=z_f Z_L.
\]
This gives one exact common family orientation.
\end{enumerate}

For the localized three-defect branch, if the common kinetic core is identical around each defect and the inter-defect tails are exponentially suppressed, then
\[
Z_L=z_0\,\mathbf 1_3+E_{\mathrm{geom}},
\qquad
\|E_{\mathrm{geom}}\|
\le
(d_0+2t_0)e^{-\mu R_{\min}}.
\]
If, moreover,
\[
\|P_L\Delta_fP_L\|=\varepsilon_f,
\]
then
\[
Z^{(f)}=z_f z_0\,\mathbf 1_3+\widetilde E_f,
\qquad
\|\widetilde E_f\|
\le
|z_f|(d_0+2t_0)e^{-\mu R_{\min}}+\varepsilon_f.
\]

Therefore a practical sufficient positivity criterion is
\[
|z_f|(d_0+2t_0)e^{-\mu R_{\min}}+\varepsilon_f
<
z_f z_0.
\]

Hence \(K2C\) is structurally closed:
the remaining work is finite microscopic insertion of the projected low-block coefficients
\[
z_0,\qquad d_0,\qquad t_0,\qquad \varepsilon_f.
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{K2D: Reduction of the Kinetic Audit to a Finite Overlap Data Sheet}

\section{Goal}

At stage \(K2\), the family kinetic matrix is defined on the common left-handed family space
\[
\mathcal H_L=\operatorname{Ran}(P_L),
\qquad
\dim \mathcal H_L=3,
\]
by
\[
Z^{(f)}_{AB}=\langle \phi_A,\mathcal K_f\phi_B\rangle.
\]

The purpose of \(K2D\) is to convert the abstract constants of \(K2C\),
\[
z_0,\qquad d_0,\qquad t_0,\qquad \varepsilon_f,
\]
into explicit finite one-defect / three-defect overlap data.

The result will be an exact finite audit sheet from which positivity of \(Z^{(f)}\) can be checked directly.

\section{Exact projected localized basis}

Assume \(K1B\) is already available at practical theorem level.
Let
\[
\psi_a(x)=\psi_\star(x-X_a),
\qquad a=1,2,3,
\]
be the three localized defect modes generated from the one-defect protected mode \(\psi_\star\).

Define the exact projected localized generators
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\psi_a:=P_L\psi_a \in \mathcal H_L.
}
\label{eq:K2D_psitilde_def}
\end{equation}

Their exact Gram matrix is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_{ab}:=\langle \widetilde\psi_a,\widetilde\psi_b\rangle.
}
\label{eq:K2D_S_def}
\end{equation}

For sufficiently separated defects and a stable low-energy projector \(P_L\), the matrix \(S\) is Hermitian positive definite.
Therefore one may define the exact orthonormal family basis
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\phi_A:=\sum_{b=1}^3 \widetilde\psi_b\,(S^{-1/2})_{bA}.
}
\label{eq:K2D_phi_from_psitilde}
\end{equation}

Then
\[
\langle \phi_A,\phi_B\rangle=\delta_{AB}.
\]

\section{Exact bridge formula from overlap data to the kinetic matrix}

Define, for each sector \(f\), the projected localized kinetic matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^{(f)}_{ab}:=\langle \widetilde\psi_a,\mathcal K_f \widetilde\psi_b\rangle.
}
\label{eq:K2D_Mf_def}
\end{equation}

\textbf{Theorem.}
In the orthonormal basis \(\{\phi_A\}\) of \(\mathcal H_L\), the family kinetic matrix is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z^{(f)}=S^{-1/2}M^{(f)}S^{-1/2}.
}
\label{eq:K2D_exact_bridge}
\end{equation}

\textbf{Proof.}
Using \eqref{eq:K2D_phi_from_psitilde},
\[
Z^{(f)}_{AB}
=
\langle \phi_A,\mathcal K_f\phi_B\rangle
=
\sum_{a,b}
(S^{-1/2})_{aA}^\ast
\langle \widetilde\psi_a,\mathcal K_f\widetilde\psi_b\rangle
(S^{-1/2})_{bB}.
\]
Since \(S^{-1/2}\) is Hermitian,
\[
Z^{(f)}=S^{-1/2}M^{(f)}S^{-1/2}.
\]
\(\square\)

Thus the full \(K2\) input is reduced to the finite matrices \(S\) and \(M^{(f)}\).

\section{Reference decomposition of the projected kinetic matrix}

Assume, as in \(K2C\), that one has a common microscopic reference operator \(\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}\) and positive sector factors \(z_f>0\), so that
\[
\mathcal K_f=z_f\,\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}+\Delta_f.
\]

Define the reference projected matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^{\mathrm{com}}_{ab}:=\langle \widetilde\psi_a,\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}\widetilde\psi_b\rangle,
}
\label{eq:K2D_Mcom_def}
\end{equation}
and the sectoral remainder matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R^{(f)}_{ab}:=\langle \widetilde\psi_a,\Delta_f\widetilde\psi_b\rangle.
}
\label{eq:K2D_Rf_def}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^{(f)}=z_f\,M^{\mathrm{com}}+R^{(f)}.
}
\label{eq:K2D_Mf_split}
\end{equation}

\section{One-defect core datum and exact diagonal/tunneling split}

The natural one-defect on-site kinetic datum is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z_0:=
\frac{\langle \psi_\star,\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}\psi_\star\rangle}
{\langle \psi_\star,\psi_\star\rangle}.
}
\label{eq:K2D_z0_def}
\end{equation}

This is the exact isolated-defect on-site kinetic normalization.

Now define the reference deviation matrix by subtracting the scalar operator \(z_0\mathbf 1\) in the Hilbert metric.
Since the matrix of the identity operator in the non-orthonormal basis \(\{\widetilde\psi_a\}\) is precisely \(S\), the correct subtraction is \(z_0 S\), not \(z_0 I\).

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E^{\mathrm{com}}:=M^{\mathrm{com}}-z_0 S.
}
\label{eq:K2D_Ecom_def}
\end{equation}

Split \(E^{\mathrm{com}}\) into diagonal environment shifts and off-diagonal tunneling terms:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D_{ab}:=
\delta_{ab}\Bigl(M^{\mathrm{com}}_{aa}-z_0 S_{aa}\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:K2D_D_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_{ab}:=
(1-\delta_{ab})\Bigl(M^{\mathrm{com}}_{ab}-z_0 S_{ab}\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:K2D_T_def}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^{\mathrm{com}}=z_0 S+D+T.
}
\label{eq:K2D_Mcom_split}
\end{equation}

Hence the exact projected sectoral kinetic matrix is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^{(f)}=z_f z_0 S+z_f(D+T)+R^{(f)}.
}
\label{eq:K2D_Mf_fullsplit}
\end{equation}

Substituting into \eqref{eq:K2D_exact_bridge} gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z^{(f)}
=
z_f z_0\,\mathbf 1_3
+
z_f\,S^{-1/2}(D+T)S^{-1/2}
+
S^{-1/2}R^{(f)}S^{-1/2}.
}
\label{eq:K2D_Zf_audit}
\end{equation}

This is the exact \(K2D\) audit identity.

\section{Definition of the finite audit scalars}

The abstract constants of \(K2C\) are now identified as finite overlap quantities.

Define:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
d_0:=\max_{a=1,2,3}|D_{aa}|,
}
\label{eq:K2D_d0_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
t_0:=\max_{a\neq b}|T_{ab}|,
}
\label{eq:K2D_t0_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_f:=\bigl\|S^{-1/2}R^{(f)}S^{-1/2}\bigr\|.
}
\label{eq:K2D_epsf_def}
\end{equation}

It is also useful to define the Gram defect
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_S:=\|S-\mathbf 1_3\|.
}
\label{eq:K2D_deltaS_def}
\end{equation}

If \(\delta_S<1\), then \(S\) is automatically positive definite and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|S^{-1}\|\le \frac{1}{1-\delta_S}.
}
\label{eq:K2D_Sinv_bound}
\end{equation}

\section{Finite norm bound}

\textbf{Lemma.}
For the \(3\times3\) matrix \(D+T\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|D+T\|\le d_0+2t_0.
}
\label{eq:K2D_DT_bound}
\end{equation}

\textbf{Proof.}
Each row contains one diagonal entry bounded by \(d_0\) and at most two off-diagonal entries bounded by \(t_0\). Therefore
\[
\|D+T\|_\infty \le d_0+2t_0.
\]
Since the matrix is Hermitian, its operator norm is bounded by the same row-sum bound, hence
\[
\|D+T\|\le d_0+2t_0.
\]
\(\square\)

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bigl\|S^{-1/2}(D+T)S^{-1/2}\bigr\|
\le
\|S^{-1}\|\,(d_0+2t_0).
}
\label{eq:K2D_conjugated_DT_bound}
\end{equation}

\section{Practical positivity theorem}

\textbf{Theorem.}
Assume \(z_f>0\) and \(z_0>0\).
Then
\begin{equation}
\lambda_{\min}\bigl(Z^{(f)}\bigr)
\ge
z_f z_0
-
|z_f|\,\|S^{-1}\|\,(d_0+2t_0)
-
\varepsilon_f.
\label{eq:K2D_lambdamin_bound}
\end{equation}

In particular, if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z_f z_0
>
|z_f|\,\|S^{-1}\|\,(d_0+2t_0)
+
\varepsilon_f,
}
\label{eq:K2D_master_pos}
\end{equation}
then
\[
Z^{(f)}>0.
\]

If moreover \(\delta_S<1\), then using \eqref{eq:K2D_Sinv_bound} it is sufficient to impose
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z_f z_0
>
\frac{|z_f|}{1-\delta_S}(d_0+2t_0)
+
\varepsilon_f.
}
\label{eq:K2D_master_pos_explicit}
\end{equation}

\textbf{Proof.}
From \eqref{eq:K2D_Zf_audit},
\[
Z^{(f)}
=
z_f z_0\,\mathbf 1_3+\mathcal E_f,
\]
where
\[
\mathcal E_f
=
z_f\,S^{-1/2}(D+T)S^{-1/2}
+
S^{-1/2}R^{(f)}S^{-1/2}.
\]
Hence
\[
\|\mathcal E_f\|
\le
|z_f|\,\|S^{-1/2}(D+T)S^{-1/2}\|
+
\varepsilon_f
\le
|z_f|\,\|S^{-1}\|\,(d_0+2t_0)
+
\varepsilon_f.
\]
Now
\[
\lambda_{\min}(z_f z_0 I+\mathcal E_f)
\ge
z_f z_0-\|\mathcal E_f\|,
\]
which proves \eqref{eq:K2D_lambdamin_bound}. The positivity criteria follow immediately.
\(\square\)

\section{Exact special cases}

The previous formula isolates several exact closure points.

\textbf{Case 1: Exact scalar low block.}
If
\[
D=0,\qquad T=0,\qquad R^{(f)}=0,
\]
then
\[
M^{(f)}=z_f z_0 S,
\qquad
Z^{(f)}=z_f z_0\,\mathbf 1_3.
\]
So the family kinetic form is already exactly scalar in the orthonormal family basis.

\textbf{Case 2: Exact common orientation.}
If
\[
D=0,\qquad T=0,
\]
but \(R^{(f)}\neq0\), then the only obstruction is the sectoral projected remainder.
Thus \(\varepsilon_f\) is the exact finite measure of how far the actual branch is from a common orientation.

\textbf{Case 3: Pure geometric obstruction.}
If
\[
R^{(f)}=0,
\]
then all sector dependence is scalar and the only nontrivial finite input is geometric:
\[
S,\qquad D,\qquad T.
\]
In that case \(K2\) reduces entirely to a one-defect on-site datum plus three-defect geometry/tunneling data.

\section{The actual finite input sheet for K2}

The exact \(K2\) microscopic input is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak I_{K2}
=
\Bigl(
S,\ z_0,\ D,\ T,\ \{R^{(f)}\}_f
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:K2D_input_sheet_exact}
\end{equation}
or, in compressed scalar form,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak I_{K2}^{\mathrm{scal}}
=
\Bigl(
\delta_S,\ z_0,\ d_0,\ t_0,\ \{\varepsilon_f\}_f
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:K2D_input_sheet_scalar}
\end{equation}

Thus the abstract constants of \(K2C\) are no longer abstract:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(z_0\): isolated one-defect on-site kinetic datum;
\item \(d_0\): diagonal environment-shift audit;
\item \(t_0\): off-diagonal tunneling audit;
\item \(\varepsilon_f\): projected sectoral low-block remainder;
\item \(\delta_S\): Gram non-orthogonality defect of the projected localized basis.
\end{itemize}

\section{Honest status}

What is now closed is the full reduction of \(K2\) to finite overlap data.
No further abstract operator algebra is needed.

What remains open is only the actual intended-branch evaluation of the finite entries:
\[
S_{ab},\qquad
\langle \widetilde\psi_a,\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}\widetilde\psi_b\rangle,
\qquad
\langle \widetilde\psi_a,\Delta_f\widetilde\psi_b\rangle.
\]

Equivalently, the remaining microscopic work is:
\[
z_0,\qquad
d_0,\qquad
t_0,\qquad
\varepsilon_f,\qquad
\delta_S.
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The family kinetic matrix is exactly reconstructed from projected localized overlap data:
\[
Z^{(f)}=S^{-1/2}M^{(f)}S^{-1/2}.
\]

Writing
\[
M^{(f)}=z_f z_0 S+z_f(D+T)+R^{(f)},
\]
one obtains the exact audit identity
\[
Z^{(f)}
=
z_f z_0\,\mathbf 1_3
+
z_f\,S^{-1/2}(D+T)S^{-1/2}
+
S^{-1/2}R^{(f)}S^{-1/2}.
\]

Hence the practical positivity criterion is
\[
z_f z_0
>
|z_f|\,\|S^{-1}\|\,(d_0+2t_0)
+
\varepsilon_f.
\]

If \(\delta_S=\|S-\mathbf 1_3\|<1\), this becomes the fully explicit scalar test
\[
z_f z_0
>
\frac{|z_f|}{1-\delta_S}(d_0+2t_0)
+
\varepsilon_f.
\]

Therefore \(K2\) is fully reduced to a finite overlap audit sheet
\[
(\delta_S,z_0,d_0,t_0,\varepsilon_f).
\]
No further structural reduction remains.

\section{K2D Final Summary}

The exact projected localized generators are
\[
\widetilde\psi_a=P_L\psi_a,
\qquad
a=1,2,3,
\]
with Gram matrix
\[
S_{ab}=\langle \widetilde\psi_a,\widetilde\psi_b\rangle.
\]
After orthonormalization,
\[
\phi_A=\sum_b \widetilde\psi_b(S^{-1/2})_{bA},
\]
the family kinetic matrix is exactly
\[
Z^{(f)}=S^{-1/2}M^{(f)}S^{-1/2},
\qquad
M^{(f)}_{ab}=\langle \widetilde\psi_a,\mathcal K_f\widetilde\psi_b\rangle.
\]

Introducing a common reference operator \(\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}\) and sector factors \(z_f\), define
\[
z_0=
\frac{\langle \psi_\star,\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}\psi_\star\rangle}
{\langle \psi_\star,\psi_\star\rangle},
\]
and decompose
\[
M^{\mathrm{com}}=z_0 S+D+T,
\]
where
\[
D_{aa}=M^{\mathrm{com}}_{aa}-z_0 S_{aa},
\qquad
T_{ab}=(1-\delta_{ab})(M^{\mathrm{com}}_{ab}-z_0 S_{ab}).
\]
Let
\[
R^{(f)}_{ab}=\langle \widetilde\psi_a,(\mathcal K_f-z_f\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}})\widetilde\psi_b\rangle.
\]
Then
\[
M^{(f)}=z_f z_0 S+z_f(D+T)+R^{(f)},
\]
and therefore
\[
Z^{(f)}
=
z_f z_0\,\mathbf 1_3
+
z_f\,S^{-1/2}(D+T)S^{-1/2}
+
S^{-1/2}R^{(f)}S^{-1/2}.
\]

Defining the scalar audit data
\[
d_0=\max_a|D_{aa}|,
\qquad
t_0=\max_{a\neq b}|T_{ab}|,
\qquad
\varepsilon_f=\|S^{-1/2}R^{(f)}S^{-1/2}\|,
\qquad
\delta_S=\|S-\mathbf 1_3\|,
\]
one obtains
\[
\lambda_{\min}(Z^{(f)})
\ge
z_f z_0
-
|z_f|\,\|S^{-1}\|\,(d_0+2t_0)
-
\varepsilon_f.
\]

Hence a sufficient positivity criterion is
\[
z_f z_0
>
|z_f|\,\|S^{-1}\|\,(d_0+2t_0)
+
\varepsilon_f.
\]
If \(\delta_S<1\), then \(\|S^{-1}\|\le (1-\delta_S)^{-1}\), so it is enough to require
\[
z_f z_0
>
\frac{|z_f|}{1-\delta_S}(d_0+2t_0)
+
\varepsilon_f.
\]

Therefore the entire \(K2\) problem is reduced to the finite microscopic audit sheet
\[
(\delta_S,\ z_0,\ d_0,\ t_0,\ \varepsilon_f).
\]
No additional structural reduction remains.
