\section{Orthodox Placement of the Precision-Enhanced Working Branch}

\section{Two Non-Equivalent Notions of Closure}

To avoid conceptual drift, we must sharply distinguish two different notions of ``closure''.

\paragraph{(i) Structural reduction closure.}
A stage is structurally closed if the original infinite-dimensional problem has been reduced to a finite audit problem with explicitly identified inputs.

\paragraph{(ii) Microscopic acceptance closure.}
A stage is microscopically closed only when the required finite inputs have actually been evaluated on the intended TECT branch and the acceptance inequalities have been verified.

These two notions are not equivalent.
In particular, a coefficient-extraction pipeline may be algebraically closed while the physical CKM program remains only conditionally supported.

\section{Correct Logical Placement of the Precision Pipeline}

The orthodox dependency order for the CKM program remains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K1 \longrightarrow K2 \longrightarrow (K3,K4) \longrightarrow K5.
}
\label{eq:orthodox_chain}
\end{equation}

The finite coefficient-extraction branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
\longrightarrow
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{Bloch}}(k)
\longrightarrow
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
\longrightarrow
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
\longrightarrow
P_*K_iP_*
\longrightarrow
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta),
}
\label{eq:working_precision_branch}
\end{equation}
is an admissible \emph{working branch}, but it is not a substitute for
\eqref{eq:orthodox_chain}.

Its correct role is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{it supplies finite microscopic inputs for }K3,K4,K5
\text{ only after }K1\text{ and }K2\text{ are respected.}
}
\label{eq:working_branch_role}
\end{equation}

Thus the precision-enhanced extraction branch is not discarded, but subordinated to the canonical derivational order.

\section{Why Canonical Kinetic Normalization Cannot Be Bypassed}

Let \(Z^{(f)}\) denote the family kinetic matrix and \(Y^{(f)}\) a raw sectoral family operator in some non-orthonormal family generators.
Under a family-basis change
\[
\psi \mapsto S\psi,
\qquad
S\in GL(3,\mathbb C),
\]
one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z^{(f)}\mapsto S^\dagger Z^{(f)}S,
\qquad
Y^{(f)}\mapsto S^\dagger Y^{(f)}S.
}
\label{eq:basis_congruence}
\end{equation}

Therefore raw overlap matrices or raw texture fits performed before kinetic normalization are basis-dependent.

\begin{proposition}[Orthodox admissibility of the precision branch]
Raw phenomenological textures extracted directly from \(Y^{(f)}\) before canonical normalization are not physical observables.
The physically meaningful reduced family operator is instead
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat Y^{(f)}
=
Z^{(f)-1/2}\,Y^{(f)}\,Z^{(f)-1/2},
}
\label{eq:canonical_Yhat}
\end{equation}
or, equivalently, the generalized eigenvalue problem
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Y^{(f)}u=E\,Z^{(f)}u.
}
\label{eq:generalized_problem}
\end{equation}
Hence any precision extraction protocol must be applied only to canonically normalized family data.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The raw matrix \(Y^{(f)}\) alone is not invariant under the congruence transformation
\eqref{eq:basis_congruence}.
By contrast, if \(Z^{(f)}>0\), then the whitening transformation \(Z^{(f)-1/2}\) is well-defined, and
\[
\widehat Y^{(f)}=Z^{(f)-1/2}Y^{(f)}Z^{(f)-1/2}
\]
is the unique positive-metric reduction of the generalized problem
\[
Y^{(f)}u=E Z^{(f)}u
\]
to an ordinary Hermitian eigenproblem.
Therefore canonical normalization is a logical prerequisite, not an optional polishing step.
\end{proof}

\section{Integration of Protocols A, B, and C into the Orthodox Route}

The proposed precision-enhancement protocols are valid, but their placement must be corrected.

\subsection{Protocol A: Background-Field Completion}

The shift
\[
\Gamma_k^{(2)} \longrightarrow \Gamma_k^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
\]
is not a replacement for \(K1\) or \(K2\).
Its correct function is to improve the microscopic operator entries that later feed into the finite family audit matrices:
\[
M^{(f)}_{ab}
=
\langle \widetilde\psi_a,\mathcal K_f\widetilde\psi_b\rangle,
\qquad
R^{(f)}_{ab}
=
\langle \widetilde\psi_a,\Delta_f\widetilde\psi_b\rangle.
\]
Thus Protocol A belongs to the upgraded microscopic evaluation of the already identified finite inputs.

\subsection{Protocol B: BCC Anisotropy and Multi-Shell Geometry}

This point must definitely be retained.
The BCC condensate breaks full rotational invariance to cubic symmetry, so an isotropic overlap model is not generally trustworthy for precision extraction.

The correct geometric replacement is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
d^2 \longrightarrow x^T G x,
}
\label{eq:anisotropic_metric_replacement}
\end{equation}
with a positive definite anisotropic metric \(G\) induced by the actual BCC working branch.

In the localized defect language, this means that the projected Gram and kinetic data should be modeled by anisotropic, not isotropic, tails; schematically,
\begin{equation}
\langle \psi_a,\psi_b\rangle
\sim
\exp\!\left[-\frac12 (X_a-X_b)^T G (X_a-X_b)\right],
\label{eq:anisotropic_overlap}
\end{equation}
and similarly for the defect-mediated matrix elements entering \(D\), \(T\), and \(R^{(f)}\).

Therefore Protocol B does \emph{not} bypass \(K2\);
rather, it specifies the correct BCC-sensitive microscopic content of the finite \(K2\) and later \(K3/K4\) audit sheets.

\subsection{Protocol C: Literal Blockwise Extraction}

This also should be retained, but with one correction:
literal blockwise extraction is valid only after the family kinetic normalization issue is explicitly under control.

The correct statement is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{OO}\to \lambda_c,
\qquad
\mathcal H_{TD},\mathcal H_{DT}\to \Lambda_E,\Lambda_O,
}
\label{eq:blockwise_extraction}
\end{equation}
but these quantities must be interpreted as entries of the canonically normalized reduced family operators, not of arbitrary raw overlap matrices.

So Protocol C is fully compatible with the current \(K2D\) reduction:
the abstract operator problem has already been reduced to explicit finite matrix-element integrations.

\section{How the Current (K2) Result Fits the Precision Branch}

At the present stage, \(K2\) has already been reduced to a finite microscopic audit sheet.

Using the projected localized generators
\[
\widetilde\psi_a=P_L\psi_a,
\]
their Gram matrix
\[
S_{ab}=\langle \widetilde\psi_a,\widetilde\psi_b\rangle,
\]
and the projected kinetic matrices
\[
M^{(f)}_{ab}
=
\langle \widetilde\psi_a,\mathcal K_f\widetilde\psi_b\rangle,
\]
the canonically normalized family kinetic matrix is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z^{(f)}=S^{-1/2}M^{(f)}S^{-1/2}.
}
\label{eq:K2_bridge_again}
\end{equation}

With the reference decomposition
\[
M^{(f)}=z_f z_0 S + z_f(D+T)+R^{(f)},
\]
this gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z^{(f)}
=
z_f z_0\,\mathbf 1_3
+
z_f\,S^{-1/2}(D+T)S^{-1/2}
+
S^{-1/2}R^{(f)}S^{-1/2}.
}
\label{eq:K2_exact_audit_identity}
\end{equation}

Hence the practical acceptance inequality is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z_f z_0
>
|z_f|\,\|S^{-1}\|\,(d_0+2t_0)
+
\varepsilon_f,
}
\label{eq:K2_acceptance_master}
\end{equation}
where
\[
d_0=\max_a |D_{aa}|,
\qquad
t_0=\max_{a\neq b}|T_{ab}|,
\qquad
\varepsilon_f=\|S^{-1/2}R^{(f)}S^{-1/2}\|.
\]

This means the correct role of the precision-enhancement branch is now completely clear:
it supplies better microscopic evaluations of the finite quantities
\[
z_0,\qquad d_0,\qquad t_0,\qquad \varepsilon_f,
\]
not a replacement for the logical \(K1\to K2\to K3\to K4\to K5\) chain.

\section{Corrected Honest Status}

The status statement should be rewritten in a two-tier form.

\subsection{Program-level acceptance status}

For the full CKM program, the honest status remains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Program-level acceptance: }
K1,\ K2,\ K3,\ K4 \text{ are conditional, while } K5 \text{ remains open.}
}
\label{eq:program_level_status}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Internal structural-reduction status}

However, this must be distinguished from the internal reduction status:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The }K2\text{ problem is already structurally reduced to a finite audit sheet.}
}
\label{eq:internal_K2_status}
\end{equation}

So the blanket phrase
\[
\boxed{\text{Closed: none}}
\]
is too coarse if read as a statement about internal derivational reduction.

The accurate formulation is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{No program-level CKM stage is fully accepted yet,}
}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{some internal stages, in particular }K2,\text{ are already reduced to explicit finite acceptance tests.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{What Should Be Carried Forward}

The following points from the proposed text should be kept and promoted:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the BCC anisotropy obstruction is real and must be incorporated into the overlap geometry;
\item canonical kinetic normalization is logically prior to observational comparison;
\item the precision branch should proceed by literal finite matrix-element extraction rather than symbolic handwaving;
\item Protocols A, B, and C are valid, but only as upgrades of the microscopic finite audit inputs.
\end{enumerate}

The following point must be corrected:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the precision pipeline is a valid working branch, but not the orthodox acceptance chain itself.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The precision-enhancement pipeline should be retained, but only after being subordinated to the orthodox derivational order
\[
K1\to K2\to K3\to K4\to K5.
\]

Its correct role is to improve the finite microscopic inputs entering the canonical family audit.
In particular, BCC anisotropy must enter through an anisotropic metric \(G\), and literal blockwise extraction must be performed on canonically normalized family operators, not on raw pre-normalized overlaps.

Therefore the best honest status statement is two-tiered:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Program-level acceptance: }K1,K2,K3,K4\text{ conditional; }K5\text{ open.}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Internal structural status: }K2\text{ is already reduced to a finite audit sheet.}
}
\end{equation}

What remains immediate is not a new conceptual reformulation, but the explicit intended-branch evaluation of the finite \(K2\) quantities
\[
\delta_S,\qquad z_0,\qquad d_0,\qquad t_0,\qquad \varepsilon_f,
\]
with the BCC-anisotropic working branch inserted from the start.

\section*{Final Summary}

The proposed precision-enhancement branch is useful and should be retained.
However, it must be placed strictly under the orthodox derivational chain
\[
K1\to K2\to K3\to K4\to K5,
\]
rather than replacing it.

Its correct function is to improve the finite microscopic inputs entering the canonically normalized family audit.
In particular:

\begin{enumerate}
\item BCC anisotropy must be incorporated through an anisotropic metric \(G\), not naive isotropic overlaps;
\item canonical kinetic normalization must precede observational comparison;
\item literal blockwise extraction is valid only for canonically normalized reduced family operators.
\end{enumerate}

Thus the honest status is two-tiered:
\[
\text{program-level acceptance: }K1,K2,K3,K4\text{ conditional, }K5\text{ open},
\]
while internally
\[
K2
\]
is already reduced to a finite microscopic audit sheet
\[
(\delta_S,\ z_0,\ d_0,\ t_0,\ \varepsilon_f).
\]

The immediate next task is the explicit BCC-anisotropic evaluation of these finite \(K2\) inputs.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{K2E: Integrated Practical Theorem and Acceptance Sheet}

\section{Goal}

The purpose of \(K2E\) is to combine the results of \(K2A\)--\(K2D\) into one final practical theorem.
At this stage, the problem is no longer infinite-dimensional.
It is a finite acceptance problem built from explicit projected overlap data.

The central question is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{When is }K2\text{ actually accepted on the intended branch?}
}
\end{equation}

The answer splits into two logically distinct levels:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Minimal \(K2\) acceptance:} each sectoral family kinetic matrix is positive definite, so sectorwise canonical normalization exists.

\item \textbf{Aligned \(K2\) acceptance:} the sectoral kinetic matrices are mutually aligned (common metric or at least common orientation up to scalars), so later sector comparison in \(K3,K4\) is physically meaningful.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Finite projected input data}

Assume \(K1\) has already isolated the common left-handed family space
\[
\mathcal H_L=\operatorname{Ran}(P_L),
\qquad
\dim \mathcal H_L=3.
\]

Let the projected localized generators be
\[
\widetilde\psi_a:=P_L\psi_a,
\qquad
a=1,2,3.
\]

Define the exact Gram matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_{ab}:=\langle \widetilde\psi_a,\widetilde\psi_b\rangle,
}
\label{eq:K2E_S}
\end{equation}
and, for each sector \(f\), the projected kinetic matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^{(f)}_{ab}:=\langle \widetilde\psi_a,\mathcal K_f\widetilde\psi_b\rangle.
}
\label{eq:K2E_Mf}
\end{equation}

Whenever \(S>0\), define the orthonormal family basis by
\[
\phi_A=\sum_b \widetilde\psi_b\,(S^{-1/2})_{bA}.
\]
Then the canonically relevant family kinetic matrix is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z^{(f)}=S^{-1/2}M^{(f)}S^{-1/2}.
}
\label{eq:K2E_bridge}
\end{equation}

Thus the exact microscopic input of \(K2\) is simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak I_{K2}^{\mathrm{exact}}
=
\bigl(S,\{M^{(f)}\}_f\bigr).
}
\label{eq:K2E_exact_input}
\end{equation}

\section{Reference decomposition}

Assume one has a common reference kinetic operator \(\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}\) and sector factors \(z_f>0\), so that
\[
\mathcal K_f=z_f\,\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}+\Delta_f.
\]

Let
\[
M^{\mathrm{com}}_{ab}:=
\langle \widetilde\psi_a,\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}\widetilde\psi_b\rangle.
\]

Define the isolated one-defect on-site kinetic datum
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z_0:=
\frac{\langle \psi_\star,\mathcal K_{\mathrm{com}}\psi_\star\rangle}
{\langle \psi_\star,\psi_\star\rangle}.
}
\label{eq:K2E_z0}
\end{equation}

Then decompose
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^{\mathrm{com}}=z_0 S + D + T,
}
\label{eq:K2E_Mcom_split}
\end{equation}
where
\[
D_{ab}:=\delta_{ab}\bigl(M^{\mathrm{com}}_{aa}-z_0S_{aa}\bigr),
\qquad
T_{ab}:=(1-\delta_{ab})\bigl(M^{\mathrm{com}}_{ab}-z_0S_{ab}\bigr).
\]

Also define the projected sectoral remainder
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R^{(f)}:=M^{(f)}-z_f M^{\mathrm{com}}.
}
\label{eq:K2E_Rf}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^{(f)}=z_f z_0 S + z_f(D+T)+R^{(f)}.
}
\label{eq:K2E_Mf_split}
\end{equation}

Substituting this into \eqref{eq:K2E_bridge} yields the exact audit identity
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z^{(f)}
=
z_f z_0\,\mathbf 1_3
+
z_f\,A
+
B_f,
}
\label{eq:K2E_Zf_split}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A:=S^{-1/2}(D+T)S^{-1/2},
\qquad
B_f:=S^{-1/2}R^{(f)}S^{-1/2}.
}
\label{eq:K2E_A_Bf}
\end{equation}

\section{Compressed scalar audit data}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_S:=\|S-\mathbf 1_3\|,
\qquad
d_0:=\max_a |D_{aa}|,
\qquad
t_0:=\max_{a\neq b}|T_{ab}|,
\qquad
\varepsilon_f:=\|B_f\|.
}
\label{eq:K2E_scalar_data}
\end{equation}

If \(\delta_S<1\), then \(S>0\) automatically and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|S^{-1}\|\le \frac{1}{1-\delta_S}.
}
\label{eq:K2E_Sinv_bound}
\end{equation}

Moreover,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|A\|
\le
\|S^{-1}\|(d_0+2t_0).
}
\label{eq:K2E_A_bound}
\end{equation}

\begin{proof}
Since
\[
\|D+T\|\le d_0+2t_0,
\]
one has
\[
\|A\|
=
\|S^{-1/2}(D+T)S^{-1/2}\|
\le
\|S^{-1}\|\,\|D+T\|
\le
\|S^{-1}\|(d_0+2t_0).
\]
\end{proof}

\section{Integrated Practical \(K2\) Theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Integrated practical \(K2\) theorem]
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(K1\) is available at practical theorem level, so \(\mathcal H_L=\operatorname{Ran}(P_L)\) is a common rank-three left-handed family space;
\item the projected localized Gram matrix \(S\) is positive definite;
\item for each sector \(f\), the projected kinetic matrix \(M^{(f)}\) is Hermitian;
\item the decomposition \eqref{eq:K2E_Mf_split} is available.
\end{enumerate}

Then the following hold.

\paragraph{(a) Exact bridge.}
The family kinetic matrix is exactly
\[
Z^{(f)}=S^{-1/2}M^{(f)}S^{-1/2}.
\]

\paragraph{(b) Sectorwise positivity bound.}
For every sector \(f\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{\min}(Z^{(f)})
\ge
z_f z_0
-
|z_f|\,\|S^{-1}\|(d_0+2t_0)
-
\varepsilon_f.
}
\label{eq:K2E_lambda_bound}
\end{equation}

Hence, if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z_f z_0
>
|z_f|\,\|S^{-1}\|(d_0+2t_0)
+
\varepsilon_f,
}
\label{eq:K2E_sector_accept}
\end{equation}
then
\[
Z^{(f)}>0.
\]

\paragraph{(c) Explicit scalar sufficient test.}
If \(\delta_S<1\), then it is sufficient to require
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z_f z_0
>
\frac{|z_f|}{1-\delta_S}(d_0+2t_0)
+
\varepsilon_f.
}
\label{eq:K2E_sector_accept_explicit}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(d) Sectorwise canonical normalization.}
Whenever \(Z^{(f)}>0\), all canonical normalizations of the sector \(f\) are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
N_f=Z^{(f)-1/2}U_f,
\qquad
U_f\in U(3).
}
\label{eq:K2E_sectorwise_whitening}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(e) Exact common metric criterion.}
A single common canonical normalization exists for all compared sectors iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^{(f)}=M^{(g)}
\qquad
\forall f,g.
}
\label{eq:K2E_common_metric_M}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\[
Z^{(f)}=Z^{(g)}
\qquad
\forall f,g.
\]

\paragraph{(f) Exact common orientation criterion.}
A common family orientation exists iff there are positive scalars \(c_f\) and one positive Hermitian matrix \(M_L\) such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^{(f)}=c_f\,M_L
\qquad
\forall f.
}
\label{eq:K2E_common_orientation_M}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\[
Z^{(f)}=c_f\,Z_L,
\qquad
Z_L:=S^{-1/2}M_LS^{-1/2}>0.
\]
\end{theorem}


Parts (a)--(d) are immediate from the exact bridge identity and the norm bound above.
For part (e), since \(S^{-1/2}\) is invertible,
\[
Z^{(f)}=Z^{(g)}
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
M^{(f)}=M^{(g)}.
\]
Likewise, for part (f),
\[
Z^{(f)}=c_f Z_L
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
M^{(f)}=c_f(S^{1/2}Z_LS^{1/2})=:c_f M_L.
\]


\section{Practical Alignment Theorem}

Exact equality is too strong for numerical intended-branch work.
So one also needs a tolerance-based aligned criterion.

Let \(M_L>0\) be a chosen reference matrix and \(c_f>0\) chosen sectorwise scalars.
Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_f:=
\bigl\|
S^{-1/2}(M^{(f)}-c_fM_L)S^{-1/2}
\bigr\|.
}
\label{eq:K2E_etaf}
\end{equation}
Also define
\[
Z_L:=S^{-1/2}M_LS^{-1/2}>0.
\]

[Tolerance-based common orientation test]
If
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\eta_f < c_f\,\lambda_{\min}(Z_L)
\qquad
\forall f,
}
\label{eq:K2E_alignment_accept}
\end{equation}
then every \(Z^{(f)}\) is positive definite and satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|Z^{(f)}-c_f Z_L\|\le \eta_f.
}
\label{eq:K2E_orientation_defect}
\end{equation}

In particular:
\begin{itemize}
\item if \(\eta_f=0\) for all \(f\), exact common orientation is achieved;
\item if \(\eta_f\) is merely small, then the kinetic misalignment is quantitatively controlled.
\end{itemize}



By definition,
\[
Z^{(f)}=c_f Z_L + E_f,
\qquad
\|E_f\|=\eta_f.
\]
Therefore
\[
\lambda_{\min}(Z^{(f)})
\ge
c_f\lambda_{\min}(Z_L)-\eta_f.
\]
Hence \eqref{eq:K2E_alignment_accept} implies positivity.
The norm bound is immediate.


\section{K2 Acceptance Sheet}

The exact acceptance problem is now finite.

\paragraph{Level 0: Structural input availability.}
The following exact matrices must be computed on the intended branch:
\[
S,\qquad M^{(f)}.
\]

\paragraph{Level 1: Gram admissibility.}
Either verify \(S>0\) directly, or verify the practical sufficient condition
\[
\delta_S<1.
\]

\paragraph{Level 2: Minimal \(K2\) acceptance (sectorwise canonical kinetics).}
For every relevant sector \(f\), accept \(K2_{\min}\) if either
\[
\lambda_{\min}(Z^{(f)})>0
\]
is checked directly from \(Z^{(f)}=S^{-1/2}M^{(f)}S^{-1/2}\),
or the sufficient inequality
\[
z_f z_0
>
|z_f|\,\|S^{-1}\|(d_0+2t_0)+\varepsilon_f
\]
is satisfied.
A fully explicit sufficient version is
\[
z_f z_0
>
\frac{|z_f|}{1-\delta_S}(d_0+2t_0)+\varepsilon_f.
\]

\paragraph{Level 3: Aligned \(K2\) acceptance for later sector comparison.}
Accept \(K2_{\mathrm{align}}\) at one of the following strengths.

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Exact common metric:}
\[
M^{(f)}=M^{(g)}
\quad
\forall f,g.
\]

\item \textbf{Exact common orientation:}
\[
M^{(f)}=c_f M_L
\quad
\forall f
\]
for some \(c_f>0\), \(M_L>0\).

\item \textbf{Tolerance-based common orientation:}
\[
\eta_f
=
\bigl\|
S^{-1/2}(M^{(f)}-c_fM_L)S^{-1/2}
\bigr\|
<
c_f\lambda_{\min}(Z_L).
\]
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Level 4: Program-level interpretation.}
Passing Level 2 means:
\[
\boxed{
K2\text{ is accepted at the minimal sectorwise canonical-normalization level.}
}
\]
Passing Level 3 means:
\[
\boxed{
K2\text{ is accepted at the aligned level required for clean }K3,K4\text{ sector comparison.}
}
\]

\section{Honest Status}

The correct honest status is now:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Structurally, }K2\text{ is closed: it has been reduced to a finite acceptance sheet.}
}
\end{equation}

But microscopically, \(K2\) is accepted only after the intended-branch finite inputs are actually inserted and the required inequalities are verified.

Therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Structural status of }K2:\ \text{closed.}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Microscopic acceptance status of }K2:\ \text{still conditional until the finite audit is executed.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The entire \(K2\) problem has now been reduced to the finite matrices
\[
S,\qquad M^{(f)},
\]
or equivalently to the compressed audit data
\[
\delta_S,\qquad z_0,\qquad d_0,\qquad t_0,\qquad \varepsilon_f,
\qquad \eta_f.
\]

The exact bridge formula is
\[
Z^{(f)}=S^{-1/2}M^{(f)}S^{-1/2}.
\]

Minimal \(K2\) acceptance is obtained by proving \(Z^{(f)}>0\) sectorwise, for example through
\[
z_f z_0
>
|z_f|\,\|S^{-1}\|(d_0+2t_0)+\varepsilon_f.
\]

Aligned \(K2\) acceptance is stronger and requires either:
\[
M^{(f)}=M^{(g)},
\qquad\text{or}\qquad
M^{(f)}=c_f M_L,
\]
or the tolerance-based variant
\[
\bigl\|
S^{-1/2}(M^{(f)}-c_fM_L)S^{-1/2}
\bigr\|
<
c_f\lambda_{\min}(Z_L).
\]

Hence \(K2\) is no longer an open structural problem.
It is an explicit finite microscopic acceptance audit.

\section*{K2E Final Summary}

The \(K2\) problem is now completely reduced to a finite microscopic acceptance audit.

The exact projected input is
\[
\mathfrak I_{K2}^{\mathrm{exact}}
=
\bigl(S,\{M^{(f)}\}_f\bigr),
\]
with
\[
S_{ab}=\langle \widetilde\psi_a,\widetilde\psi_b\rangle,
\qquad
M^{(f)}_{ab}=\langle \widetilde\psi_a,\mathcal K_f\widetilde\psi_b\rangle.
\]

The family kinetic matrices are exactly
\[
Z^{(f)}=S^{-1/2}M^{(f)}S^{-1/2}.
\]

A practical sufficient positivity criterion is
\[
z_f z_0
>
|z_f|\,\|S^{-1}\|(d_0+2t_0)+\varepsilon_f,
\]
or, if \(\delta_S<1\),
\[
z_f z_0
>
\frac{|z_f|}{1-\delta_S}(d_0+2t_0)+\varepsilon_f.
\]

Thus minimal \(K2\) acceptance means:
\[
Z^{(f)}>0
\qquad
\forall f.
\]

For aligned sector comparison, one needs the stronger conditions:
\[
M^{(f)}=M^{(g)}
\quad\text{(exact common metric),}
\]
or
\[
M^{(f)}=c_f M_L
\quad\text{(exact common orientation),}
\]
or the tolerance-based bound
\[
\bigl\|
S^{-1/2}(M^{(f)}-c_fM_L)S^{-1/2}
\bigr\|
<
c_f\lambda_{\min}(Z_L).
\]

Therefore the honest status is:
\[
\text{structurally, }K2\text{ is closed;}
\qquad
\text{microscopically, }K2\text{ remains conditional until the finite audit is executed.}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{K3A: Nondegenerate Splitting Criterion for Canonically Normalized Family Operators}

\section{Goal}

After \(K2\), each sector \(f\) is described by the canonically normalized family operator
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat Y^{(f)}:=Z^{(f)-1/2}Y^{(f)}Z^{(f)-1/2},
}
\label{eq:K3A_Yhat_def}
\end{equation}
provided \(Z^{(f)}>0\).

The purpose of \(K3A\) is to determine when \(\widehat Y^{(f)}\) has a simple three-level spectrum,
i.e. when the three family eigenvalues are all distinct.

This is the minimal splitting problem.
It is logically prior to any hierarchy comparison between different sectors.

\section{1. Logical dependence on \(K2\)}

\begin{proposition}[What \(K2\) is needed for \(K3A\)]
The minimal \(K3A\) problem for one fixed sector \(f\) requires only \(K2_{\min}\), namely
\[
Z^{(f)}>0.
\]
In that case \(\widehat Y^{(f)}\) is well-defined and Hermitian whenever \(Y^{(f)}\) is Hermitian.

By contrast, comparison of splittings across sectors in one common family basis requires the stronger aligned form \(K2_{\mathrm{align}}\).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
If \(Z^{(f)}>0\), then \(Z^{(f)-1/2}\) exists and \eqref{eq:K3A_Yhat_def} is well-defined.
Since \(Z^{(f)-1/2}\) is Hermitian, Hermiticity of \(Y^{(f)}\) implies Hermiticity of \(\widehat Y^{(f)}\).

No cross-sector statement is needed for this sectorwise construction.
However, if two sectors are to be compared in a common basis, one must eliminate independent sectorwise whitening ambiguities, which is precisely the role of \(K2_{\mathrm{align}}\).
\end{proof}

\section{2. Exact finite criterion via the cubic discriminant}

Let the characteristic polynomial of \(\widehat Y^{(f)}\) be
\begin{equation}
\chi_f(\lambda)=\det(\lambda I-\widehat Y^{(f)})
=
\lambda^3-c_1^{(f)}\lambda^2+c_2^{(f)}\lambda-c_3^{(f)},
\label{eq:K3A_charpoly}
\end{equation}
with invariants
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_1^{(f)}=\operatorname{tr}\widehat Y^{(f)},
}
\label{eq:K3A_c1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_2^{(f)}=
\frac12\Bigl((\operatorname{tr}\widehat Y^{(f)})^2-\operatorname{tr}((\widehat Y^{(f)})^2)\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:K3A_c2}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_3^{(f)}=\det \widehat Y^{(f)}.
}
\label{eq:K3A_c3}
\end{equation}

The cubic discriminant is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_f
=
18c_1^{(f)}c_2^{(f)}c_3^{(f)}
-4(c_1^{(f)})^3 c_3^{(f)}
+(c_1^{(f)})^2(c_2^{(f)})^2
-4(c_2^{(f)})^3
-27(c_3^{(f)})^2.
}
\label{eq:K3A_discriminant}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Exact \(K3A\) criterion]
Let \(\widehat Y^{(f)}\) be Hermitian \(3\times3\), with eigenvalues
\[
m_1^{(f)},\ m_2^{(f)},\ m_3^{(f)}\in\mathbb R.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_f
=
\prod_{1\le i<j\le 3}(m_i^{(f)}-m_j^{(f)})^2.
}
\label{eq:K3A_disc_factor}
\end{equation}
Hence the following are equivalent:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\widehat Y^{(f)}\) has simple spectrum;
\item \(m_i^{(f)}\neq m_j^{(f)}\) for all \(i\neq j\);
\item
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_f>0.
}
\label{eq:K3A_exact_accept}
\end{equation}
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}


For any cubic polynomial
\[
\chi_f(\lambda)=\prod_{i=1}^3(\lambda-m_i^{(f)}),
\]
its discriminant equals
\[
\prod_{i<j}(m_i^{(f)}-m_j^{(f)})^2.
\]
Since \(\widehat Y^{(f)}\) is Hermitian, all eigenvalues are real, so \(\Delta_f\ge 0\).
Moreover, \(\Delta_f=0\) iff at least two eigenvalues coincide, while \(\Delta_f>0\) iff all three are distinct.


\paragraph{Meaning.}
This is the exact finite acceptance criterion for \(K3A\).
No further infinite-dimensional reduction is needed.

\section{3. Practical sufficient criterion from a reference splitting matrix}

For actual intended-branch work, the discriminant test is exact but not always the most transparent.
A more useful sufficient criterion comes from splitting \(\widehat Y^{(f)}\) into a reference diagonal part plus a controlled remainder.

Assume
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat Y^{(f)} = D_f + E_f,
}
\label{eq:K3A_DplusE}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
D_f=\operatorname{diag}(d^{(f)}_1,d^{(f)}_2,d^{(f)}_3),
\qquad
d^{(f)}_1<d^{(f)}_2<d^{(f)}_3.
\label{eq:K3A_Df}
\end{equation}
Define the reference gap
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_f:=\min\bigl(d^{(f)}_2-d^{(f)}_1,\ d^{(f)}_3-d^{(f)}_2\bigr)>0.
}
\label{eq:K3A_gap}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Gap-stability criterion for simple spectrum]
If
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2\|E_f\|<g_f,
}
\label{eq:K3A_gap_condition}
\end{equation}
then \(\widehat Y^{(f)}\) has simple spectrum.
\end{theorem}


Let \(\lambda_i^{(f)}\) be the ordered eigenvalues of \(\widehat Y^{(f)}\).
By Weyl's inequality,
\[
|\lambda_i^{(f)}-d_i^{(f)}|\le \|E_f\|
\qquad
(i=1,2,3).
\]
Thus
\[
\lambda_i^{(f)}\in [d_i^{(f)}-\|E_f\|,\ d_i^{(f)}+\|E_f\|].
\]
If \(2\|E_f\|<g_f\), then the three intervals are pairwise disjoint, because the minimum distance between adjacent \(d_i^{(f)}\) is \(g_f\).
Hence each interval contains exactly one eigenvalue, so all three eigenvalues are distinct.


\paragraph{Interpretation.}
A pre-existing reference splitting survives canonical normalization as long as the residual off-diagonal or sectoral correction is too small to close the reference gaps.

\section{4. Basis-invariant sufficient criterion from a simple reference operator}

The previous theorem used a diagonal reference basis.
A more invariant statement is the following.

\begin{theorem}[Simple-spectrum stability around a Hermitian reference]
Suppose
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat Y^{(f)}=\widehat Y^{(f)}_{\mathrm{ref}}+\delta \widehat Y^{(f)},
}
\label{eq:K3A_ref_split}
\end{equation}
where \(\widehat Y^{(f)}_{\mathrm{ref}}\) is Hermitian with simple eigenvalues
\[
\mu^{(f)}_1<\mu^{(f)}_2<\mu^{(f)}_3.
\]
Define the minimum reference spectral gap
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\gamma_f:=\min(\mu^{(f)}_2-\mu^{(f)}_1,\ \mu^{(f)}_3-\mu^{(f)}_2).
}
\label{eq:K3A_gamma}
\end{equation}
If
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2\|\delta \widehat Y^{(f)}\|<\gamma_f,
}
\label{eq:K3A_ref_gap_condition}
\end{equation}
then \(\widehat Y^{(f)}\) has simple spectrum.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Diagonalize \(\widehat Y^{(f)}_{\mathrm{ref}}\) by a unitary transformation.
The operator norm is unitary invariant, so the previous theorem applies in the diagonal basis.
\end{proof}

This is the form most naturally used in actual TECT work.

\section{5. Direct relation to the \(K2\) output}

Since
\[
\widehat Y^{(f)}=Z^{(f)-1/2}Y^{(f)}Z^{(f)-1/2},
\]
the \(K3A\) problem is already finite once \(K2\) is accepted.
Equivalently, if the projected pre-normalized family operator is computed in the localized generators as
\[
N^{(f)}_{ab}:=\langle \widetilde\psi_a,\mathcal Y_f\widetilde\psi_b\rangle,
\]
then in the orthonormal family basis,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat Y^{(f)} = S^{-1/2}\,N^{(f)}\,S^{-1/2}
}
\label{eq:K3A_bridge_N}
\end{equation}
provided the same \(S\) is used for the orthonormal family basis and \(K2\) has already supplied the canonical kinetic metric.

Thus the exact \(K3A\) microscopic input is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak I_{K3A}^{\mathrm{exact}}
=
\bigl(Z^{(f)},\,Y^{(f)}\bigr)
\quad\text{or equivalently}\quad
\bigl(S,\,N^{(f)}\bigr)
}
\label{eq:K3A_exact_input}
\end{equation}
for each sector \(f\).

\section{6. Practical \(K3A\) theorem}

We may now state the integrated practical theorem.

\begin{theorem}[Integrated practical \(K3A\) theorem]
Fix one sector \(f\).
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(K2_{\min}\) has been accepted for sector \(f\), so \(Z^{(f)}>0\);
\item \(Y^{(f)}\) is Hermitian on the family space;
\item \(\widehat Y^{(f)}=Z^{(f)-1/2}Y^{(f)}Z^{(f)-1/2}\) is therefore Hermitian;
\item either the exact discriminant \(\Delta_f\) can be computed, or a reference splitting decomposition \eqref{eq:K3A_ref_split} is available.
\end{enumerate}

Then:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(K3A\) is exactly accepted iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_f>0.
}
\label{eq:K3A_exact_final}
\end{equation}

\item A practical sufficient acceptance condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2\|\delta \widehat Y^{(f)}\|<\gamma_f,
}
\label{eq:K3A_sufficient_final}
\end{equation}
where \(\gamma_f\) is the minimum gap of a chosen simple-spectrum Hermitian reference operator \(\widehat Y^{(f)}_{\mathrm{ref}}\).
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from the exact discriminant criterion and the simple-spectrum stability theorem.
\end{proof}

\section{7. \(K3A\) Acceptance Sheet}

The exact acceptance audit is now finite.

\paragraph{Level 0: Canonical admissibility.}
Verify \(K2_{\min}\):
\[
Z^{(f)}>0.
\]

\paragraph{Level 1: Build the normalized family operator.}
Compute
\[
\widehat Y^{(f)}=Z^{(f)-1/2}Y^{(f)}Z^{(f)-1/2}.
\]

\paragraph{Level 2: Exact nondegeneracy test.}
Compute
\[
c_1^{(f)}=\operatorname{tr}\widehat Y^{(f)},
\qquad
c_2^{(f)}=\frac12\Bigl((\operatorname{tr}\widehat Y^{(f)})^2-\operatorname{tr}((\widehat Y^{(f)})^2)\Bigr),
\qquad
c_3^{(f)}=\det\widehat Y^{(f)},
\]
then the discriminant
\[
\Delta_f
=
18c_1^{(f)}c_2^{(f)}c_3^{(f)}
-4(c_1^{(f)})^3 c_3^{(f)}
+(c_1^{(f)})^2(c_2^{(f)})^2
-4(c_2^{(f)})^3
-27(c_3^{(f)})^2.
\]
Accept exact \(K3A\) iff
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_f>0.
}
\]

\paragraph{Level 3: Practical sufficient test.}
Choose a simple-spectrum Hermitian reference operator
\[
\widehat Y^{(f)}_{\mathrm{ref}},
\]
compute its minimum gap \(\gamma_f\), and define
\[
\delta \widehat Y^{(f)}:=\widehat Y^{(f)}-\widehat Y^{(f)}_{\mathrm{ref}}.
\]
Then a sufficient acceptance condition is
\[
\boxed{
2\|\delta \widehat Y^{(f)}\|<\gamma_f.
}
\]

\paragraph{Level 4: Program-level interpretation.}
If the above passes for one sector, then that sector has genuine nondegenerate family splitting.
If it passes for both up and down sectors, then \(K3A\) is accepted sectorwise.
If, in addition, \(K2_{\mathrm{align}}\) holds, then the two sectors can be compared in one common family basis without kinetic-basis ambiguity.

\section{Honest Status}

The structural status of \(K3A\) is now the same type as late \(K2\):

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K3A\text{ is structurally reduced to a finite spectral audit.}
}
\end{equation}

What remains open is not conceptual reduction, but actual intended-branch insertion of the canonically normalized sectoral family operators.

Thus the honest status is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Structural status of }K3A:\ \text{closed at finite-audit level.}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Microscopic acceptance status of }K3A:\ \text{conditional until }\widehat Y^{(f)}\text{ is explicitly audited.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

After \(K2\), the \(K3A\) problem is no longer an infinite-dimensional PDE problem.
It is the finite spectral problem of the Hermitian \(3\times3\) operator
\[
\widehat Y^{(f)}=Z^{(f)-1/2}Y^{(f)}Z^{(f)-1/2}.
\]

The exact criterion for nondegenerate three-family splitting is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_f>0,
}
\]
where \(\Delta_f\) is the cubic discriminant of the characteristic polynomial of \(\widehat Y^{(f)}\).

A practical sufficient criterion is obtained from a reference simple-spectrum Hermitian operator:
if
\[
2\|\delta \widehat Y^{(f)}\|<\gamma_f,
\]
where \(\gamma_f\) is the minimum reference gap, then the spectrum remains simple.

Therefore \(K3A\) is fully reduced to a finite spectral acceptance sheet.
The remaining work is the intended-branch computation of the normalized family operators and the evaluation of the discriminant or gap inequalities.

\section*{K3A Final Summary}

Given \(K2_{\min}\), each sector admits the canonically normalized Hermitian family operator
\[
\widehat Y^{(f)}=Z^{(f)-1/2}Y^{(f)}Z^{(f)-1/2}.
\]

The exact \(K3A\) acceptance criterion is that the cubic discriminant of \(\widehat Y^{(f)}\) be strictly positive:
\[
\Delta_f>0.
\]
Equivalently, the three eigenvalues of \(\widehat Y^{(f)}\) are pairwise distinct.

A practical sufficient criterion is obtained from a simple-spectrum Hermitian reference operator
\[
\widehat Y^{(f)}_{\mathrm{ref}},
\]
with minimum gap \(\gamma_f\):
if
\[
2\|\widehat Y^{(f)}-\widehat Y^{(f)}_{\mathrm{ref}}\|<\gamma_f,
\]
then \(\widehat Y^{(f)}\) has simple spectrum.

Therefore the \(K3A\) problem is structurally closed:
it is a finite spectral audit of a Hermitian \(3\times3\) matrix.
What remains is the explicit intended-branch evaluation of \(\widehat Y^{(f)}\).

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{K3B: Literal Blockwise Splitting Seeds in the Canonically Normalized Family Operator}

\section{Goal}

After \(K2\), each sector \(f\) is described by the canonically normalized Hermitian family operator
\[
\widehat Y^{(f)}=Z^{(f)-1/2}Y^{(f)}Z^{(f)-1/2}.
\]

At \(K3A\), the exact question was whether \(\widehat Y^{(f)}\) has simple spectrum.
The purpose of \(K3B\) is more refined:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{which matrix entries actually seed the splitting?}
}
\end{equation}

We now show that the splitting problem is controlled entirely by the traceless part of \(\widehat Y^{(f)}\), and that its blockwise seed structure can be made completely explicit.

\section{1. Scalar part versus genuine splitting part}

For one fixed sector \(f\), define the scalar center
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c^{(f)}:=\frac13\operatorname{tr}\widehat Y^{(f)}.
}
\label{eq:K3B_lambdac}
\end{equation}
Then write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat Y^{(f)}=\lambda_c^{(f)}\mathbf 1_3 + Q^{(f)},
\qquad
\operatorname{tr}Q^{(f)}=0.
}
\label{eq:K3B_scalar_split}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Scalar irrelevance theorem]
The spectrum of \(\widehat Y^{(f)}\) is simple if and only if the spectrum of \(Q^{(f)}\) is simple.
Equivalently, the scalar part \(\lambda_c^{(f)}\mathbf 1_3\) never creates or removes degeneracy.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
If \(\mu_1,\mu_2,\mu_3\) are the eigenvalues of \(Q^{(f)}\), then the eigenvalues of \(\widehat Y^{(f)}\) are
\[
m_i^{(f)}=\lambda_c^{(f)}+\mu_i.
\]
Hence
\[
m_i^{(f)}-m_j^{(f)}=\mu_i-\mu_j.
\]
Therefore multiplicities are unchanged by adding a scalar multiple of the identity.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Meaning.}
The literal coefficient
\[
\mathcal H_{OO}\to \lambda_c
\]
controls the sectoral center of mass of the spectrum, but not the splitting itself.

\section{2. Blockwise seed decomposition}

The splitting-relevant traceless matrix \(Q^{(f)}\) is now decomposed into blockwise contributions.

Choose a unitary family basis in which the traceless part of the \(OO\)-sector contribution is diagonal.
Then write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q^{(f)} = D^{(f)} + X^{(f)} + R^{(f)},
}
\label{eq:K3B_QDXR}
\end{equation}
where:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(D^{(f)}\) is the traceless diagonal \(OO\)-anisotropy seed,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D^{(f)}=\operatorname{diag}(d_1^{(f)},d_2^{(f)},d_3^{(f)}),
\qquad
d_1^{(f)}+d_2^{(f)}+d_3^{(f)}=0;
}
\label{eq:K3B_D}
\end{equation}

\item \(X^{(f)}\) is the Hermitian mixed-coupling seed extracted from the \(TD/DT\) blocks,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
X^{(f)}=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & \Lambda_{12}^{(f)} & \Lambda_{13}^{(f)}\\
\overline{\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}} & 0 & \Lambda_{23}^{(f)}\\
\overline{\Lambda_{13}^{(f)}} & \overline{\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}} & 0
\end{pmatrix};
}
\label{eq:K3B_X}
\end{equation}

\item \(R^{(f)}\) is any remaining Hermitian traceless remainder not absorbed into the literal \(OO,TD,DT\) seed extraction.
\end{enumerate}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat Y^{(f)}
=
\lambda_c^{(f)}\mathbf 1_3
+
D^{(f)}
+
X^{(f)}
+
R^{(f)}.
}
\label{eq:K3B_full_seed_split}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
This realizes the literal blockwise philosophy:

\[
\mathcal H_{OO}\to \lambda_c^{(f)} \text{ and } D^{(f)},
\qquad
\mathcal H_{TD},\mathcal H_{DT}\to \Lambda_{12}^{(f)},\Lambda_{13}^{(f)},\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}.
\]

The scalar \(OO\) piece gives \(\lambda_c^{(f)}\), the traceless diagonal \(OO\) piece gives \(D^{(f)}\), and the mixed blocks give the off-diagonal couplings.

\section{3. Exact invariant form of the splitting problem}

Ignore the remainder for the moment and define the literal seed matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q^{(f)}_{\mathrm{seed}}:=D^{(f)}+X^{(f)}.
}
\label{eq:K3B_Qseed}
\end{equation}

Since \(Q^{(f)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\) is Hermitian and traceless, its characteristic polynomial is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\chi_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(f)}(\mu)
=
\det(\mu I-Q^{(f)}_{\mathrm{seed}})
=
\mu^3-p_f\,\mu-q_f,
}
\label{eq:K3B_char_traceless}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
p_f=\frac12\operatorname{tr}\bigl((Q^{(f)}_{\mathrm{seed}})^2\bigr),
\qquad
q_f=\det Q^{(f)}_{\mathrm{seed}}.
}
\label{eq:K3B_pq_def}
\end{equation}

Its discriminant is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_f^{\mathrm{seed}}
=
4p_f^3-27q_f^2.
}
\label{eq:K3B_seed_discriminant}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Exact seed criterion]
The literal seed matrix \(Q^{(f)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\) has simple spectrum if and only if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_f^{\mathrm{seed}}>0.
}
\label{eq:K3B_exact_seed_accept}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
For a depressed cubic
\[
\mu^3-p\mu-q,
\]
the discriminant is \(4p^3-27q^2\).
Because \(Q^{(f)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\) is Hermitian, all roots are real, and simple spectrum is equivalent to positivity of the discriminant.
\end{proof}

\section{4. Exact blockwise formulas for \(p_f\) and \(q_f\)}

The main advantage of the \(D+X\) form is that the invariants can be written explicitly.

\subsection{Quadratic invariant}

\begin{theorem}[Exact quadratic seed invariant]
For
\[
Q^{(f)}_{\mathrm{seed}}=D^{(f)}+X^{(f)},
\]
one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
p_f
=
\frac12\sum_{i=1}^3 (d_i^{(f)})^2
+
\sum_{1\le i<j\le 3}\bigl|\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}\bigr|^2.
}
\label{eq:K3B_p_formula}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Since \(D^{(f)}\) is diagonal and \(X^{(f)}\) has zero diagonal,
\[
\operatorname{tr}(D^{(f)}X^{(f)})=0.
\]
Hence
\[
\operatorname{tr}\bigl((D^{(f)}+X^{(f)})^2\bigr)
=
\operatorname{tr}\bigl((D^{(f)})^2\bigr)+\operatorname{tr}\bigl((X^{(f)})^2\bigr).
\]
Now
\[
\operatorname{tr}\bigl((D^{(f)})^2\bigr)=\sum_i (d_i^{(f)})^2,
\]
and for the Hermitian off-diagonal matrix \(X^{(f)}\),
\[
\operatorname{tr}\bigl((X^{(f)})^2\bigr)
=
2\sum_{i<j}|\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}|^2.
\]
Therefore
\[
p_f=\frac12\operatorname{tr}\bigl((Q^{(f)}_{\mathrm{seed}})^2\bigr)
=
\frac12\sum_i (d_i^{(f)})^2+\sum_{i<j}|\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}|^2.
\]
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Meaning.}
Every diagonal anisotropy \(d_i\) and every mixed coupling \(\Lambda_{ij}\) contributes positively to the quadratic splitting strength.
The scalar \(\lambda_c\) does not appear at all.

\subsection{Cubic invariant}

\begin{theorem}[Exact cubic seed invariant]
For
\[
Q^{(f)}_{\mathrm{seed}}=D^{(f)}+X^{(f)},
\]
one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
q_f
=
d_1^{(f)}d_2^{(f)}d_3^{(f)}
-d_1^{(f)}|\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}|^2
-d_2^{(f)}|\Lambda_{13}^{(f)}|^2
-d_3^{(f)}|\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}|^2
+2\,\Re\!\Bigl(\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}\overline{\Lambda_{13}^{(f)}}\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:K3B_q_formula}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Expand the determinant of
\[
\begin{pmatrix}
d_1^{(f)} & \Lambda_{12}^{(f)} & \Lambda_{13}^{(f)}\\
\overline{\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}} & d_2^{(f)} & \Lambda_{23}^{(f)}\\
\overline{\Lambda_{13}^{(f)}} & \overline{\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}} & d_3^{(f)}
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
A direct cofactor expansion gives
\[
q_f
=
d_1^{(f)}d_2^{(f)}d_3^{(f)}
-d_1^{(f)}|\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}|^2
-d_2^{(f)}|\Lambda_{13}^{(f)}|^2
-d_3^{(f)}|\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}|^2
+\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}\overline{\Lambda_{13}^{(f)}}
+\overline{\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}\overline{\Lambda_{13}^{(f)}}},
\]
which is precisely \eqref{eq:K3B_q_formula}.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Meaning.}
The remote \(1\text{--}3\) coupling \(\Lambda_{13}^{(f)}\) enters:

\begin{enumerate}
\item quadratically in \(p_f\) through \(|\Lambda_{13}^{(f)}|^2\),
\item quadratically in \(q_f\) through \(-d_2^{(f)}|\Lambda_{13}^{(f)}|^2\),
\item cubically through the interference term
\[
2\,\Re\!\bigl(\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}\overline{\Lambda_{13}^{(f)}}\bigr).
\]
\end{enumerate}

This is exactly why the remote \(1\text{--}3\) channel is often numerically delicate:
it is subleading in crude models, but it can decisively control fine splitting structure and later phase-sensitive observables.

\section{5. Rephasing structure and what is already physical at \(K3B\)}

Under a diagonal family rephasing
\[
e_i\mapsto e^{i\alpha_i}e_i,
\]
the couplings transform as
\[
\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}\mapsto e^{i(\alpha_j-\alpha_i)}\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}.
\]
Hence the individual phases of \(\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}\) are basis-dependent.
However:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}|
\text{ is invariant,}
\qquad
\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}\overline{\Lambda_{13}^{(f)}}
\text{ is also invariant.}
}
\label{eq:K3B_rephasing_invariants}
\end{equation}

Therefore the exact \(K3B\) splitting data are already controlled by rephasing-invariant quantities.
This is consistent with the fact that \(K3B\) is about spectral splitting, not yet about irreducible CP violation.
The latter is deferred to \(K5\).

\section{6. Special exact seed cases}

The explicit formulas immediately give several sharp lemmas.

\subsection{Pure scalar case}

\begin{theorem}[No splitting from a pure scalar]
If
\[
D^{(f)}=0,
\qquad
X^{(f)}=0,
\]
then
\[
\widehat Y^{(f)}=\lambda_c^{(f)}\mathbf 1_3
\]
has triple degeneracy.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Immediate.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Pure diagonal seed}

\begin{theorem}[Diagonal \(OO\)-anisotropy seed]
If
\[
X^{(f)}=0,
\qquad
R^{(f)}=0,
\]
then the eigenvalues are
\[
\lambda_c^{(f)}+d_1^{(f)},
\qquad
\lambda_c^{(f)}+d_2^{(f)},
\qquad
\lambda_c^{(f)}+d_3^{(f)}.
\]
Hence the spectrum is simple iff
\[
d_i^{(f)}\neq d_j^{(f)}
\qquad
(i\neq j).
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Immediate, since \(D^{(f)}\) is diagonal.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Single-link mixed seed}

\begin{theorem}[One nonzero mixed link already splits]
Assume
\[
D^{(f)}=0,
\qquad
R^{(f)}=0,
\]
and exactly one mixed coupling is nonzero, e.g.
\[
\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}\neq 0,
\qquad
\Lambda_{13}^{(f)}=\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}=0.
\]
Then the eigenvalues are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c^{(f)}-|\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}|,
\qquad
\lambda_c^{(f)},
\qquad
\lambda_c^{(f)}+|\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}|.
}
\label{eq:K3B_single_link_spectrum}
\end{equation}
In particular, the spectrum is simple whenever \(\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}\neq 0\).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
In this case
\[
X^{(f)}=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & \Lambda_{12}^{(f)} & 0\\
\overline{\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}} & 0 & 0\\
0 & 0 & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\]
whose spectrum is \(\{-|\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}|,0,+|\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}|\}\).
Adding \(\lambda_c^{(f)}I\) shifts all eigenvalues by \(\lambda_c^{(f)}\).
\end{proof}

\subsection{Nearest-neighbor chain seed}

\begin{theorem}[Two-link chain seed]
Assume
\[
D^{(f)}=0,
\qquad
R^{(f)}=0,
\qquad
\Lambda_{13}^{(f)}=0,
\]
but
\[
(\Lambda_{12}^{(f)},\Lambda_{23}^{(f)})\neq (0,0).
\]
Then the eigenvalues are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c^{(f)},
\qquad
\lambda_c^{(f)}\pm \sqrt{|\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}|^2+|\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}|^2}.
}
\label{eq:K3B_chain_spectrum}
\end{equation}
Hence the spectrum is simple whenever at least one of the two links is nonzero.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
For
\[
X^{(f)}=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & \Lambda_{12}^{(f)} & 0\\
\overline{\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}} & 0 & \Lambda_{23}^{(f)}\\
0 & \overline{\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}} & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\]
one computes
\[
\det(\mu I-X^{(f)})
=
\mu\Bigl(\mu^2-(|\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}|^2+|\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}|^2)\Bigr).
\]
So the spectrum of \(X^{(f)}\) is
\[
0,\ \pm \sqrt{|\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}|^2+|\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}|^2}.
\]
Shifting by \(\lambda_c^{(f)}\) gives \eqref{eq:K3B_chain_spectrum}.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Meaning.}
Even without diagonal anisotropy, the \(TD/DT\) mixed blocks alone can already generate a nondegenerate three-family split.

\section{7. Remainder stability theorem}

The literal seed matrix \(D^{(f)}+X^{(f)}\) may not be the whole story.
So we now include the remainder \(R^{(f)}\).

Define the seed operator
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat Y^{(f)}_{\mathrm{seed}}
:=
\lambda_c^{(f)}\mathbf 1_3 + D^{(f)}+X^{(f)}.
}
\label{eq:K3B_Yseed}
\end{equation}
Let its ordered eigenvalues be
\[
\nu_1^{(f)}<\nu_2^{(f)}<\nu_3^{(f)},
\]
and define its minimum gap
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(f)}
:=
\min\bigl(\nu_2^{(f)}-\nu_1^{(f)},\ \nu_3^{(f)}-\nu_2^{(f)}\bigr).
}
\label{eq:K3B_gseed}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Seed stability criterion]
If \(\widehat Y^{(f)}_{\mathrm{seed}}\) has simple spectrum and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
2\|R^{(f)}\|<g_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(f)},
}
\label{eq:K3B_remainder_gap}
\end{equation}
then the full operator
\[
\widehat Y^{(f)}=\widehat Y^{(f)}_{\mathrm{seed}}+R^{(f)}
\]
also has simple spectrum.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Apply Weyl's eigenvalue perturbation theorem exactly as in \(K3A\).
Each eigenvalue moves by at most \(\|R^{(f)}\|\).
If
\[
2\|R^{(f)}\|<g_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(f)},
\]
the seed spectral intervals remain disjoint, so no degeneracy can occur.
\end{proof}

This theorem is the literal blockwise refinement of the general \(K3A\) gap-stability condition.

\section{8. Integrated practical \(K3B\) theorem}

We may now state the full practical theorem.

\begin{theorem}[Integrated practical \(K3B\) theorem]
Fix one sector \(f\).
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(K2_{\min}\) has been accepted, so \(\widehat Y^{(f)}\) is well-defined and Hermitian;
\item a blockwise decomposition
\[
\widehat Y^{(f)}
=
\lambda_c^{(f)}\mathbf 1_3
+
D^{(f)}
+
X^{(f)}
+
R^{(f)}
\]
has been extracted, with \(D^{(f)}\) diagonal traceless, \(X^{(f)}\) Hermitian off-diagonal, and \(R^{(f)}\) Hermitian traceless;
\item either the seed discriminant \(\Delta_f^{\mathrm{seed}}\) or the seed gap \(g_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(f)}\) is computed.
\end{enumerate}

Then:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the exact splitting seed is \(Q^{(f)}_{\mathrm{seed}}=D^{(f)}+X^{(f)}\);
\item the exact seed nondegeneracy criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_f^{\mathrm{seed}}=4p_f^3-27q_f^2>0,
}
\label{eq:K3B_seed_accept_final}
\end{equation}
with \(p_f,q_f\) given explicitly by \eqref{eq:K3B_p_formula} and \eqref{eq:K3B_q_formula};
\item a practical sufficient condition for the full operator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_f^{\mathrm{seed}}>0
\quad\text{and}\quad
2\|R^{(f)}\|<g_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(f)}.
}
\label{eq:K3B_full_accept_final}
\end{equation}
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The first statement is just the scalar irrelevance theorem.
The second is the exact discriminant criterion for the traceless Hermitian seed matrix.
The third follows from the seed stability theorem.
\end{proof}

\section{9. \(K3B\) Acceptance Sheet}

The \(K3B\) audit is now completely finite and literal.

\paragraph{Level 0: Canonical admissibility.}
Verify \(K2_{\min}\) so that \(\widehat Y^{(f)}\) is defined.

\paragraph{Level 1: Literal block extraction.}
Extract:
\[
\lambda_c^{(f)}=\frac13\operatorname{tr}\widehat Y^{(f)},
\]
\[
D^{(f)}=\operatorname{diag}(d_1^{(f)},d_2^{(f)},d_3^{(f)}),
\qquad
d_1^{(f)}+d_2^{(f)}+d_3^{(f)}=0,
\]
\[
X^{(f)}=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & \Lambda_{12}^{(f)} & \Lambda_{13}^{(f)}\\
\overline{\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}} & 0 & \Lambda_{23}^{(f)}\\
\overline{\Lambda_{13}^{(f)}} & \overline{\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}} & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\]
and the remainder \(R^{(f)}\).

\paragraph{Level 2: Exact seed audit.}
Compute
\[
p_f
=
\frac12\sum_i (d_i^{(f)})^2
+
\sum_{i<j}|\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}|^2,
\]
\[
q_f
=
d_1^{(f)}d_2^{(f)}d_3^{(f)}
-d_1^{(f)}|\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}|^2
-d_2^{(f)}|\Lambda_{13}^{(f)}|^2
-d_3^{(f)}|\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}|^2
+2\Re\!\Bigl(\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}\overline{\Lambda_{13}^{(f)}}\Bigr),
\]
and then
\[
\Delta_f^{\mathrm{seed}}=4p_f^3-27q_f^2.
\]
Accept exact seed splitting iff
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_f^{\mathrm{seed}}>0.
}
\]

\paragraph{Level 3: Full practical audit.}
Compute the seed gap \(g_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(f)}\).
Then accept practical full \(K3B\) iff
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_f^{\mathrm{seed}}>0
\quad\text{and}\quad
2\|R^{(f)}\|<g_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(f)}.
}
\]

\paragraph{Level 4: Physical interpretation.}
\begin{itemize}
\item \(\lambda_c^{(f)}\) shifts the whole spectrum but does not split it.
\item \(d_i^{(f)}\) measure traceless \(OO\)-anisotropy splitting.
\item \(\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}\) are the literal mixed \(TD/DT\) splitting seeds.
\item The remote \(1\text{--}3\) channel \(\Lambda_{13}^{(f)}\) is especially important for fine hierarchy control.
\end{itemize}

\section{Honest Status}

The structural status of \(K3B\) is now closed:
the question
\[
\text{“which entries actually seed the splitting?”}
\]
has been reduced to a fully explicit finite invariant audit.

What remains open is only the actual intended-branch insertion of the blockwise extracted numbers
\[
\lambda_c^{(f)},\quad d_i^{(f)},\quad \Lambda_{ij}^{(f)},\quad \|R^{(f)}\|.
\]

So the honest status is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Structural status of }K3B:\ \text{closed at literal finite block-audit level.}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Microscopic acceptance status of }K3B:\ \text{conditional until the extracted seed data are inserted.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The canonically normalized family operator admits the literal blockwise decomposition
\[
\widehat Y^{(f)}
=
\lambda_c^{(f)}\mathbf 1_3
+
D^{(f)}
+
X^{(f)}
+
R^{(f)}.
\]

Here \(\lambda_c^{(f)}\) is spectrally irrelevant for splitting,
\(D^{(f)}\) is the traceless diagonal \(OO\)-anisotropy seed,
and \(X^{(f)}\) contains the mixed \(TD/DT\) couplings
\(\Lambda_{12}^{(f)},\Lambda_{13}^{(f)},\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}\).

The exact seed splitting problem is controlled by the traceless Hermitian matrix
\[
Q^{(f)}_{\mathrm{seed}}=D^{(f)}+X^{(f)},
\]
whose characteristic polynomial is
\[
\mu^3-p_f\mu-q_f,
\]
with
\[
p_f
=
\frac12\sum_i (d_i^{(f)})^2
+
\sum_{i<j}|\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}|^2,
\]
and
\[
q_f
=
d_1^{(f)}d_2^{(f)}d_3^{(f)}
-d_1^{(f)}|\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}|^2
-d_2^{(f)}|\Lambda_{13}^{(f)}|^2
-d_3^{(f)}|\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}|^2
+2\Re\!\Bigl(\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}\overline{\Lambda_{13}^{(f)}}\Bigr).
\]

Therefore the exact seed nondegeneracy criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_f^{\mathrm{seed}}=4p_f^3-27q_f^2>0.
}
\]

A practical full sufficient criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_f^{\mathrm{seed}}>0
\quad\text{and}\quad
2\|R^{(f)}\|<g_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(f)}.
}
\]

Hence \(K3B\) is fully reduced to a literal finite blockwise seed audit.

\section*{K3B Final Summary}

For one fixed sector, the canonically normalized family operator can be written as
\[
\widehat Y^{(f)}
=
\lambda_c^{(f)}\mathbf 1_3
+
D^{(f)}
+
X^{(f)}
+
R^{(f)},
\]
where
\[
D^{(f)}=\operatorname{diag}(d_1^{(f)},d_2^{(f)},d_3^{(f)}),
\qquad
d_1^{(f)}+d_2^{(f)}+d_3^{(f)}=0,
\]
and
\[
X^{(f)}=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & \Lambda_{12}^{(f)} & \Lambda_{13}^{(f)}\\
\overline{\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}} & 0 & \Lambda_{23}^{(f)}\\
\overline{\Lambda_{13}^{(f)}} & \overline{\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}} & 0
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

The scalar part \(\lambda_c^{(f)}\mathbf 1_3\) does not affect degeneracy.
The exact splitting seed is the traceless Hermitian matrix
\[
Q^{(f)}_{\mathrm{seed}}=D^{(f)}+X^{(f)}.
\]

Its characteristic polynomial is
\[
\mu^3-p_f\mu-q_f,
\]
with
\[
p_f
=
\frac12\sum_i (d_i^{(f)})^2
+
\sum_{i<j}|\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}|^2,
\]
and
\[
q_f
=
d_1^{(f)}d_2^{(f)}d_3^{(f)}
-d_1^{(f)}|\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}|^2
-d_2^{(f)}|\Lambda_{13}^{(f)}|^2
-d_3^{(f)}|\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}|^2
+2\Re\!\Bigl(\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}\overline{\Lambda_{13}^{(f)}}\Bigr).
\]

Therefore the exact seed nondegeneracy criterion is
\[
\Delta_f^{\mathrm{seed}}
=
4p_f^3-27q_f^2>0.
\]

If the remainder \(R^{(f)}\) is present, a practical sufficient condition for the full operator is
\[
\Delta_f^{\mathrm{seed}}>0
\quad\text{and}\quad
2\|R^{(f)}\|<g_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(f)},
\]
where \(g_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(f)}\) is the minimum gap of the seed operator
\[
\lambda_c^{(f)}\mathbf 1_3+D^{(f)}+X^{(f)}.
\]

Hence \(K3B\) is fully reduced to a literal finite blockwise seed audit.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{K3C: Sectorwise Hierarchy Seed for the Family Diagonalizer}

\section{Goal}

At \(K3B\), we identified the exact splitting seed
\[
Q^{(f)}_{\mathrm{seed}}=D^{(f)}+X^{(f)}
\]
inside the canonically normalized Hermitian family operator
\[
\widehat Y^{(f)}
=
\lambda_c^{(f)}\mathbf 1_3
+
D^{(f)}
+
X^{(f)}
+
R^{(f)}.
\]

The next question is not merely whether the spectrum is simple, but whether the corresponding diagonalizer already carries a \emph{hierarchical mixing seed}.

The key point is that this is still a \emph{sectorwise} statement.
It does \emph{not} yet equal the CKM hierarchy, because the physical CKM matrix is
\[
V_{\mathrm{CKM}}=U_u^\dagger U_d.
\]
Hence \(K3C\) concerns the hierarchy seed in each sectoral diagonalizer \(U_f\), while the actual inter-sector hierarchy is deferred to \(K4\).

\section{1. Canonical diagonalization setup}

For one fixed sector \(f\), absorb all traceless diagonal contributions into a single ordered diagonal matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D_f=\operatorname{diag}(d_1^{(f)},d_2^{(f)},d_3^{(f)}),
\qquad
d_1^{(f)}<d_2^{(f)}<d_3^{(f)}.
}
\label{eq:K3C_Df}
\end{equation}
Define the ordered gaps
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{12}^{(f)}:=d_2^{(f)}-d_1^{(f)},
\qquad
\Delta_{23}^{(f)}:=d_3^{(f)}-d_2^{(f)},
\qquad
\Delta_{13}^{(f)}:=d_3^{(f)}-d_1^{(f)}.
}
\label{eq:K3C_gaps}
\end{equation}

Let the off-diagonal Hermitian part be
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_f:=X^{(f)}+\operatorname{Off}R^{(f)}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & w_{12}^{(f)} & w_{13}^{(f)}\\
\overline{w_{12}^{(f)}} & 0 & w_{23}^{(f)}\\
\overline{w_{13}^{(f)}} & \overline{w_{23}^{(f)}} & 0
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:K3C_Wf}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat Y^{(f)}
=
\lambda_c^{(f)}\mathbf 1_3
+
D_f
+
W_f.
}
\label{eq:K3C_Yhat_DW}
\end{equation}

The scalar part \(\lambda_c^{(f)}\mathbf 1_3\) is irrelevant for the diagonalizer.
Thus the hierarchy seed problem is entirely controlled by the pair \((D_f,W_f)\).

\section{2. Small-mixing parameter and perturbative diagonalizer}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_f:=\min(\Delta_{12}^{(f)},\Delta_{23}^{(f)}),
\qquad
\eta_f:=\frac{\|W_f\|}{g_f}.
}
\label{eq:K3C_etaf}
\end{equation}

In the diagonal-dominant regime \(\eta_f\ll 1\), there exists a unitary diagonalizer
\[
U_f=e^{\Omega_f},
\qquad
\Omega_f^\dagger=-\Omega_f,
\]
such that
\[
U_f^\dagger \widehat Y^{(f)} U_f
\]
is diagonal.

\begin{theorem}[First-order hierarchy seed formula]
Assume \(2\|W_f\|<g_f\).
Then the sectoral diagonalizer may be chosen so that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Omega_f)_{ij}
=
\frac{w_{ij}^{(f)}}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}}
+
O(\eta_f^2),
\qquad
1\le i<j\le 3.
}
\label{eq:K3C_Omega_first}
\end{equation}
Consequently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|U_{ij}^{(f)}|
=
\frac{|w_{ij}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}}
+
O(\eta_f^2)
\qquad
(i<j),
}
\label{eq:K3C_Uij_first}
\end{equation}
where the \(O(\eta_f^2)\) term is uniform on a sufficiently small perturbative norm ball.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Choose \(\Omega_f^{(1)}\) solving the first-order homological equation
\[
[D_f,\Omega_f^{(1)}]+W_f=0.
\]
Since
\[
([D_f,\Omega_f^{(1)}])_{ij}
=
(d_i^{(f)}-d_j^{(f)})(\Omega_f^{(1)})_{ij},
\]
the unique off-diagonal solution is
\[
(\Omega_f^{(1)})_{ij}
=
\frac{w_{ij}^{(f)}}{d_j^{(f)}-d_i^{(f)}}
=
\frac{w_{ij}^{(f)}}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}}.
\]
Standard Baker--Campbell--Hausdorff perturbative diagonalization then gives
\[
\Omega_f=\Omega_f^{(1)}+O(\eta_f^2),
\]
and \(U_f=e^{\Omega_f}=I+\Omega_f+O(\eta_f^2)\), which implies \eqref{eq:K3C_Uij_first}.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
The leading hierarchy seed is controlled by the ratio
\[
\frac{|w_{ij}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}}.
\]
So the diagonal anisotropy creates the denominators, while the mixed blocks create the numerators.

\section{3. Literal seed amplitudes}

Define the three primary hierarchy-seed amplitudes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_{12}^{(f)}:=\frac{|w_{12}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{12}^{(f)}},
\qquad
h_{23}^{(f)}:=\frac{|w_{23}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{23}^{(f)}},
\qquad
h_{13,\mathrm{dir}}^{(f)}:=\frac{|w_{13}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{13}^{(f)}}.
}
\label{eq:K3C_h_primary}
\end{equation}

These are the literal first-order seed sizes for the three pairwise mixings.

However, the remote \(1\text{--}3\) channel receives not only the direct term \(w_{13}^{(f)}\), but also an indirect chain contribution through \(1\leftrightarrow 2\leftrightarrow 3\).

\section{4. Effective remote \(1\text{--}3\) seed}

At second order, the \(1\text{--}3\) channel receives an indirect contribution controlled by the product of the two nearest-neighbor links.
A robust upper seed is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_{13,\mathrm{eff}}^{(f)}
:=
\frac{|w_{13}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{13}^{(f)}}
+
\frac{|w_{12}^{(f)}w_{23}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{13}^{(f)}}
\left(
\frac{1}{\Delta_{12}^{(f)}}+\frac{1}{\Delta_{23}^{(f)}}
\right).
}
\label{eq:K3C_h13eff}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Meaning.}
The first term is the direct remote coupling.
The second term is the chain-mediated \(1\to2\to3\) feed.
Therefore even when \(w_{13}^{(f)}\) is tiny, the remote channel may still be generated indirectly.

This is the sectorwise hierarchy analogue of the \(K3B\) observation that the \(13\)-channel is unusually delicate.

\section{5. Exact scope statement}

\begin{proposition}[What \(K3C\) does and does not prove]
The quantities
\[
h_{12}^{(f)},\qquad
h_{23}^{(f)},\qquad
h_{13,\mathrm{eff}}^{(f)}
\]
control the hierarchy seed of one sectoral diagonalizer \(U_f\).

They do \emph{not} by themselves prove the physical CKM ordering
\[
|V_{12}|>|V_{23}|>|V_{13}|.
\]
That physical statement belongs to \(K4\), because it depends on the relative misalignment of two sectoral diagonalizers:
\[
V_{\mathrm{CKM}}=U_u^\dagger U_d.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Immediate.
\end{proof}

\section{6. Practical hierarchy-seed theorem}

We now state the practical theorem relevant for \(K3C\).

\begin{theorem}[Practical sectorwise hierarchy-seed criterion]
Fix one sector \(f\), and assume the diagonal-dominant regime
\[
\eta_f=\frac{\|W_f\|}{g_f}\ll 1.
\]
Suppose there exists a positive margin \(m_f>0\) such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_{12}^{(f)}-h_{23}^{(f)} > m_f,
}
\label{eq:K3C_margin12}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_{23}^{(f)}-h_{13,\mathrm{eff}}^{(f)} > m_f.
}
\label{eq:K3C_margin23}
\end{equation}
If, moreover, the perturbative remainder satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_f \gg O(\eta_f^2),
}
\label{eq:K3C_margin_vs_remainder}
\end{equation}
then the sectoral diagonalizer obeys
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|U_{12}^{(f)}|>|U_{23}^{(f)}|>|U_{13}^{(f)}|.
}
\label{eq:K3C_sectoral_ordering}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By \eqref{eq:K3C_Uij_first},
\[
|U_{12}^{(f)}|=h_{12}^{(f)}+O(\eta_f^2),
\qquad
|U_{23}^{(f)}|=h_{23}^{(f)}+O(\eta_f^2),
\]
and
\[
|U_{13}^{(f)}|
\le
h_{13,\mathrm{eff}}^{(f)}+O(\eta_f^2).
\]
If the gaps \eqref{eq:K3C_margin12}--\eqref{eq:K3C_margin23} dominate the higher-order error, the stated ordering follows.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
The hierarchy seed is not arbitrary.
It comes from a clean finite comparison of three dimensionless quantities:
\[
\frac{|w_{12}|}{\Delta_{12}},
\qquad
\frac{|w_{23}|}{\Delta_{23}},
\qquad
\frac{|w_{13}|}{\Delta_{13}}
+
\frac{|w_{12}w_{23}|}{\Delta_{13}}
\left(
\frac{1}{\Delta_{12}}+\frac{1}{\Delta_{23}}
\right).
\]

\section{7. Literal blockwise meaning}

Recall from \(K3B\) that
\[
w_{ij}^{(f)}=\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}+r_{ij}^{(f)},
\]
where \(\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}\) is the literal \(TD/DT\) blockwise extraction and \(r_{ij}^{(f)}\) is the off-diagonal remainder.

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_{12}^{(f)}
=
\frac{|\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}+r_{12}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{12}^{(f)}},
\qquad
h_{23}^{(f)}
=
\frac{|\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}+r_{23}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{23}^{(f)}},
}
\label{eq:K3C_h12h23_literal}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_{13,\mathrm{eff}}^{(f)}
=
\frac{|\Lambda_{13}^{(f)}+r_{13}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{13}^{(f)}}
+
\frac{|\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}+r_{12}^{(f)}|\,|\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}+r_{23}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{13}^{(f)}}
\left(
\frac{1}{\Delta_{12}^{(f)}}+\frac{1}{\Delta_{23}^{(f)}}
\right).
}
\label{eq:K3C_h13_literal}
\end{equation}

Thus the hierarchy seed has a fully literal blockwise interpretation:

\begin{itemize}
\item \(OO\)-anisotropy produces the gap denominators \(\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}\);
\item \(TD/DT\) block extraction produces the leading numerators \(\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}\);
\item the remote \(13\)-channel is suppressed unless either
\begin{enumerate}
\item a direct \(\Lambda_{13}^{(f)}\) is present, or
\item the two-link chain \(\Lambda_{12}^{(f)}\Lambda_{23}^{(f)}\) feeds it at second order.
\end{enumerate}
\end{itemize}

\section{8. Important special case: nearest-neighbor dominance}

A particularly important seed regime is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|w_{12}^{(f)}| \text{ largest},
\qquad
|w_{23}^{(f)}| \text{ intermediate},
\qquad
|w_{13}^{(f)}| \text{ small},
}
\label{eq:K3C_nndom}
\end{equation}
with ordered gaps that do not undo this hierarchy.

\begin{theorem}[Nearest-neighbor dominance gives natural remote suppression]
Assume
\[
w_{13}^{(f)}=0
\]
and \(\eta_f\ll 1\).
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|U_{13}^{(f)}|
=
O\!\left(
\frac{|w_{12}^{(f)}w_{23}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{13}^{(f)}}
\left(
\frac{1}{\Delta_{12}^{(f)}}+\frac{1}{\Delta_{23}^{(f)}}
\right)
\right).
}
\label{eq:K3C_U13_chain}
\end{equation}
Hence the remote channel is automatically second-order suppressed.
If, in addition,
\[
h_{12}^{(f)}>h_{23}^{(f)}
\]
with sufficient margin, then the sectoral hierarchy seed is automatically of the form
\[
|U_{12}^{(f)}|>|U_{23}^{(f)}|>|U_{13}^{(f)}|.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
If \(w_{13}^{(f)}=0\), the first-order \(13\)-mixing vanishes.
So \(U_{13}^{(f)}\) begins at second order, and the chain estimate \eqref{eq:K3C_h13eff} gives the stated bound.
The remaining claim follows from the previous practical theorem.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Meaning.}
This is the cleanest regime for generating a natural hierarchy seed:
the remote channel is not forbidden, but it is automatically delayed by one perturbative order.

\section{9. Integrated practical \(K3C\) theorem}

We can now state the integrated theorem.

\begin{theorem}[Integrated practical \(K3C\) theorem]
Fix one sector \(f\).
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(K3B\) has already isolated the blockwise data \(D_f\), \(X^{(f)}\), and \(R^{(f)}\);
\item after absorbing the diagonal traceless remainder into \(D_f\), the operator has the form
\[
\widehat Y^{(f)}
=
\lambda_c^{(f)}\mathbf 1_3 + D_f + W_f,
\]
with \(D_f\) diagonal ordered and \(W_f\) off-diagonal Hermitian;
\item the diagonal-dominant regime \(2\|W_f\|<g_f\) holds.
\end{enumerate}

Then:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the sectoral diagonalizer satisfies
\[
|U_{ij}^{(f)}|
=
\frac{|w_{ij}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}} + O(\eta_f^2);
\]

\item the effective remote seed is bounded by
\[
|U_{13}^{(f)}|
\le
h_{13,\mathrm{eff}}^{(f)}+O(\eta_f^2);
\]

\item a practical sufficient condition for the sectoral hierarchy seed ordering
\[
|U_{12}^{(f)}|>|U_{23}^{(f)}|>|U_{13}^{(f)}|
\]
is that
\[
h_{12}^{(f)}-h_{23}^{(f)}>m_f,
\qquad
h_{23}^{(f)}-h_{13,\mathrm{eff}}^{(f)}>m_f,
\]
for some margin \(m_f\) dominating the \(O(\eta_f^2)\) uncertainty.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from the perturbative diagonalizer theorem and the effective \(13\)-seed estimate.
\end{proof}

\section{10. \(K3C\) Acceptance Sheet}

The \(K3C\) audit is now finite and literal.

\paragraph{Level 0: Structural input.}
Use the \(K3B\) output
\[
D_f,\qquad \Lambda_{12}^{(f)},\Lambda_{23}^{(f)},\Lambda_{13}^{(f)},\qquad R^{(f)}.
\]

\paragraph{Level 1: Build the ordered gaps.}
Compute
\[
\Delta_{12}^{(f)},\qquad \Delta_{23}^{(f)},\qquad \Delta_{13}^{(f)}.
\]

\paragraph{Level 2: Build the literal off-diagonal seeds.}
Compute
\[
w_{ij}^{(f)}=\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}+r_{ij}^{(f)}.
\]

\paragraph{Level 3: Compute the hierarchy-seed amplitudes.}
Compute
\[
h_{12}^{(f)}=\frac{|w_{12}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{12}^{(f)}},
\qquad
h_{23}^{(f)}=\frac{|w_{23}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{23}^{(f)}},
\]
and
\[
h_{13,\mathrm{eff}}^{(f)}
=
\frac{|w_{13}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{13}^{(f)}}
+
\frac{|w_{12}^{(f)}w_{23}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{13}^{(f)}}
\left(
\frac{1}{\Delta_{12}^{(f)}}+\frac{1}{\Delta_{23}^{(f)}}
\right).
\]

\paragraph{Level 4: Accept practical \(K3C\) if}
\[
h_{12}^{(f)}>h_{23}^{(f)}>h_{13,\mathrm{eff}}^{(f)}
\]
with a margin large compared with the perturbative \(O(\eta_f^2)\) uncertainty.

\paragraph{Level 5: Program-level interpretation.}
Passing \(K3C\) means:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the sector }f\text{ carries a hierarchical mixing seed in its own diagonalizer.}
}
\]
It does \emph{not} yet prove the physical CKM hierarchy.
That inter-sector statement belongs to \(K4\).

\section{Honest Status}

The structural status of \(K3C\) is now:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K3C\text{ is reduced to a finite hierarchy-seed audit on }
(D_f,W_f).
}
\end{equation}

But the microscopic acceptance status remains conditional until the actual intended-branch values of
\[
\Delta_{ij}^{(f)},\qquad
w_{ij}^{(f)}
\]
are inserted.

So the correct honest statement is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Structural status of }K3C:\ \text{closed at finite hierarchy-seed level.}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Microscopic acceptance status of }K3C:\ \text{conditional until the literal seed ratios are computed.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The hierarchy seed problem is sectorwise and is controlled by the ordered diagonal gaps
\[
\Delta_{12}^{(f)},\qquad \Delta_{23}^{(f)},\qquad \Delta_{13}^{(f)},
\]
together with the off-diagonal Hermitian seed entries
\[
w_{12}^{(f)},\qquad w_{23}^{(f)},\qquad w_{13}^{(f)}.
\]

In the diagonal-dominant regime,
\[
|U_{ij}^{(f)}|
=
\frac{|w_{ij}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}}+O(\eta_f^2),
\]
so the literal primary hierarchy seeds are
\[
h_{12}^{(f)}=\frac{|w_{12}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{12}^{(f)}},
\qquad
h_{23}^{(f)}=\frac{|w_{23}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{23}^{(f)}}.
\]

The remote channel requires special care and is controlled by the effective seed
\[
h_{13,\mathrm{eff}}^{(f)}
=
\frac{|w_{13}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{13}^{(f)}}
+
\frac{|w_{12}^{(f)}w_{23}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{13}^{(f)}}
\left(
\frac{1}{\Delta_{12}^{(f)}}+\frac{1}{\Delta_{23}^{(f)}}
\right).
\]

Therefore a practical sufficient condition for the sectorwise hierarchy seed ordering is
\[
h_{12}^{(f)}>h_{23}^{(f)}>h_{13,\mathrm{eff}}^{(f)},
\]
with margin large compared with the \(O(\eta_f^2)\) uncertainty.

This is not yet the physical CKM hierarchy.
It is the correct \(K3C\) input that will later feed the inter-sector comparison in \(K4\).

\section*{K3C Final Summary}

The \(K3C\) problem is the sectorwise hierarchy-seed problem for the diagonalizer \(U_f\) of the canonically normalized family operator.

Writing
\[
\widehat Y^{(f)}=\lambda_c^{(f)}\mathbf 1_3+D_f+W_f,
\]
with ordered diagonal gaps
\[
\Delta_{12}^{(f)},\quad \Delta_{23}^{(f)},\quad \Delta_{13}^{(f)},
\]
and off-diagonal entries
\[
w_{12}^{(f)},\quad w_{23}^{(f)},\quad w_{13}^{(f)},
\]
the diagonal-dominant regime gives
\[
|U_{ij}^{(f)}|
=
\frac{|w_{ij}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}}+O(\eta_f^2).
\]

Thus the primary hierarchy-seed amplitudes are
\[
h_{12}^{(f)}=\frac{|w_{12}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{12}^{(f)}},
\qquad
h_{23}^{(f)}=\frac{|w_{23}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{23}^{(f)}}.
\]

The remote channel must be controlled by the effective seed
\[
h_{13,\mathrm{eff}}^{(f)}
=
\frac{|w_{13}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{13}^{(f)}}
+
\frac{|w_{12}^{(f)}w_{23}^{(f)}|}{\Delta_{13}^{(f)}}
\left(
\frac{1}{\Delta_{12}^{(f)}}+\frac{1}{\Delta_{23}^{(f)}}
\right).
\]

Therefore a practical sufficient condition for the sectoral hierarchy seed ordering is
\[
h_{12}^{(f)}>h_{23}^{(f)}>h_{13,\mathrm{eff}}^{(f)},
\]
with margin large compared with the perturbative \(O(\eta_f^2)\) uncertainty.

This is the correct \(K3C\) output.
It is not yet the physical CKM hierarchy, but the sectorwise hierarchy seed that feeds the inter-sector analysis in \(K4\).
