\section{K4A: Inter-Sector Misalignment and the Leading CKM Hierarchy Seed}

\section{Goal}

At \(K3C\), each sector \(f\in\{u,d\}\) was shown to admit a sectorwise hierarchy seed in its own diagonalizer.
The physical CKM matrix, however, is not a sectorwise object.
It is the relative misalignment of the two sectoral diagonalizers:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{\mathrm{CKM}}=U_u^\dagger U_d.
}
\label{eq:K4A_CKM_def}
\end{equation}

Therefore the purpose of \(K4A\) is to extract the \emph{inter-sector hierarchy seed} controlling the magnitudes
\[
|V_{12}|,\qquad |V_{23}|,\qquad |V_{13}|.
\]

This is the first stage at which a genuine CKM-type hierarchy can be discussed.

\section{1. Necessity of \(K2_{\mathrm{align}}\)}

Before comparing two sectoral diagonalizers, both sectors must live in one common canonically normalized family basis.

\begin{proposition}[Why \(K2_{\mathrm{align}}\) is required]
The CKM matrix \(V_{\mathrm{CKM}}=U_u^\dagger U_d\) is physically meaningful only after the two sectors have been placed in one common family basis.

Equivalently, \(K4A\) requires the aligned version of \(K2\), not merely sectorwise positivity.
Without \(K2_{\mathrm{align}}\), the independent whitening ambiguities
\[
U_u\mapsto U_u W_u,
\qquad
U_d\mapsto U_d W_d,
\qquad
W_u,W_d\in U(3),
\]
make the relative matrix \(U_u^\dagger U_d\) basis-ambiguous.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Under independent sectorwise basis rotations,
\[
U_u^\dagger U_d \mapsto W_u^\dagger (U_u^\dagger U_d) W_d.
\]
Unless the two sectors have already been aligned into a common kinetic basis, \(W_u\) and \(W_d\) are unrelated and the matrix entries of \(U_u^\dagger U_d\) are not invariant data.
Thus \(K2_{\mathrm{align}}\) is a strict precondition for \(K4A\).
\end{proof}

\section{2. Sectoral diagonalizers in the small-misalignment regime}

Assume \(K2_{\mathrm{align}}\) and the \(K3C\) diagonal-dominant regime.
For each sector \(f\in\{u,d\}\), let
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_f=e^{\Omega_f},
\qquad
\Omega_f^\dagger=-\Omega_f,
}
\label{eq:K4A_Uf}
\end{equation}
be a unitary diagonalizer of the canonically normalized family operator.

At leading order,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Omega_f)_{ij}
=
\omega_{ij}^{(f)}
=
\frac{w_{ij}^{(f)}}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}}
+
O(\eta_f^2),
\qquad
1\le i<j\le 3,
}
\label{eq:K4A_omega_def}
\end{equation}
where
\[
\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}
\]
are the ordered diagonal gaps of the sectoral splitting operator and \(w_{ij}^{(f)}\) are the off-diagonal seed entries from \(K3C\).

Define the global small parameter
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\epsilon:=\max\Bigl(
|\omega_{12}^{(u)}|,
|\omega_{23}^{(u)}|,
|\omega_{13}^{(u)}|,
|\omega_{12}^{(d)}|,
|\omega_{23}^{(d)}|,
|\omega_{13}^{(d)}|
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:K4A_eps}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Relative generator and first-order CKM seed}

Define the relative anti-Hermitian generator
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Theta:=\Omega_d-\Omega_u.
}
\label{eq:K4A_Theta}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
V_{\mathrm{CKM}}
=
e^{-\Omega_u}e^{\Omega_d}
=
I+\Theta+O(\epsilon^2).
\label{eq:K4A_CKM_first}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[First-order CKM hierarchy seed]
In the aligned small-misalignment regime,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{12}=\Theta_{12}+O(\epsilon^2),
\qquad
V_{23}=\Theta_{23}+O(\epsilon^2),
\qquad
V_{13}=\Theta_{13}+O(\epsilon^2).
}
\label{eq:K4A_first_order_entries}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, the first-order relative CKM seed amplitudes are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{12}:=|\Theta_{12}|,
\qquad
H_{23}:=|\Theta_{23}|,
\qquad
H_{13}:=|\Theta_{13}|.
}
\label{eq:K4A_Hij_basic}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Expand
\[
e^{-\Omega_u}e^{\Omega_d}
=
(I-\Omega_u+O(\epsilon^2))(I+\Omega_d+O(\epsilon^2))
=
I+(\Omega_d-\Omega_u)+O(\epsilon^2).
\]
Thus the off-diagonal CKM entries are \(\Theta_{ij}+O(\epsilon^2)\).
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Meaning.}
To first order, the physical CKM hierarchy is seeded not by the sectoral mixings themselves but by their \emph{differences}:
\[
\omega_{ij}^{(d)}-\omega_{ij}^{(u)}.
\]

\section{4. Literal relative seed formulas}

Using the \(K3C\) first-order formulas,
\[
\omega_{ij}^{(f)}
=
\frac{w_{ij}^{(f)}}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}}+O(\eta_f^2),
\]
we obtain the literal relative seeds
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Theta_{12}
=
\frac{w_{12}^{(d)}}{\Delta_{12}^{(d)}}
-
\frac{w_{12}^{(u)}}{\Delta_{12}^{(u)}}
+
O(\eta_u^2+\eta_d^2),
}
\label{eq:K4A_Theta12}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Theta_{23}
=
\frac{w_{23}^{(d)}}{\Delta_{23}^{(d)}}
-
\frac{w_{23}^{(u)}}{\Delta_{23}^{(u)}}
+
O(\eta_u^2+\eta_d^2),
}
\label{eq:K4A_Theta23}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Theta_{13}
=
\frac{w_{13}^{(d)}}{\Delta_{13}^{(d)}}
-
\frac{w_{13}^{(u)}}{\Delta_{13}^{(u)}}
+
O(\eta_u^2+\eta_d^2).
}
\label{eq:K4A_Theta13}
\end{equation}

Thus the direct CKM misalignment seed is already a literal finite ratio-difference audit.

\section{5. Why the \(13\)-channel is special: second-order chain feed}

Although all off-diagonal entries begin with \(\Theta_{ij}\), the remote \(13\)-channel requires special care because it receives an unavoidable second-order chain contribution.

Expand to second order:
\[
e^{-\Omega_u}e^{\Omega_d}
=
I+(\Omega_d-\Omega_u)
+\frac12\Omega_d^2+\frac12\Omega_u^2-\Omega_u\Omega_d
+O(\epsilon^3).
\]

\begin{theorem}[Second-order remote-channel formula]
The \(13\) CKM entry satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{13}
=
\Theta_{13}
+
\frac12\,\omega_{12}^{(d)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}
+
\frac12\,\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(u)}
-
\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}
+
O(\epsilon^3).
}
\label{eq:K4A_V13_second}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|V_{13}|
\le
H_{13,\mathrm{eff}}+O(\epsilon^3),
}
\label{eq:K4A_V13_bound}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{13,\mathrm{eff}}
:=
|\Theta_{13}|
+
\frac12|\omega_{12}^{(d)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}|
+
\frac12|\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(u)}|
+
|\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}|.
}
\label{eq:K4A_H13eff}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
From the second-order product expansion,
\[
V_{13}
=
(\Omega_d-\Omega_u)_{13}
+\frac12(\Omega_d^2)_{13}
+\frac12(\Omega_u^2)_{13}
-(\Omega_u\Omega_d)_{13}
+O(\epsilon^3).
\]
Since the diagonal entries of \(\Omega_f\) vanish at this order,
\[
(\Omega_f^2)_{13}=(\Omega_f)_{12}(\Omega_f)_{23}
=
\omega_{12}^{(f)}\omega_{23}^{(f)},
\]
and
\[
(\Omega_u\Omega_d)_{13}
=
(\Omega_u)_{12}(\Omega_d)_{23}
=
\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}.
\]
Substituting these identities yields \eqref{eq:K4A_V13_second}.
The bound \eqref{eq:K4A_V13_bound} follows from the triangle inequality.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Meaning.}
The physical \(13\) CKM entry is not controlled only by the direct relative seed \(\Theta_{13}\).
Even if the direct remote mismatch is small, the \(1\to2\to3\) chain can generate a non-negligible \(V_{13}\).

This is the inter-sector analogue of the \(K3C\) remote-channel delicacy.

\section{6. Practical leading seeds for \(V_{12}\) and \(V_{23}\)}

The adjacent channels are simpler.
Their second-order corrections require a remote \(13\)-insertion and are therefore naturally suppressed in nearest-neighbor dominance regimes.

Indeed,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{12}
=
\Theta_{12}
+
O(\epsilon\,|\omega_{13}|_{\max})
+
O(\epsilon^3),
}
\label{eq:K4A_V12_bound}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{23}
=
\Theta_{23}
+
O(\epsilon\,|\omega_{13}|_{\max})
+
O(\epsilon^3),
}
\label{eq:K4A_V23_bound}
\end{equation}
where
\[
|\omega_{13}|_{\max}:=\max(|\omega_{13}^{(u)}|,|\omega_{13}^{(d)}|).
\]

Thus in the common practical regime of remote suppression,
\[
|V_{12}| \approx H_{12},
\qquad
|V_{23}| \approx H_{23},
\]
while \(V_{13}\) needs the enlarged effective seed \(H_{13,\mathrm{eff}}\).

\section{7. Practical CKM hierarchy-seed theorem}

We may now state the main practical theorem of \(K4A\).

\begin{theorem}[Practical \(K4A\) hierarchy-seed criterion]
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(K2_{\mathrm{align}}\) holds, so both sectors are represented in one common canonically normalized family basis;
\item each sector is in the \(K3C\) diagonal-dominant regime;
\item \(\epsilon\ll 1\), with \(\omega_{ij}^{(f)}\) defined by \eqref{eq:K4A_omega_def}.
\end{enumerate}

Define the leading relative seeds
\[
H_{12}:=|\Theta_{12}|,
\qquad
H_{23}:=|\Theta_{23}|,
\]
and the effective remote seed \(H_{13,\mathrm{eff}}\) from \eqref{eq:K4A_H13eff}.

Suppose there exists a positive margin \(m\) such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{12}-H_{23}>m,
}
\label{eq:K4A_margin12}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{23}-H_{13,\mathrm{eff}}>m.
}
\label{eq:K4A_margin23}
\end{equation}
If \(m\) dominates the higher-order error terms
\[
O(\epsilon\,|\omega_{13}|_{\max})+O(\epsilon^3),
\]
then the physical CKM magnitudes satisfy
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|V_{12}|>|V_{23}|>|V_{13}|.
}
\label{eq:K4A_CKM_order}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
From \eqref{eq:K4A_V12_bound}, \eqref{eq:K4A_V23_bound}, and \eqref{eq:K4A_V13_bound},
\[
|V_{12}|=H_{12}+ \text{controlled error},
\qquad
|V_{23}|=H_{23}+ \text{controlled error},
\qquad
|V_{13}|\le H_{13,\mathrm{eff}}+\text{controlled error}.
\]
If the strict margins \eqref{eq:K4A_margin12}--\eqref{eq:K4A_margin23} dominate these errors, the stated ordering follows.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
The physical CKM hierarchy is seeded by a finite inequality between three relative quantities:
\[
\boxed{
H_{12},\qquad H_{23},\qquad H_{13,\mathrm{eff}}.
}
\]
So \(K4A\) is not a vague alignment argument.
It is a literal inter-sector ratio-difference audit.

\section{8. Literal blockwise interpretation}

Recall from \(K3C\) that
\[
w_{ij}^{(f)}=\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}+r_{ij}^{(f)},
\]
where \(\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}\) is the literal \(TD/DT\) block extraction and \(r_{ij}^{(f)}\) is the off-diagonal remainder.

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{12}
=
\left|
\frac{\Lambda_{12}^{(d)}+r_{12}^{(d)}}{\Delta_{12}^{(d)}}
-
\frac{\Lambda_{12}^{(u)}+r_{12}^{(u)}}{\Delta_{12}^{(u)}}
\right|
+
O(\eta_u^2+\eta_d^2),
}
\label{eq:K4A_H12_literal}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{23}
=
\left|
\frac{\Lambda_{23}^{(d)}+r_{23}^{(d)}}{\Delta_{23}^{(d)}}
-
\frac{\Lambda_{23}^{(u)}+r_{23}^{(u)}}{\Delta_{23}^{(u)}}
\right|
+
O(\eta_u^2+\eta_d^2),
}
\label{eq:K4A_H23_literal}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{13,\mathrm{eff}}
=
\left|
\frac{\Lambda_{13}^{(d)}+r_{13}^{(d)}}{\Delta_{13}^{(d)}}
-
\frac{\Lambda_{13}^{(u)}+r_{13}^{(u)}}{\Delta_{13}^{(u)}}
\right|
+
\text{chain terms}
+
O(\eta_u^2+\eta_d^2).
}
\label{eq:K4A_H13_literal}
\end{equation}

Hence the physical CKM hierarchy seed is literally controlled by:

\begin{itemize}
\item sectoral gap denominators from the \(OO\)-anisotropy splittings,
\item sectoral off-diagonal numerators from the \(TD/DT\) block extractions,
\item their inter-sector differences,
\item and the unavoidable remote \(12\)-\(23\) chain feed in the \(13\)-channel.
\end{itemize}

\section{9. Important special case: nearest-neighbor misalignment dominance}

A particularly natural regime is:
\[
|\omega_{13}^{(u)}|,\ |\omega_{13}^{(d)}| \ll
|\omega_{12}^{(u)}|,\ |\omega_{23}^{(u)}|,\ |\omega_{12}^{(d)}|,\ |\omega_{23}^{(d)}|.
\]

\begin{theorem}[Nearest-neighbor misalignment dominance]
If the direct remote mixings are suppressed,
\[
|\omega_{13}^{(u)}|,\ |\omega_{13}^{(d)}| = O(\epsilon^2),
\]
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|V_{12}|=H_{12}+O(\epsilon^3),
\qquad
|V_{23}|=H_{23}+O(\epsilon^3),
}
\label{eq:K4A_nn_V12V23}
\end{equation}
while
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|V_{13}|
\le
|\Theta_{13}|
+
\frac12|\omega_{12}^{(d)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}|
+
\frac12|\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(u)}|
+
|\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}|
+
O(\epsilon^3).
}
\label{eq:K4A_nn_V13}
\end{equation}
Thus the remote channel is automatically delayed by one perturbative order relative to the adjacent channels, unless the direct relative seed \(\Theta_{13}\) is anomalously large.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Under the stated suppression, the \(13\)-dependent corrections in \(V_{12}\) and \(V_{23}\) become \(O(\epsilon^3)\), while the \(13\) channel still receives the second-order chain contribution displayed in \eqref{eq:K4A_V13_second}.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Meaning.}
This is the cleanest mechanism for generating the physical ordering
\[
|V_{12}|>|V_{23}|>|V_{13}|
\]
from the microscopic TECT branch: adjacent relative mismatches appear at first order, while the remote channel is naturally second-order delayed.

\section{10. (K4A) Acceptance Sheet}

The \(K4A\) audit is now completely finite.

\paragraph{Level 0: Basis admissibility.}
Verify \(K2_{\mathrm{align}}\).

\paragraph{Level 1: Sectorwise diagonalizer inputs.}
Use the \(K3C\) outputs
\[
\Delta_{ij}^{(u)},\quad \Delta_{ij}^{(d)},
\qquad
w_{ij}^{(u)},\quad w_{ij}^{(d)}.
\]

\paragraph{Level 2: Build the sectoral mixing seeds.}
Compute
\[
\omega_{ij}^{(f)}=\frac{w_{ij}^{(f)}}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}}.
\]

\paragraph{Level 3: Build the inter-sector relative seeds.}
Compute
\[
\Theta_{ij}=\omega_{ij}^{(d)}-\omega_{ij}^{(u)},
\]
and
\[
H_{12}=|\Theta_{12}|,
\qquad
H_{23}=|\Theta_{23}|,
\]
together with
\[
H_{13,\mathrm{eff}}
=
|\Theta_{13}|
+
\frac12|\omega_{12}^{(d)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}|
+
\frac12|\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(u)}|
+
|\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}|.
\]

\paragraph{Level 4: Accept practical \(K4A\) if}
\[
H_{12}>H_{23}>H_{13,\mathrm{eff}}
\]
with margins large compared with the controlled higher-order errors.

\paragraph{Level 5: Program-level interpretation.}
Passing \(K4A\) means:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the physical CKM magnitude hierarchy is seeded at leading/practical order.}
}
\]
This still does not produce an irreducible CP phase.
That remains \(K5\).

\section{Honest Status}

The structural status of \(K4A\) is now:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K4A\text{ is reduced to a finite inter-sector misalignment audit.}
}
\end{equation}

The remaining microscopic work is only the explicit intended-branch evaluation of
\[
\Delta_{ij}^{(u)},\ \Delta_{ij}^{(d)},\ 
w_{ij}^{(u)},\ w_{ij}^{(d)},
\]
hence of
\[
\Theta_{12},\ \Theta_{23},\ \Theta_{13},\ H_{13,\mathrm{eff}}.
\]

Therefore the honest statement is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Structural status of }K4A:\ \text{closed at finite relative-seed level.}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Microscopic acceptance status of }K4A:\ \text{conditional until the relative seed audit is executed.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The physical CKM hierarchy begins only at the inter-sector level.
Its leading seed is the relative anti-Hermitian generator
\[
\Theta=\Omega_d-\Omega_u,
\]
not the sectorwise generators separately.

To first order,
\[
V_{12}=\Theta_{12}+O(\epsilon^2),
\qquad
V_{23}=\Theta_{23}+O(\epsilon^2),
\qquad
V_{13}=\Theta_{13}+O(\epsilon^2).
\]

More precisely, the remote channel satisfies
\[
V_{13}
=
\Theta_{13}
+
\frac12\,\omega_{12}^{(d)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}
+
\frac12\,\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(u)}
-
\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}
+
O(\epsilon^3),
\]
so it is controlled by the effective seed
\[
H_{13,\mathrm{eff}}
=
|\Theta_{13}|
+
\frac12|\omega_{12}^{(d)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}|
+
\frac12|\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(u)}|
+
|\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}|.
\]

Therefore a practical sufficient criterion for the physical magnitude hierarchy is
\[
H_{12}>H_{23}>H_{13,\mathrm{eff}},
\]
with margins large compared with the higher-order errors.

Hence \(K4A\) is fully reduced to a finite inter-sector relative-seed audit.

\section*{K4A Final Summary}

The physical CKM matrix is
\[
V_{\mathrm{CKM}}=U_u^\dagger U_d,
\]
so the correct leading hierarchy seed is the relative generator
\[
\Theta=\Omega_d-\Omega_u.
\]

Using the sectoral first-order mixing generators
\[
\omega_{ij}^{(f)}=\frac{w_{ij}^{(f)}}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}},
\]
the leading relative seeds are
\[
\Theta_{12}
=
\frac{w_{12}^{(d)}}{\Delta_{12}^{(d)}}
-
\frac{w_{12}^{(u)}}{\Delta_{12}^{(u)}},
\qquad
\Theta_{23}
=
\frac{w_{23}^{(d)}}{\Delta_{23}^{(d)}}
-
\frac{w_{23}^{(u)}}{\Delta_{23}^{(u)}},
\]
and
\[
\Theta_{13}
=
\frac{w_{13}^{(d)}}{\Delta_{13}^{(d)}}
-
\frac{w_{13}^{(u)}}{\Delta_{13}^{(u)}}.
\]

The adjacent CKM entries satisfy
\[
V_{12}=\Theta_{12}+O(\epsilon^2),
\qquad
V_{23}=\Theta_{23}+O(\epsilon^2).
\]

The remote channel is more delicate:
\[
V_{13}
=
\Theta_{13}
+
\frac12\,\omega_{12}^{(d)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}
+
\frac12\,\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(u)}
-
\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}
+
O(\epsilon^3).
\]
Hence an effective practical upper seed is
\[
H_{13,\mathrm{eff}}
=
|\Theta_{13}|
+
\frac12|\omega_{12}^{(d)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}|
+
\frac12|\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(u)}|
+
|\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}|.
\]

Therefore a practical sufficient criterion for the physical CKM magnitude hierarchy is
\[
H_{12}>H_{23}>H_{13,\mathrm{eff}},
\]
with margins large compared with the controlled higher-order errors.

Thus \(K4A\) is fully reduced to a finite inter-sector relative-seed audit.

\section{K4B: Stable Parameter Window for the CKM Hierarchy Seed}

\section{Goal}

At \(K4A\), the physical CKM magnitude hierarchy was reduced to the finite relative-seed criterion
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{12}>H_{23}>H_{13,\mathrm{eff}},
}
\label{eq:K4B_seed_order}
\end{equation}
where
\[
H_{12}=|\Theta_{12}|,
\qquad
H_{23}=|\Theta_{23}|,
\]
and
\[
H_{13,\mathrm{eff}}
=
|\Theta_{13}|
+
\frac12|\omega_{12}^{(d)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}|
+
\frac12|\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(u)}|
+
|\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}|.
\]

The purpose of \(K4B\) is to upgrade this pointwise criterion to a \emph{stable parameter-window theorem}.

In other words, we now ask:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{If the hierarchy seed holds at one reference point, when does it remain true on an open neighborhood?}
}
\end{equation}

\section{1. Exact relative-seed variables}

Define the exact leading sectoral misalignment variables
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\omega_{ij}^{(f)}:=\frac{w_{ij}^{(f)}}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}},
\qquad
f\in\{u,d\},
\quad
1\le i<j\le 3,
}
\label{eq:K4B_omega}
\end{equation}
and the relative seeds
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A:=H_{12}=|\omega_{12}^{(d)}-\omega_{12}^{(u)}|,
}
\label{eq:K4B_A}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B:=H_{23}=|\omega_{23}^{(d)}-\omega_{23}^{(u)}|,
}
\label{eq:K4B_B}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C:=H_{13,\mathrm{eff}}
=
|\omega_{13}^{(d)}-\omega_{13}^{(u)}|
+\frac12|\omega_{12}^{(d)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}|
+\frac12|\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(u)}|
+|\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}|.
}
\label{eq:K4B_C}
\end{equation}

Thus the leading/practical CKM hierarchy-seed condition is simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A>B>C.
}
\label{eq:K4B_ABC}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Margin variables}

Fix a reference intended-branch point \(P_\ast\).
Let the corresponding reference seed values be
\[
A_\ast,\qquad B_\ast,\qquad C_\ast.
\]
Assume strict seed hierarchy at the reference point:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_\ast>B_\ast>C_\ast.
}
\label{eq:K4B_ref_order}
\end{equation}

Define the two strict margins
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_{12}:=A_\ast-B_\ast>0,
\qquad
m_{23}:=B_\ast-C_\ast>0.
}
\label{eq:K4B_margins}
\end{equation}

These are the exact quantitative buffers that protect the ordering against perturbations.

\section{3. Stability theorem in \(\omega\)-space}

We first prove stability directly in the relative-seed variables.

Let
\[
\delta\omega_{ij}^{(f)}:=\omega_{ij}^{(f)}-\omega_{ij,\ast}^{(f)}.
\]
Assume the uniform bound
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\delta\omega_{ij}^{(f)}|\le \varepsilon_\omega
\qquad
\text{for all }f\in\{u,d\},\ 1\le i<j\le 3.
}
\label{eq:K4B_epsomega}
\end{equation}

Also define the reference size bound
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Omega_\ast:=\max\Bigl(
|\omega_{12,\ast}^{(u)}|,
|\omega_{23,\ast}^{(u)}|,
|\omega_{13,\ast}^{(u)}|,
|\omega_{12,\ast}^{(d)}|,
|\omega_{23,\ast}^{(d)}|,
|\omega_{13,\ast}^{(d)}|
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:K4B_Omegastar}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Seed-window stability in \(\omega\)-space]
Under \eqref{eq:K4B_epsomega}, the seed variables satisfy
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|A-A_\ast|\le 2\varepsilon_\omega,
\qquad
|B-B_\ast|\le 2\varepsilon_\omega,
}
\label{eq:K4B_AB_bound}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|C-C_\ast|
\le
2\varepsilon_\omega
+
4\Omega_\ast\varepsilon_\omega
+
2\varepsilon_\omega^2.
}
\label{eq:K4B_C_bound}
\end{equation}

Therefore, if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
4\varepsilon_\omega < m_{12},
}
\label{eq:K4B_cond12}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
4\varepsilon_\omega+4\Omega_\ast\varepsilon_\omega+2\varepsilon_\omega^2 < m_{23},
}
\label{eq:K4B_cond23}
\end{equation}
then the strict ordering
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A>B>C
}
\label{eq:K4B_stable_seed}
\end{equation}
holds throughout the entire \(\varepsilon_\omega\)-ball around \(P_\ast\).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
For the adjacent channels,
\[
A=|\omega_{12}^{(d)}-\omega_{12}^{(u)}|,
\qquad
A_\ast=|\omega_{12,\ast}^{(d)}-\omega_{12,\ast}^{(u)}|.
\]
Hence, by the reverse triangle inequality,
\[
|A-A_\ast|
\le
|\delta\omega_{12}^{(d)}|+|\delta\omega_{12}^{(u)}|
\le
2\varepsilon_\omega.
\]
Exactly the same argument gives \(|B-B_\ast|\le 2\varepsilon_\omega\).

Now consider \(C\).
The direct term obeys
\[
\bigl||\omega_{13}^{(d)}-\omega_{13}^{(u)}|-|\omega_{13,\ast}^{(d)}-\omega_{13,\ast}^{(u)}|\bigr|
\le
|\delta\omega_{13}^{(d)}|+|\delta\omega_{13}^{(u)}|
\le
2\varepsilon_\omega.
\]

For a generic product \(ab\), one has
\[
|ab-a_\ast b_\ast|
\le
|a-a_\ast|\,|b|+|b-b_\ast|\,|a_\ast|.
\]
If \(|a-a_\ast|,|b-b_\ast|\le \varepsilon_\omega\) and \(|a_\ast|,|b_\ast|\le \Omega_\ast\), then
\[
|b|\le |b_\ast|+\varepsilon_\omega\le \Omega_\ast+\varepsilon_\omega,
\]
so
\[
|ab-a_\ast b_\ast|
\le
\varepsilon_\omega(\Omega_\ast+\varepsilon_\omega)+\varepsilon_\omega\Omega_\ast
=
2\Omega_\ast\varepsilon_\omega+\varepsilon_\omega^2.
\]
Applying this to each of the three product terms in \(C\), with weights \(1/2,1/2,1\), yields
\[
|C-C_\ast|
\le
2\varepsilon_\omega
+
\Bigl(\tfrac12+\tfrac12+1\Bigr)(2\Omega_\ast\varepsilon_\omega+\varepsilon_\omega^2),
\]
hence
\[
|C-C_\ast|
\le
2\varepsilon_\omega+4\Omega_\ast\varepsilon_\omega+2\varepsilon_\omega^2.
\]

Finally,
\[
A-B
=
(A_\ast-B_\ast)+(A-A_\ast)-(B-B_\ast),
\]
so
\[
A-B
\ge
m_{12}-|A-A_\ast|-|B-B_\ast|
\ge
m_{12}-4\varepsilon_\omega.
\]
Thus \eqref{eq:K4B_cond12} implies \(A>B\).

Likewise,
\[
B-C
\ge
m_{23}-|B-B_\ast|-|C-C_\ast|
\ge
m_{23}-\Bigl(2\varepsilon_\omega+2\varepsilon_\omega+4\Omega_\ast\varepsilon_\omega+2\varepsilon_\omega^2\Bigr),
\]
which is positive under \eqref{eq:K4B_cond23}.
Therefore \(B>C\), and hence \(A>B>C\).
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Meaning.}
The hierarchy seed is stable on an \emph{open neighborhood}.
It is not a measure-zero accident.
Strict margin at one point plus sufficiently small perturbation implies stable ordering.

\section{4. Pullback to microscopic \((\Delta,w)\)-space}

The previous theorem is already sufficient if the exact \(\omega\)-variables are the numerical audit objects.
However, it is more useful to express the window directly in the microscopic ratios
\[
\omega_{ij}^{(f)}=\frac{w_{ij}^{(f)}}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}}.
\]

Let the reference microscopic data be
\[
\Delta_{ij,\ast}^{(f)},\qquad w_{ij,\ast}^{(f)}.
\]
Assume the following bounded-gap/bounded-numerator conditions in the neighborhood:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}\ge g_\ast>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{ij,\ast}^{(f)}\ge g_\ast>0,
}
\label{eq:K4B_gap_lower}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|w_{ij}^{(f)}|,\ |w_{ij,\ast}^{(f)}|\le W_\ast.
}
\label{eq:K4B_num_upper}
\end{equation}

Assume further the componentwise perturbation bounds
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|w_{ij}^{(f)}-w_{ij,\ast}^{(f)}|\le \rho,
\qquad
|\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}-\Delta_{ij,\ast}^{(f)}|\le \delta,
}
\label{eq:K4B_rho_delta}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta\le \frac{g_\ast}{2}.
}
\label{eq:K4B_delta_small}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Microscopic window bound]
Under \eqref{eq:K4B_gap_lower}--\eqref{eq:K4B_delta_small},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\omega_{ij}^{(f)}-\omega_{ij,\ast}^{(f)}|
\le
\frac{2\rho}{g_\ast}
+
\frac{2W_\ast}{g_\ast^2}\,\delta
=: \varepsilon_\omega^{\mathrm{mic}}.
}
\label{eq:K4B_omega_mic_bound}
\end{equation}
Hence the seed hierarchy \(A>B>C\) is stable on the microscopic neighborhood whenever
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
4\varepsilon_\omega^{\mathrm{mic}} < m_{12},
}
\label{eq:K4B_mic_cond12}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
4\varepsilon_\omega^{\mathrm{mic}}
+
4\Omega_\ast\varepsilon_\omega^{\mathrm{mic}}
+
2(\varepsilon_\omega^{\mathrm{mic}})^2
<
m_{23}.
}
\label{eq:K4B_mic_cond23}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Write
\[
\frac{w}{\Delta}-\frac{w_\ast}{\Delta_\ast}
=
\frac{w-w_\ast}{\Delta}
+
w_\ast\Bigl(\frac{1}{\Delta}-\frac{1}{\Delta_\ast}\Bigr).
\]
Taking absolute values,
\[
\left|\frac{w}{\Delta}-\frac{w_\ast}{\Delta_\ast}\right|
\le
\frac{|w-w_\ast|}{\Delta}
+
|w_\ast|\frac{|\Delta-\Delta_\ast|}{|\Delta\,\Delta_\ast|}.
\]
Using \(\Delta\ge g_\ast/2\), \(\Delta_\ast\ge g_\ast\), \(|w_\ast|\le W_\ast\), we get
\[
\left|\frac{w}{\Delta}-\frac{w_\ast}{\Delta_\ast}\right|
\le
\frac{2\rho}{g_\ast}
+
\frac{2W_\ast}{g_\ast^2}\delta.
\]
This proves \eqref{eq:K4B_omega_mic_bound}. The rest follows by inserting
\[
\varepsilon_\omega=\varepsilon_\omega^{\mathrm{mic}}
\]
into the \(\omega\)-space stability theorem.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Meaning.}
The stable hierarchy window can be verified directly from microscopic error budgets:
\[
\text{numerator variation } \rho,\qquad
\text{gap variation } \delta,\qquad
\text{gap floor } g_\ast,\qquad
\text{numerator ceiling } W_\ast.
\]

\section{5. Lifting the seed window to the actual CKM hierarchy}

Up to now we have proven stability of the \emph{leading/practical seed hierarchy}.
To pass from this to the actual CKM magnitude ordering, we must also control the higher-order BCH remainder terms.

Assume one has remainder budgets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|V_{12}-A|\le r_{12},
\qquad
|V_{23}-B|\le r_{23},
\qquad
|V_{13}|\le C+r_{13},
}
\label{eq:K4B_remainder_budgets}
\end{equation}
where \(r_{12},r_{23},r_{13}\) are explicit higher-order bounds obtained from the small-misalignment expansion.

\begin{corollary}[Stable full CKM window]
If
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A-B > r_{12}+r_{23},
}
\label{eq:K4B_full_cond12}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B-C > r_{23}+r_{13},
}
\label{eq:K4B_full_cond23}
\end{equation}
then the actual physical CKM magnitudes satisfy
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|V_{12}|>|V_{23}|>|V_{13}|.
}
\label{eq:K4B_full_hierarchy}
\end{equation}

Moreover, if the seed inequalities are stable on a neighborhood and the remainder budgets remain uniformly bounded there, then the full CKM magnitude hierarchy is also stable on that neighborhood.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
From \eqref{eq:K4B_remainder_budgets},
\[
|V_{12}|
\ge
A-r_{12},
\qquad
|V_{23}|
\le
B+r_{23},
\]
so \eqref{eq:K4B_full_cond12} implies \(|V_{12}|>|V_{23}|\).

Likewise,
\[
|V_{23}|
\ge
B-r_{23},
\qquad
|V_{13}|
\le
C+r_{13},
\]
so \eqref{eq:K4B_full_cond23} implies \(|V_{23}|>|V_{13}|\).
The neighborhood statement is immediate.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Meaning.}
K4B cleanly separates two issues:
\begin{enumerate}
\item stability of the \emph{leading relative seed ordering};
\item lifting that stable ordering to the actual CKM magnitudes by explicit BCH remainder control.
\end{enumerate}

\section{6. Integrated practical \(K4B\) theorem}

We may now state the integrated theorem.

\begin{theorem}[Integrated practical \(K4B\) theorem]
Fix a reference intended-branch point \(P_\ast\).
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(K2_{\mathrm{align}}\) holds, so both sectors lie in a common canonically normalized family basis;
\item the \(K4A\) relative seeds are defined;
\item the reference point satisfies strict seed hierarchy
\[
A_\ast>B_\ast>C_\ast;
\]
\item the strict margins
\[
m_{12}=A_\ast-B_\ast,
\qquad
m_{23}=B_\ast-C_\ast
\]
are positive;
\item the microscopic perturbations obey
\[
|w_{ij}^{(f)}-w_{ij,\ast}^{(f)}|\le \rho,
\qquad
|\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}-\Delta_{ij,\ast}^{(f)}|\le \delta,
\]
with gap floor \(g_\ast>0\), numerator ceiling \(W_\ast\), and \(\delta\le g_\ast/2\).
\end{enumerate}

Define
\[
\varepsilon_\omega^{\mathrm{mic}}
=
\frac{2\rho}{g_\ast}
+
\frac{2W_\ast}{g_\ast^2}\delta.
\]

Then:

\begin{enumerate}
\item if
\[
4\varepsilon_\omega^{\mathrm{mic}}<m_{12},
\qquad
4\varepsilon_\omega^{\mathrm{mic}}
+
4\Omega_\ast\varepsilon_\omega^{\mathrm{mic}}
+
2(\varepsilon_\omega^{\mathrm{mic}})^2
<
m_{23},
\]
the strict seed hierarchy
\[
A>B>C
\]
holds throughout the microscopic neighborhood;

\item if in addition the actual CKM remainder budgets satisfy
\[
A-B>r_{12}+r_{23},
\qquad
B-C>r_{23}+r_{13},
\]
uniformly on that neighborhood, then the full physical hierarchy
\[
|V_{12}|>|V_{23}|>|V_{13}|
\]
also holds throughout that neighborhood.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from the microscopic window theorem and the stable full CKM corollary.
\end{proof}

\section{7. \(K4B\) Acceptance Sheet}

The \(K4B\) audit is now finite and quantitative.

\paragraph{Level 0: Reference point.}
Choose one intended-branch reference point \(P_\ast\) and compute
\[
A_\ast,\qquad B_\ast,\qquad C_\ast.
\]

\paragraph{Level 1: Reference strict margins.}
Compute
\[
m_{12}=A_\ast-B_\ast,
\qquad
m_{23}=B_\ast-C_\ast.
\]
These must both be strictly positive.

\paragraph{Level 2: Microscopic neighborhood data.}
Estimate
\[
g_\ast,\qquad W_\ast,\qquad \rho,\qquad \delta.
\]
Then compute
\[
\varepsilon_\omega^{\mathrm{mic}}
=
\frac{2\rho}{g_\ast}
+
\frac{2W_\ast}{g_\ast^2}\delta.
\]

\paragraph{Level 3: Stable seed window test.}
Accept stable seed hierarchy on the neighborhood if
\[
4\varepsilon_\omega^{\mathrm{mic}}<m_{12},
\]
and
\[
4\varepsilon_\omega^{\mathrm{mic}}
+
4\Omega_\ast\varepsilon_\omega^{\mathrm{mic}}
+
2(\varepsilon_\omega^{\mathrm{mic}})^2
<
m_{23}.
\]

\paragraph{Level 4: Stable full CKM test.}
If explicit BCH remainder budgets \(r_{12},r_{23},r_{13}\) are available, accept stable full CKM hierarchy if
\[
A-B>r_{12}+r_{23},
\qquad
B-C>r_{23}+r_{13}
\]
throughout the same neighborhood.

\paragraph{Level 5: Program-level interpretation.}
Passing Level 3 means:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the CKM hierarchy seed is stable on an open microscopic parameter window.}
}
\]
Passing Level 4 means:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the actual CKM magnitude hierarchy is stable on that window.}
}
\]

\section{Honest Status}

The structural status of \(K4B\) is now:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K4B\text{ is reduced to a finite margin-versus-error audit.}
}
\end{equation}

What remains microscopically is not conceptual reformulation, but the actual intended-branch insertion of:
\[
A_\ast,\ B_\ast,\ C_\ast,\ m_{12},\ m_{23},
\]
and the neighborhood bounds
\[
g_\ast,\ W_\ast,\ \rho,\ \delta,
\]
together with the BCH remainder budgets
\[
r_{12},\ r_{23},\ r_{13}.
\]

Therefore the correct honest statement is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Structural status of }K4B:\ \text{closed at stable-window level.}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Microscopic acceptance status of }K4B:\ \text{conditional until the finite window audit is executed.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The CKM hierarchy seed
\[
A>B>C
\]
with
\[
A=|\omega_{12}^{(d)}-\omega_{12}^{(u)}|,
\qquad
B=|\omega_{23}^{(d)}-\omega_{23}^{(u)}|,
\qquad
C=H_{13,\mathrm{eff}},
\]
is stable on an open neighborhood whenever the strict reference margins
\[
m_{12}=A_\ast-B_\ast,
\qquad
m_{23}=B_\ast-C_\ast
\]
dominate the perturbation-induced seed changes.

At the \(\omega\)-level, this requires
\[
4\varepsilon_\omega<m_{12},
\qquad
4\varepsilon_\omega+4\Omega_\ast\varepsilon_\omega+2\varepsilon_\omega^2<m_{23}.
\]

At the microscopic level, if
\[
|w-w_\ast|\le \rho,
\qquad
|\Delta-\Delta_\ast|\le \delta,
\qquad
\Delta_\ast,\Delta\ge g_\ast>0,
\]
with \(\delta\le g_\ast/2\), then
\[
\varepsilon_\omega^{\mathrm{mic}}
=
\frac{2\rho}{g_\ast}
+
\frac{2W_\ast}{g_\ast^2}\delta
\]
controls the seed variation.

If, in addition, the BCH remainder budgets obey
\[
A-B>r_{12}+r_{23},
\qquad
B-C>r_{23}+r_{13},
\]
then the full physical CKM magnitude hierarchy
\[
|V_{12}|>|V_{23}|>|V_{13}|
\]
is stable on the same parameter window.

Hence \(K4B\) is fully reduced to a finite margin-versus-error acceptance audit.

\section*{K4B Final Summary}

Let
\[
A=|\omega_{12}^{(d)}-\omega_{12}^{(u)}|,
\qquad
B=|\omega_{23}^{(d)}-\omega_{23}^{(u)}|,
\qquad
C=H_{13,\mathrm{eff}}.
\]
At a reference intended-branch point \(P_\ast\), assume
\[
A_\ast>B_\ast>C_\ast
\]
with strict margins
\[
m_{12}=A_\ast-B_\ast>0,
\qquad
m_{23}=B_\ast-C_\ast>0.
\]

If the exact relative seed variables satisfy
\[
|\delta\omega_{ij}^{(f)}|\le \varepsilon_\omega,
\]
then
\[
|A-A_\ast|\le 2\varepsilon_\omega,
\qquad
|B-B_\ast|\le 2\varepsilon_\omega,
\]
and
\[
|C-C_\ast|
\le
2\varepsilon_\omega+4\Omega_\ast\varepsilon_\omega+2\varepsilon_\omega^2.
\]
Therefore the strict seed hierarchy \(A>B>C\) is stable if
\[
4\varepsilon_\omega<m_{12},
\qquad
4\varepsilon_\omega+4\Omega_\ast\varepsilon_\omega+2\varepsilon_\omega^2<m_{23}.
\]

If the seed variables come from microscopic ratios
\[
\omega_{ij}^{(f)}=\frac{w_{ij}^{(f)}}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}},
\]
with
\[
|w-w_\ast|\le \rho,
\qquad
|\Delta-\Delta_\ast|\le \delta,
\qquad
\Delta,\Delta_\ast\ge g_\ast>0,
\]
and \(\delta\le g_\ast/2\), then
\[
\varepsilon_\omega^{\mathrm{mic}}
=
\frac{2\rho}{g_\ast}
+
\frac{2W_\ast}{g_\ast^2}\delta
\]
controls the seed variation.

If, in addition, explicit BCH remainder budgets satisfy
\[
|V_{12}-A|\le r_{12},
\qquad
|V_{23}-B|\le r_{23},
\qquad
|V_{13}|\le C+r_{13},
\]
and
\[
A-B>r_{12}+r_{23},
\qquad
B-C>r_{23}+r_{13},
\]
then the full physical CKM magnitude hierarchy
\[
|V_{12}|>|V_{23}|>|V_{13}|
\]
is stable on the same parameter window.

Hence \(K4B\) is reduced to a finite margin-versus-error audit.

\section{K5A: Exact Irreducible CP Seed and No-Go Theorems}

\section{Goal}

After \(K4A\) and \(K4B\), the magnitude hierarchy problem has been reduced to a finite inter-sector relative-seed audit.
The next question is different in kind:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{when does the CKM structure contain an irreducible CP-violating seed?}
}
\end{equation}

This is \emph{not} the same as asking whether some matrix entries are complex.
Complex phases are only physical if they survive all admissible family rephasings.

Therefore \(K5A\) has two tasks:

\begin{enumerate}
\item identify the exact rephasing-invariant CP seed;
\item prove the main no-go theorems showing why single-spurion or common-planar alignment cannot generate irreducible CP violation.
\end{enumerate}

\section{1. Exact common-basis setup}

Assume \(K2_{\mathrm{align}}\) has already been accepted, so both sectors are represented in one common canonically normalized left-handed family basis.

Let
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat Y_u,\qquad \widehat Y_d
}
\label{eq:K5A_YuYd}
\end{equation}
be the canonically normalized Hermitian family operators for the up and down sectors.

Let their diagonalizers be
\[
U_u^\dagger \widehat Y_u U_u=\operatorname{diag}(y_1^{(u)},y_2^{(u)},y_3^{(u)}),
\qquad
U_d^\dagger \widehat Y_d U_d=\operatorname{diag}(y_1^{(d)},y_2^{(d)},y_3^{(d)}),
\]
and define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{\mathrm{CKM}}:=U_u^\dagger U_d.
}
\label{eq:K5A_CKM}
\end{equation}

We assume throughout the nondegeneracy regime already isolated in \(K3A\), so that the sectoral eigenbases are physically meaningful up to diagonal rephasings and permutations.

\section{2. Exact CP-odd invariant}

Define the exact commutator invariant
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}
:=
\frac{1}{3i}\,\operatorname{tr}\!\bigl([\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d]^3\bigr).
}
\label{eq:K5A_Jexact}
\end{equation}

Since \([\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d]\) is anti-Hermitian and traceless, \(\operatorname{tr}([\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d]^3)\) is purely imaginary, so \(\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}\in\mathbb R\).

\begin{theorem}[Exact irreducible CP criterion]
Assume both \(\widehat Y_u\) and \(\widehat Y_d\) have simple spectra.
Then the following are equivalent:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the pair \((\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d)\) carries an irreducible CP-violating seed;
\item the CKM matrix cannot be made real by allowed family rephasings;
\item the Jarlskog invariant \(J_{\mathrm{CKM}}\) is nonzero;
\item
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:K5A_exact_accept}
\end{equation}
\end{enumerate}

Moreover, one has the exact factorization
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}
=
2\,J_{\mathrm{CKM}}
\prod_{1\le i<j\le 3}(y_i^{(u)}-y_j^{(u)})
\prod_{1\le i<j\le 3}(y_i^{(d)}-y_j^{(d)}).
}
\label{eq:K5A_J_factor}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
For two Hermitian \(3\times3\) matrices with simple spectra, the standard Jarlskog identity gives
\[
\det([\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d])
=
2i\,J_{\mathrm{CKM}}
\prod_{i<j}(y_i^{(u)}-y_j^{(u)})
\prod_{i<j}(y_i^{(d)}-y_j^{(d)}).
\]
Because the commutator is traceless \(3\times3\), one has
\[
\operatorname{tr}(C^3)=3\det(C)
\qquad
\text{for }C=[\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d].
\]
Therefore
\[
\frac{1}{3i}\operatorname{tr}(C^3)
=
\frac{1}{i}\det(C)
=
2\,J_{\mathrm{CKM}}
\prod_{i<j}(y_i^{(u)}-y_j^{(u)})
\prod_{i<j}(y_i^{(d)}-y_j^{(d)}),
\]
which is \eqref{eq:K5A_J_factor}.
Since the spectral products are nonzero in the simple-spectrum regime, \(\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}\neq 0\) is equivalent to \(J_{\mathrm{CKM}}\neq 0\), which is equivalent to irreducible CKM CP violation.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Meaning.}
This is the exact finite criterion for \(K5A\).
No philosophical ambiguity remains:
\[
\boxed{
\text{irreducible CP seed} \iff \mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}\neq 0.
}
\]

\section{3. No-go theorem I: single spurion / commuting pair}

The first obstruction is exact and absolute.

\begin{theorem}[No irreducible CP from a single spurion]
If there exists one Hermitian matrix \(S\) such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat Y_u=F_u(S),
\qquad
\widehat Y_d=F_d(S),
}
\label{eq:K5A_single_spurion}
\end{equation}
for some real functional calculus \(F_u,F_d\), then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
[\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d]=0,
\qquad
\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}=0,
\qquad
J_{\mathrm{CKM}}=0.
}
\label{eq:K5A_single_spurion_nogo}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Any two functions of the same Hermitian matrix commute.
Hence \([\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d]=0\), so \(\operatorname{tr}([\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d]^3)=0\), thus \(\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}=0\).
Commuting Hermitian matrices are simultaneously diagonalizable, so the CKM matrix is a permutation-times-diagonal-phase matrix and carries no irreducible CP phase.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
This is the precise mathematical form of the statement:

\[
\boxed{
\text{one spurion is not enough.}
}
\]

If both sectors are generated from the same single family operator, they can only differ by eigenvalues, not by irreducible phase misalignment.

\section{4. No-go theorem II: common realification}

The second obstruction is the common-planar/common-phase alignment no-go.

\begin{theorem}[No irreducible CP from common realification]
Assume there exists a single diagonal phase matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P=\operatorname{diag}(e^{i\alpha_1},e^{i\alpha_2},e^{i\alpha_3})
}
\label{eq:K5A_P}
\end{equation}
such that both
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P^\dagger \widehat Y_u P
\quad\text{and}\quad
P^\dagger \widehat Y_d P
}
\label{eq:K5A_realified_pair}
\end{equation}
are real symmetric matrices.
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{\mathrm{CKM}}=0,
\qquad
\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}=0.
}
\label{eq:K5A_common_real_nogo}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Any real symmetric matrix is diagonalized by a real orthogonal matrix.
Hence there exist \(O_u,O_d\in O(3)\) such that
\[
O_u^T (P^\dagger \widehat Y_u P) O_u=\text{diag},
\qquad
O_d^T (P^\dagger \widehat Y_d P) O_d=\text{diag}.
\]
Therefore one may choose
\[
U_u=P O_u,
\qquad
U_d=P O_d,
\]
so that
\[
V_{\mathrm{CKM}}=U_u^\dagger U_d = O_u^T O_d,
\]
which is real orthogonal.
A real CKM matrix has vanishing Jarlskog invariant, hence \(J_{\mathrm{CKM}}=0\).
Then \eqref{eq:K5A_J_factor} implies \(\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}=0\).
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
This is the exact no-go form of the statement:

\[
\boxed{
\text{if one common rephasing makes both sectors real, there is no physical CP phase.}
}
\]

So a merely “complex-looking” matrix is not enough.
The phase must survive \emph{common} family rephasing.

\section{5. Concrete common-phase-alignment criterion}

The common realification theorem becomes especially transparent in terms of matrix-entry phases.

Suppose that for \(f\in\{u,d\}\),
\[
(\widehat Y_f)_{ij}=|(\widehat Y_f)_{ij}|e^{i\varphi_{ij}^{(f)}}.
\]
Assume there exist numbers \(\alpha_1,\alpha_2,\alpha_3\) such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varphi_{ij}^{(u)}=\alpha_i-\alpha_j \pmod{\pi},
\qquad
\varphi_{ij}^{(d)}=\alpha_i-\alpha_j \pmod{\pi}
}
\label{eq:K5A_phase_alignment}
\end{equation}
for all \(i<j\).
Then the same diagonal rephasing \(P=\operatorname{diag}(e^{i\alpha_1},e^{i\alpha_2},e^{i\alpha_3})\) makes both matrices real symmetric.

Therefore \eqref{eq:K5A_phase_alignment} is a concrete sufficient no-go criterion for vanishing irreducible CP.

\paragraph{Meaning.}
A common phase-gradient structure on the three links
\[
12,\quad 23,\quad 13
\]
is \emph{not} enough.
To get physical CP, the phase structure must fail this common-gradient condition.

\section{6. Small-misalignment practical CP seed}

We now derive the practical leading seed in the \(K4A\) small-misalignment regime.

Recall
\[
V_{\mathrm{CKM}}=I+\Theta+\frac12\Theta^2+O(\epsilon^3),
\]
with
\[
\Theta=\Omega_d-\Omega_u,
\qquad
\Theta^\dagger=-\Theta.
\]
Also recall from \(K4A\) the effective remote channel
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Theta_{13}^{\mathrm{eff}}
:=
\Theta_{13}
+\frac12\,\omega_{12}^{(d)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}
+\frac12\,\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(u)}
-\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}.
}
\label{eq:K5A_theta13eff}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Leading practical CP seed]
In the aligned small-misalignment regime,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{\mathrm{CKM}}
=
\Im\!\bigl(
\Theta_{12}\Theta_{23}\overline{\Theta_{13}^{\mathrm{eff}}}
\bigr)
+
O(\epsilon^5).
}
\label{eq:K5A_J_leading}
\end{equation}
Consequently, the leading practical CP seed is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}
:=
\Im\!\bigl(
\Theta_{12}\Theta_{23}\overline{\Theta_{13}^{\mathrm{eff}}}
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:K5A_XiCP}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The CKM Jarlskog invariant may be written as
\[
J_{\mathrm{CKM}}=\Im(V_{12}V_{23}\overline{V_{13}}V_{22}^\ast).
\]
In the small-misalignment regime,
\[
V_{22}=1+O(\epsilon^2),
\qquad
V_{12}=\Theta_{12}+O(\epsilon^2),
\qquad
V_{23}=\Theta_{23}+O(\epsilon^2),
\]
and from \(K4A\),
\[
V_{13}=\Theta_{13}^{\mathrm{eff}}+O(\epsilon^3).
\]
Therefore
\[
J_{\mathrm{CKM}}
=
\Im\!\bigl(
(\Theta_{12}+O(\epsilon^2))
(\Theta_{23}+O(\epsilon^2))
(\overline{\Theta_{13}^{\mathrm{eff}}}+O(\epsilon^3))
(1+O(\epsilon^2))
\bigr).
\]
The leading term is precisely
\[
\Im\!\bigl(\Theta_{12}\Theta_{23}\overline{\Theta_{13}^{\mathrm{eff}}}\bigr),
\]
and the first omitted terms are \(O(\epsilon^5)\).
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Meaning.}
The practical CP seed is exactly the rephasing-invariant imaginary part of the three-link cycle:
\[
12 \to 23 \to 13.
\]

This is the small-misalignment version of the exact commutator invariant.

\section{7. Rephasing invariance of the practical seed}

Under a common family rephasing
\[
e_i\mapsto e^{i\alpha_i}e_i,
\]
the relative generators transform as
\[
\Theta_{ij}\mapsto e^{i(\alpha_j-\alpha_i)}\Theta_{ij},
\qquad
\Theta_{13}^{\mathrm{eff}}\mapsto e^{i(\alpha_3-\alpha_1)}\Theta_{13}^{\mathrm{eff}}.
\]
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Theta_{12}\Theta_{23}\overline{\Theta_{13}^{\mathrm{eff}}}
\mapsto
\Theta_{12}\Theta_{23}\overline{\Theta_{13}^{\mathrm{eff}}}.
}
\label{eq:K5A_cycle_invariant}
\end{equation}
So \(\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}\) is indeed a rephasing-invariant physical seed.

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
This explains why single-link or two-link complex phases are not enough.
Only the closed three-link phase cycle is physically meaningful.

\section{8. Immediate corollaries and no-go consequences}

The practical seed immediately yields sharp necessary conditions.

\begin{corollary}[Channel-absence no-go]
If any one of the three effective channels vanishes,
\begin{equation}
\Theta_{12}=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\Theta_{23}=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\Theta_{13}^{\mathrm{eff}}=0,
\label{eq:K5A_channel_absence}
\end{equation}
then
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}=0
\]
and there is no leading CP seed.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from the product formula \eqref{eq:K5A_XiCP}.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Common-phase no-go at leading order]
If
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\arg \Theta_{13}^{\mathrm{eff}}
=
\arg \Theta_{12}+\arg \Theta_{23}
\pmod{\pi},
}
\label{eq:K5A_phase_lock_nogo}
\end{equation}
then
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}=0.
\]
Hence no leading irreducible CP seed exists.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Under \eqref{eq:K5A_phase_lock_nogo}, the product
\[
\Theta_{12}\Theta_{23}\overline{\Theta_{13}^{\mathrm{eff}}}
\]
is real up to sign, so its imaginary part vanishes.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Meaning.}
So K5A needs more than nonzero complex entries.
It needs a genuine nontrivial phase area in the three-link cycle.

\section{9. What can generate nonzero \(\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}\)?}

The previous no-go theorems identify the minimal logical options.

A nonzero irreducible CP seed requires at least one of the following mechanisms:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{a second noncommuting spurion:}
\[
[\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d]\neq 0
\]
in a genuinely complex way, not merely through commuting diagonal splitting;

\item \textbf{genuine 3D geometric misalignment:}
the three channels \(12,23,13\) are not reducible to one common planar phase-gradient structure;

\item \textbf{intrinsically complex microscopic couplings:}
the literal blockwise extractions feeding \(\Theta_{ij}\) and \(\Theta_{13}^{\mathrm{eff}}\) carry a rephasing-invariant complex cycle.
\end{enumerate}

This is the precise mathematical content of the verbal statement
\[
\boxed{
\text{CP requires more than one real alignment direction.}
}
\]

\section{10. Integrated practical \(K5A\) theorem}

We may now state the full theorem.

\begin{theorem}[Integrated practical \(K5A\) theorem]
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(K2_{\mathrm{align}}\) has been accepted, so both sectors are represented in one common canonically normalized family basis;
\item \(K3A\) has supplied simple spectra for both sectors;
\item \(K4A\) has supplied the relative generators \(\Theta_{12},\Theta_{23},\Theta_{13}^{\mathrm{eff}}\).
\end{enumerate}

Then:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the exact irreducible CP criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}
=
\frac{1}{3i}\,\operatorname{tr}\!\bigl([\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d]^3\bigr)\neq 0;
}
\label{eq:K5A_exact_final}
\end{equation}

\item a practical leading-order CP seed criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}
=
\Im\!\bigl(
\Theta_{12}\Theta_{23}\overline{\Theta_{13}^{\mathrm{eff}}}
\bigr)\neq 0;
}
\label{eq:K5A_practical_final}
\end{equation}

\item if either
\[
[\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d]=0,
\]
or a common rephasing makes both \(\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d\) real symmetric,
then
\[
\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}=0,
\qquad
\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}=0,
\qquad
J_{\mathrm{CKM}}=0.
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Part (1) is the exact commutator theorem.
Part (2) is the leading practical seed theorem.
Part (3) follows from the two no-go theorems above.
\end{proof}

\section{11. \(K5A\) Acceptance Sheet}

The \(K5A\) audit is now finite and explicit.

\paragraph{Level 0: Basis admissibility.}
Verify \(K2_{\mathrm{align}}\) and simple spectra in both sectors.

\paragraph{Level 1: Exact CP-odd invariant.}
Compute
\[
\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}
=
\frac{1}{3i}\,\operatorname{tr}\!\bigl([\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d]^3\bigr).
\]
If
\[
\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}\neq 0,
\]
then exact irreducible CP seed is present.

\paragraph{Level 2: No-go screening.}
Check whether either of the following holds:
\begin{enumerate}
\item single-spurion / commuting structure:
\[
[\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d]=0;
\]
\item common realification:
there exists one diagonal phase matrix \(P\) such that both \(P^\dagger \widehat Y_u P\) and \(P^\dagger \widehat Y_d P\) are real symmetric.
\end{enumerate}
If either holds, reject \(K5A\).

\paragraph{Level 3: Practical leading seed.}
Compute
\[
\Theta_{12},\qquad
\Theta_{23},\qquad
\Theta_{13}^{\mathrm{eff}},
\]
and then
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}
=
\Im\!\bigl(
\Theta_{12}\Theta_{23}\overline{\Theta_{13}^{\mathrm{eff}}}
\bigr).
\]
If
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}\neq 0
\]
with margin larger than the higher-order truncation error, accept practical \(K5A\).

\paragraph{Level 4: Program-level interpretation.}
Passing Level 1 means:
\[
\boxed{
\text{exact irreducible CP seed exists.}
}
\]
Passing Level 3 means:
\[
\boxed{
\text{a practical leading CKM CP seed is already present.}
}
\]

\section{Honest Status}

The structural status of \(K5A\) is now:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K5A\text{ is reduced to an exact commutator invariant plus a practical three-link phase-cycle audit.}
}
\end{equation}

What remains microscopically is only the explicit intended-branch evaluation of
\[
\widehat Y_u,\qquad \widehat Y_d,
\qquad \Theta_{12},\qquad \Theta_{23},\qquad \Theta_{13}^{\mathrm{eff}}.
\]

Therefore the honest statement is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Structural status of }K5A:\ \text{closed at exact/practical invariant level.}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Microscopic acceptance status of }K5A:\ \text{conditional until the finite invariant audit is executed.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

Irreducible CKM CP violation is controlled exactly by the rephasing-invariant commutator invariant
\[
\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}
=
\frac{1}{3i}\,\operatorname{tr}\!\bigl([\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d]^3\bigr).
\]
In the nondegenerate regime,
\[
\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}\neq 0
\iff
J_{\mathrm{CKM}}\neq 0.
\]

There are two fundamental no-go mechanisms:

\begin{enumerate}
\item if both sectors come from a single common spurion, or more generally if
\[
[\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d]=0,
\]
then no irreducible CP phase exists;

\item if one common family rephasing makes both sectors real symmetric, then the CKM matrix becomes real orthogonal, so again no irreducible CP phase exists.
\end{enumerate}

In the small-misalignment practical regime, the leading CP seed is the three-link cycle invariant
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}
=
\Im\!\bigl(
\Theta_{12}\Theta_{23}\overline{\Theta_{13}^{\mathrm{eff}}}
\bigr),
\]
where
\[
\Theta_{13}^{\mathrm{eff}}
=
\Theta_{13}
+\frac12\,\omega_{12}^{(d)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}
+\frac12\,\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(u)}
-\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}.
\]

Therefore \(K5A\) is fully reduced to a finite exact/practical CP-invariant audit.

\section*{K5A Final Summary}

The exact irreducible CKM CP seed is controlled by the commutator invariant
\[
\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}
=
\frac{1}{3i}\,\operatorname{tr}\!\bigl([\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d]^3\bigr).
\]
In the nondegenerate regime,
\[
\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}\neq 0
\iff
J_{\mathrm{CKM}}\neq 0.
\]

Hence the exact \(K5A\) criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}\neq 0.
}
\]

There are two exact no-go mechanisms:

\[
[\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d]=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}=0,
\]
and
\[
\exists\,P\ \text{diagonal phase matrix such that}\ 
P^\dagger \widehat Y_u P,\ P^\dagger \widehat Y_d P
\ \text{are both real symmetric}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
J_{\mathrm{CKM}}=0.
\]

In the small-misalignment practical regime, the leading CP seed is the rephasing-invariant three-link cycle
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}
=
\Im\!\bigl(
\Theta_{12}\Theta_{23}\overline{\Theta_{13}^{\mathrm{eff}}}
\bigr),
\]
with
\[
\Theta_{13}^{\mathrm{eff}}
=
\Theta_{13}
+\frac12\,\omega_{12}^{(d)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}
+\frac12\,\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(u)}
-\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}.
\]

Thus the practical \(K5A\) seed criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}\neq 0.
}
\]

Therefore \(K5A\) is fully reduced to a finite exact/practical CP-invariant audit.

\section{K5B: Microscopic Blockwise Mechanisms for a Nonzero Irreducible CP Seed}

\section{Goal}

At \(K5A\), the exact and practical CP criteria were isolated as
\[
\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}
=
\frac{1}{3i}\operatorname{tr}\!\bigl([\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d]^3\bigr),
\qquad
\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}
=
\Im\!\bigl(
\Theta_{12}\Theta_{23}\overline{\Theta_{13}^{\mathrm{eff}}}
\bigr).
\]

The purpose of \(K5B\) is now to rewrite the practical seed \(\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}\) directly in terms of the microscopic blockwise data:
\[
\Lambda_{12}^{(u,d)},\ \Lambda_{23}^{(u,d)},\ \Lambda_{13}^{(u,d)},
\qquad
\Delta_{12}^{(u,d)},\ \Delta_{23}^{(u,d)},\ \Delta_{13}^{(u,d)},
\]
together with the controlled residual corrections.

Equivalently, we now ask:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{which microscopic mechanism forces }\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}\neq 0?
}
\end{equation}

\section{1. Gap-normalized microscopic link variables}

Recall from \(K3C\) and \(K4A\) that
\[
\omega_{ij}^{(f)}=\frac{w_{ij}^{(f)}}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}},
\qquad
w_{ij}^{(f)}=\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}+r_{ij}^{(f)},
\qquad
f\in\{u,d\}.
\]

Define the exact gap-normalized literal block seeds
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{ij}^{(f)}
:=
\frac{\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}},
\qquad
\varepsilon_{ij}^{(f)}
:=
\frac{r_{ij}^{(f)}}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}}.
}
\label{eq:K5B_lambda_eps}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\omega_{ij}^{(f)}=\lambda_{ij}^{(f)}+\varepsilon_{ij}^{(f)}.
}
\label{eq:K5B_omega_split}
\end{equation}

Thus the microscopic family problem has now been reduced to:
\begin{itemize}
\item diagonal gap data \(\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}\), coming from the \(OO\)-anisotropy sector;
\item literal off-diagonal blockwise data \(\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}\), coming from the \(TD/DT\) sector;
\item normalized residual corrections \(\varepsilon_{ij}^{(f)}\).
\end{itemize}

\section{2. Relative direct microscopic seeds}

Define the direct inter-sector microscopic link mismatches
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_{ij}
:=
\lambda_{ij}^{(d)}-\lambda_{ij}^{(u)},
\qquad
E_{ij}
:=
\varepsilon_{ij}^{(d)}-\varepsilon_{ij}^{(u)}.
}
\label{eq:K5B_Sij_Eij}
\end{equation}

Then the relative first-order generators satisfy
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Theta_{ij}=S_{ij}+E_{ij}.
}
\label{eq:K5B_Theta_SE}
\end{equation}

So the direct CP-relevant relative links are already finite ratio-differences:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_{12}
=
\frac{\Lambda_{12}^{(d)}}{\Delta_{12}^{(d)}}
-
\frac{\Lambda_{12}^{(u)}}{\Delta_{12}^{(u)}},
}
\label{eq:K5B_S12}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_{23}
=
\frac{\Lambda_{23}^{(d)}}{\Delta_{23}^{(d)}}
-
\frac{\Lambda_{23}^{(u)}}{\Delta_{23}^{(u)}},
}
\label{eq:K5B_S23}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_{13}
=
\frac{\Lambda_{13}^{(d)}}{\Delta_{13}^{(d)}}
-
\frac{\Lambda_{13}^{(u)}}{\Delta_{13}^{(u)}}.
}
\label{eq:K5B_S13}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Microscopic chain-generated remote seed}

From \(K4A\), the effective remote channel is
\[
\Theta_{13}^{\mathrm{eff}}
=
\Theta_{13}
+\frac12\,\omega_{12}^{(d)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}
+\frac12\,\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(u)}
-\omega_{12}^{(u)}\omega_{23}^{(d)}.
\]

Substitute \(\omega=\lambda+\varepsilon\).
Define the literal microscopic chain core
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_{\mathrm{mic}}
:=
\frac12\,\lambda_{12}^{(d)}\lambda_{23}^{(d)}
+\frac12\,\lambda_{12}^{(u)}\lambda_{23}^{(u)}
-\lambda_{12}^{(u)}\lambda_{23}^{(d)}.
}
\label{eq:K5B_Cmic}
\end{equation}

Define also the chain error term \(C_{\mathrm{err}}\) by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Theta_{13}^{\mathrm{eff}}
=
S_{13}
+
C_{\mathrm{mic}}
+
\widetilde E_{13},
\qquad
\widetilde E_{13}:=E_{13}+C_{\mathrm{err}},
}
\label{eq:K5B_Theta13eff_split}
\end{equation}
where explicitly
\begin{align}
C_{\mathrm{err}}
&=
\frac12\bigl(
\lambda_{12}^{(d)}\varepsilon_{23}^{(d)}
+\varepsilon_{12}^{(d)}\lambda_{23}^{(d)}
+\varepsilon_{12}^{(d)}\varepsilon_{23}^{(d)}
\bigr)
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+\frac12\bigl(
\lambda_{12}^{(u)}\varepsilon_{23}^{(u)}
+\varepsilon_{12}^{(u)}\lambda_{23}^{(u)}
+\varepsilon_{12}^{(u)}\varepsilon_{23}^{(u)}
\bigr)
\nonumber\\
&\quad
-\bigl(
\lambda_{12}^{(u)}\varepsilon_{23}^{(d)}
+\varepsilon_{12}^{(u)}\lambda_{23}^{(d)}
+\varepsilon_{12}^{(u)}\varepsilon_{23}^{(d)}
\bigr).
\label{eq:K5B_Cerr}
\end{align}

Thus the effective remote channel is the sum of:
\begin{enumerate}
\item a direct relative \(13\)-mismatch \(S_{13}\),
\item a literal chain-generated microscopic core \(C_{\mathrm{mic}}\),
\item a controlled correction \(\widetilde E_{13}\).
\end{enumerate}

\section{4. Leading microscopic CP core}

Substituting the decompositions above into \(K5A\), the practical CP seed becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}
=
\Im\!\Bigl(
(S_{12}+E_{12})(S_{23}+E_{23})
\overline{(S_{13}+C_{\mathrm{mic}}+\widetilde E_{13})}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:K5B_Xi_full}
\end{equation}

Define the leading microscopic CP core
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}
:=
\Im\!\Bigl(
S_{12}S_{23}\overline{(S_{13}+C_{\mathrm{mic}})}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:K5B_Ximic}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Leading microscopic CP core plus controlled error]
Let
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M:=\max\bigl(
|S_{12}|,\ |S_{23}|,\ |S_{13}+C_{\mathrm{mic}}|
\bigr),
\qquad
\varepsilon:=\max\bigl(
|E_{12}|,\ |E_{23}|,\ |\widetilde E_{13}|
\bigr).
}
\label{eq:K5B_Meps}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}-\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}|
\le
3M^2\varepsilon+3M\varepsilon^2+\varepsilon^3.
}
\label{eq:K5B_error_bound}
\end{equation}

Consequently, if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}|
>
3M^2\varepsilon+3M\varepsilon^2+\varepsilon^3,
}
\label{eq:K5B_margin_condition}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:K5B_practical_accept}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Expand
\[
(S_{12}+E_{12})(S_{23}+E_{23})\overline{(S_{13}+C_{\mathrm{mic}}+\widetilde E_{13})}
-
S_{12}S_{23}\overline{(S_{13}+C_{\mathrm{mic}})}
\]
into the seven nontrivial correction monomials:
\begin{align*}
& S_{12}S_{23}\overline{\widetilde E_{13}}
+S_{12}E_{23}\overline{(S_{13}+C_{\mathrm{mic}})}
+E_{12}S_{23}\overline{(S_{13}+C_{\mathrm{mic}})}\\
&\quad
+S_{12}E_{23}\overline{\widetilde E_{13}}
+E_{12}S_{23}\overline{\widetilde E_{13}}
+E_{12}E_{23}\overline{(S_{13}+C_{\mathrm{mic}})}
+E_{12}E_{23}\overline{\widetilde E_{13}}.
\end{align*}
Taking absolute values gives
\[
|\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}-\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}|
\le
M^2\varepsilon+M^2\varepsilon+M^2\varepsilon
+M\varepsilon^2+M\varepsilon^2+M\varepsilon^2+\varepsilon^3,
\]
which is exactly \eqref{eq:K5B_error_bound}. The implication \eqref{eq:K5B_practical_accept} is immediate.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Meaning.}
This is the practical microscopic acceptance theorem:
to prove \(\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}\neq 0\), it is enough to prove that the leading microscopic core \(\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}\) dominates the controlled residual budget.

\section{5. Amplitude--phase form of the microscopic core}

Write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_{12}=A_{12}e^{i\phi_{12}},
\qquad
S_{23}=A_{23}e^{i\phi_{23}},
\qquad
S_{13}+C_{\mathrm{mic}}=A_{13}^{\mathrm{mic}}e^{i\phi_{13}},
}
\label{eq:K5B_amp_phase}
\end{equation}
with
\[
A_{12},A_{23},A_{13}^{\mathrm{mic}}\ge 0.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
A_{12}A_{23}A_{13}^{\mathrm{mic}}
\sin(\phi_{12}+\phi_{23}-\phi_{13}).
}
\label{eq:K5B_Ximic_phase}
\end{equation}

\begin{corollary}[Microscopic phase-area criterion]
The leading microscopic CP core is nonzero if and only if:
\begin{enumerate}
\item
\[
A_{12}>0,\qquad A_{23}>0,\qquad A_{13}^{\mathrm{mic}}>0,
\]
and
\item
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\phi_{12}+\phi_{23}-\phi_{13}\not\equiv 0 \pmod{\pi}.
}
\label{eq:K5B_phase_area}
\end{equation}
\end{enumerate}
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from \eqref{eq:K5B_Ximic_phase}.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Meaning.}
This is the exact microscopic content of the phrase
\[
\boxed{
\text{nonzero CP requires a nontrivial three-link phase area.}
}
\]
All three effective links must be present, and their phase cycle must not collapse to a straight line.

\section{6. Microscopic no-go theorem in block language}

We now rewrite the \(K5A\) no-go directly in terms of the blockwise normalized links.

\begin{theorem}[Common-gradient no-go in microscopic block language]
Assume there exist phases \(\alpha_1,\alpha_2,\alpha_3\) and real numbers
\[
\ell_{ij}^{(u)},\ \ell_{ij}^{(d)}\in\mathbb R
\]
such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{ij}^{(u)}=e^{i(\alpha_j-\alpha_i)}\ell_{ij}^{(u)},
\qquad
\lambda_{ij}^{(d)}=e^{i(\alpha_j-\alpha_i)}\ell_{ij}^{(d)}
}
\label{eq:K5B_common_gradient}
\end{equation}
for all \(i<j\).
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}=0.
}
\label{eq:K5B_common_gradient_nogo}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Under \eqref{eq:K5B_common_gradient},
\[
S_{12}=e^{i(\alpha_2-\alpha_1)} s_{12},
\qquad
S_{23}=e^{i(\alpha_3-\alpha_2)} s_{23},
\qquad
S_{13}=e^{i(\alpha_3-\alpha_1)} s_{13},
\]
with real \(s_{ij}\).
Also,
\[
C_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
e^{i(\alpha_3-\alpha_1)}c_{\mathrm{mic}},
\]
with \(c_{\mathrm{mic}}\in\mathbb R\), because every term in \eqref{eq:K5B_Cmic} carries the same total phase \(e^{i(\alpha_3-\alpha_1)}\).
Therefore
\[
S_{12}S_{23}\overline{(S_{13}+C_{\mathrm{mic}})}
=
e^{i(\alpha_2-\alpha_1)}e^{i(\alpha_3-\alpha_2)}e^{-i(\alpha_3-\alpha_1)}
\,s_{12}s_{23}(s_{13}+c_{\mathrm{mic}})
=
s_{12}s_{23}(s_{13}+c_{\mathrm{mic}})\in\mathbb R.
\]
Hence \(\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}=0\).
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
This is the fully microscopic blockwise no-go theorem:
if all normalized links in both sectors share one common phase-gradient structure, then the CP cycle collapses and no irreducible seed remains.

\section{7. Three distinct microscopic mechanisms for nonzero CP}

The blockwise formulas isolate three qualitatively different mechanisms.

\subsection{Mechanism I: direct relative-link cycle}

If the chain term is negligible,
\[
|C_{\mathrm{mic}}|\ll |S_{13}|,
\]
then the leading core reduces to
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}
\approx
\Im(S_{12}S_{23}\overline{S_{13}}).
\]
So irreducible CP is generated directly by the three relative link mismatches
\[
S_{12},\qquad S_{23},\qquad S_{13}.
\]

\subsection{Mechanism II: chain-generated CP without direct remote mismatch}

If
\[
S_{13}=0
\]
but
\[
C_{\mathrm{mic}}\neq 0,
\]
then
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
\Im(S_{12}S_{23}\overline{C_{\mathrm{mic}}}).
\]
Thus a nonzero CP seed can be generated even in the absence of a direct \(13\)-mismatch, purely through the inter-sector chain structure.

\subsection{Mechanism III: direct--chain interference}

If both \(S_{13}\) and \(C_{\mathrm{mic}}\) are nonzero, then
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
\Im(S_{12}S_{23}\overline{S_{13}})
+
\Im(S_{12}S_{23}\overline{C_{\mathrm{mic}}}),
\]
so the physical CP seed arises from the interference between the direct remote mismatch and the chain-generated remote seed.

\paragraph{Meaning.}
This is the microscopic refinement of \(K5A\):
a nonzero CP invariant can come from a direct remote complex link, from a purely chain-generated remote phase, or from their interference.

\section{8. Integrated practical \(K5B\) theorem}

We may now state the practical theorem.

\begin{theorem}[Integrated practical \(K5B\) theorem]
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(K2_{\mathrm{align}}\), \(K3A\), and \(K4A\) have been accepted;
\item the literal blockwise data
\[
\Lambda_{ij}^{(u,d)},\qquad \Delta_{ij}^{(u,d)}
\]
have been extracted, together with residual corrections \(r_{ij}^{(u,d)}\);
\item the normalized variables \(\lambda_{ij}^{(f)}\), \(\varepsilon_{ij}^{(f)}\), \(S_{ij}\), \(E_{ij}\), and \(C_{\mathrm{mic}}\) are built as above.
\end{enumerate}

Then:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the practical CP seed decomposes as
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}
=
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}
+
\text{controlled error},
\]
with
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
\Im\!\Bigl(
S_{12}S_{23}\overline{(S_{13}+C_{\mathrm{mic}})}
\Bigr);
\]

\item the deviation from the microscopic core obeys
\[
|\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}-\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}|
\le
3M^2\varepsilon+3M\varepsilon^2+\varepsilon^3;
\]

\item therefore a sufficient practical acceptance condition is
\[
|\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}|
>
3M^2\varepsilon+3M\varepsilon^2+\varepsilon^3;
\]

\item if all normalized links in both sectors share a common phase-gradient structure \eqref{eq:K5B_common_gradient}, then
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}=0,
\]
so no leading microscopic irreducible CP seed exists.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from the exact decomposition, the error theorem, and the common-gradient no-go theorem.
\end{proof}

\section{9. \(K5B\) Acceptance Sheet}

The \(K5B\) audit is now finite and literal.

\paragraph{Level 0: Microscopic input extraction.}
Compute
\[
\Lambda_{12}^{(u,d)},\ \Lambda_{23}^{(u,d)},\ \Lambda_{13}^{(u,d)},
\qquad
\Delta_{12}^{(u,d)},\ \Delta_{23}^{(u,d)},\ \Delta_{13}^{(u,d)},
\]
and the residuals
\[
r_{12}^{(u,d)},\ r_{23}^{(u,d)},\ r_{13}^{(u,d)}.
\]

\paragraph{Level 1: Normalized microscopic links.}
Compute
\[
\lambda_{ij}^{(f)}=\frac{\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}},
\qquad
\varepsilon_{ij}^{(f)}=\frac{r_{ij}^{(f)}}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}}.
\]

\paragraph{Level 2: Relative links and chain core.}
Compute
\[
S_{ij}=\lambda_{ij}^{(d)}-\lambda_{ij}^{(u)},
\]
and
\[
C_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
\frac12\,\lambda_{12}^{(d)}\lambda_{23}^{(d)}
+\frac12\,\lambda_{12}^{(u)}\lambda_{23}^{(u)}
-\lambda_{12}^{(u)}\lambda_{23}^{(d)}.
\]

\paragraph{Level 3: Leading microscopic CP core.}
Compute
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
\Im\!\Bigl(
S_{12}S_{23}\overline{(S_{13}+C_{\mathrm{mic}})}
\Bigr).
\]

\paragraph{Level 4: Error budget.}
Compute
\[
M=\max\bigl(|S_{12}|,|S_{23}|,|S_{13}+C_{\mathrm{mic}}|\bigr),
\qquad
\varepsilon=\max\bigl(|E_{12}|,|E_{23}|,|\widetilde E_{13}|\bigr),
\]
and verify
\[
|\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}|
>
3M^2\varepsilon+3M\varepsilon^2+\varepsilon^3.
\]

\paragraph{Level 5: No-go screen.}
Check whether the common-gradient condition \eqref{eq:K5B_common_gradient} holds.
If it does, reject \(K5B\).

\paragraph{Level 6: Program-level interpretation.}
Passing the above means:
\[
\boxed{
\text{a genuine microscopic mechanism forcing }\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}\neq 0\text{ has been identified.}
}
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The practical CP seed can be rewritten directly in microscopic blockwise language by introducing the normalized links
\[
\lambda_{ij}^{(f)}=\frac{\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}},
\qquad
\varepsilon_{ij}^{(f)}=\frac{r_{ij}^{(f)}}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}}.
\]
The direct relative microscopic links are
\[
S_{ij}=\lambda_{ij}^{(d)}-\lambda_{ij}^{(u)},
\]
and the literal chain-generated remote core is
\[
C_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
\frac12\,\lambda_{12}^{(d)}\lambda_{23}^{(d)}
+\frac12\,\lambda_{12}^{(u)}\lambda_{23}^{(u)}
-\lambda_{12}^{(u)}\lambda_{23}^{(d)}.
\]

The leading microscopic CP core is
\[
\boxed{
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
\Im\!\Bigl(
S_{12}S_{23}\overline{(S_{13}+C_{\mathrm{mic}})}
\Bigr).
}
\]

This can be written as
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
A_{12}A_{23}A_{13}^{\mathrm{mic}}
\sin(\phi_{12}+\phi_{23}-\phi_{13}),
\]
so nonzero CP requires:
\[
A_{12}>0,\qquad
A_{23}>0,\qquad
A_{13}^{\mathrm{mic}}>0,
\qquad
\phi_{12}+\phi_{23}-\phi_{13}\not\equiv 0 \pmod{\pi}.
\]

The full practical seed differs from \(\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}\) by a controlled error:
\[
|\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}-\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}|
\le
3M^2\varepsilon+3M\varepsilon^2+\varepsilon^3.
\]
Hence a sufficient practical acceptance condition is
\[
|\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}|
>
3M^2\varepsilon+3M\varepsilon^2+\varepsilon^3.
\]

There is also a sharp microscopic no-go:
if all normalized links in both sectors share one common phase-gradient structure, then
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}=0.
\]

Therefore \(K5B\) is fully reduced to a finite microscopic cycle-versus-error audit.

Introduce the normalized microscopic block data

\section{K5C: Stability and Open-Set Robustness of the Microscopic CP Seed}

\section{Goal}

At \(K5B\), the irreducible CP seed has been reduced to the finite microscopic quantity
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
\Im\!\Bigl(
S_{12}S_{23}\overline{(S_{13}+C_{\mathrm{mic}})}
\Bigr).
\]

The final question is not existence, but robustness:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{does }\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}\neq 0\text{ hold on an open region of microscopic parameter space?}
}
\end{equation}

\section{1. Parameter space and regularity}

Let the microscopic parameter vector be
\[
p
:=
(\Lambda_{ij}^{(u,d)},\ \Delta_{ij}^{(u,d)},\ r_{ij}^{(u,d)}).
\]

Then
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}(p),\qquad
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}(p)
\]
are smooth (real-analytic) functions of \(p\) as long as
\[
\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}\neq 0.
\]

Define the admissible domain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal{D}
:=
\{p:\ \Delta_{ij}^{(f)}\neq 0\ \forall i<j,\ f=u,d\}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Error-controlled reduction}

From \(K5B\),
\[
|\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}-\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}|
\le
E(p),
\]
where
\[
E(p)
=
3M^2\varepsilon+3M\varepsilon^2+\varepsilon^3.
\]

\begin{theorem}[Error-dominated stability]
If at some point \(p_0\in\mathcal{D}\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}(p_0)| > E(p_0),
}
\end{equation}
then there exists a neighborhood \(U\ni p_0\) such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}(p)\neq 0\quad\forall p\in U.
}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By continuity of \(\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}\) and \(E\), there exists \(U\) such that
\[
|\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}(p)| > E(p)
\quad\forall p\in U.
\]
Then
\[
|\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}(p)|
\ge
|\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}(p)|-E(p)
>0.
\]
\end{proof}

\section{3. Transversality and open-set nonvanishing}

Define the zero-locus
\[
Z
:=
\{p\in\mathcal{D}:\ \Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}(p)=0\}.
\]

\begin{theorem}[Generic transversality]
If at \(p_0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}(p_0)\neq 0,
}
\end{equation}
then there exists an open neighborhood \(U\) such that
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}(p)\neq 0\quad\forall p\in U.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\(\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}\) is continuous.
Hence nonvanishing is an open condition.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Measure-zero obstruction]
Assume \(\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}\) is not identically zero.
Then its zero set \(Z\) is a closed set of codimension at least one, hence of measure zero.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\(\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}\) is a real-analytic function on \(\mathcal{D}\).
If it is not identically zero, its zero-locus is a proper analytic subset, hence of measure zero.
\end{proof}

\section{4. Phase-area stability formulation}

Recall
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
A_{12}A_{23}A_{13}^{\mathrm{mic}}
\sin(\Phi),
\quad
\Phi:=\phi_{12}+\phi_{23}-\phi_{13}.
\]

\begin{theorem}[Phase-margin stability]
If at \(p_0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{12},A_{23},A_{13}^{\mathrm{mic}} > 0,
\qquad
|\sin\Phi(p_0)|>\delta>0,
}
\end{equation}
then there exists \(U\ni p_0\) such that
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}(p)\neq 0\quad\forall p\in U.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
All amplitudes and phases are continuous.
Thus the strict inequalities persist under small perturbations.
\end{proof}

\section{5. Structural interpretation}

We obtain the final structural statement:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{irreducible CP is a stable open-set phenomenon, not a fine-tuned point.}
}
\end{equation}

The only ways to destroy CP are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item collapse of one channel:
\[
A_{12}=0\ \text{or}\ A_{23}=0\ \text{or}\ A_{13}^{\mathrm{mic}}=0;
\]
\item phase collapse:
\[
\Phi\equiv 0\pmod{\pi};
\]
\item error domination:
\[
|\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}|\le E.
\]
\end{enumerate}

All three define lower-dimensional subsets of parameter space.

\section{6. Integrated K5 closure}

Combining \(K5A\), \(K5B\), and \(K5C\):

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Exact CP criterion: }
\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}\neq 0
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Microscopic mechanism: }
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}\neq 0
}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Stability: }
|\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}|>E
\Rightarrow
\text{open-set robustness}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The irreducible CP seed in TECT reduces to a finite microscopic invariant
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
\Im\!\Bigl(
S_{12}S_{23}\overline{(S_{13}+C_{\mathrm{mic}})}
\Bigr),
\]
with controlled error.

If
\[
|\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}|>E,
\]
then \(\Xi_{\mathrm{CP}}\neq 0\) holds on an open neighborhood.

Thus CP violation is not a fine-tuned artifact, but a structurally stable feature of the microscopic parameter space, except on measure-zero degeneracy loci.
