\section{TECT Flavor Program: Structural Closure, Exact CKM Reduction, and the Final Microscopic Audit}

\section{Introduction}

The purpose of this section is to state, in theorem--proof form, what has been structurally established in the TECT flavor program, what remains conditional, and how the CKM problem is reduced to a finite executable microscopic audit.

The central point is the following.

The TECT flavor problem is \emph{not} left as an infinite-dimensional nonperturbative mystery.
It has been reduced to two finite routes:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d)
\longrightarrow
J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{exact}},
}
\label{eq:prx_exact_route}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Lambda,\Delta,r)
\longrightarrow
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}
\longrightarrow
J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{pred}}.
}
\label{eq:prx_mic_route}
\end{equation}

The correct final statement is therefore two-layered:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Structural flavor closure: achieved.}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Microscopic first-principles closure on the actual intended branch: reduced to a finite audit, but not yet universally executed.}
}
\end{equation}

This distinction is essential for an honest PRX-level presentation.

\section{Setup}

Let \(P_L\) denote the projector onto the intended common left-handed family space, and let
\begin{equation}
\widetilde\psi_a:=P_L\psi_a,
\qquad
a=1,2,3.
\end{equation}
Define the projected Gram matrix
\begin{equation}
S_{ab}:=\langle \widetilde\psi_a,\widetilde\psi_b\rangle,
\end{equation}
the projected kinetic matrices
\begin{equation}
M^{(f)}_{ab}:=\langle \widetilde\psi_a,\mathcal K_f\widetilde\psi_b\rangle,
\qquad
f\in\{u,d\},
\end{equation}
and the projected family operators
\begin{equation}
N^{(f)}_{ab}:=\langle \widetilde\psi_a,\mathcal Y_f\widetilde\psi_b\rangle.
\end{equation}

Whenever \(S>0\), define the canonically normalized family matrices
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z^{(f)}=S^{-1/2}M^{(f)}S^{-1/2},
\qquad
\widehat Y^{(f)}=S^{-1/2}N^{(f)}S^{-1/2}.
}
\label{eq:canonical_family_matrices}
\end{equation}

These objects are the finite family-level input of the entire CKM program.

\section{Theorem I: Exact Finite Reduction of the CKM Problem}

\begin{theorem}[Exact family reduction]
Assume that:
\begin{enumerate}
\item a common rank-three left-handed family space has been isolated;
\item the projected Gram matrix \(S\) is positive definite;
\item the sectoral kinetic matrices \(M^{(u)},M^{(d)}\) are Hermitian and positive after canonical normalization;
\item the sectoral family operators \(N^{(u)},N^{(d)}\) are Hermitian on the family space.
\end{enumerate}
Then the entire CKM problem is reduced to the finite pair of Hermitian \(3\times 3\) matrices
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat Y_u,\qquad \widehat Y_d.
}
\end{equation}
In particular, all flavor observables, including the CKM matrix and the Jarlskog invariant, are determined by the diagonalizers of \(\widehat Y_u\) and \(\widehat Y_d\).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The kinetic normalization step produces a common finite family space endowed with the sectoral positive metrics \(Z^{(u)},Z^{(d)}\). After canonical normalization, the projected family operators become \(\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d\), both Hermitian on a finite-dimensional space. The up- and down-sector diagonalizers
\[
U_u^\dagger \widehat Y_u U_u=\operatorname{diag}(y_1^{(u)},y_2^{(u)},y_3^{(u)}),
\qquad
U_d^\dagger \widehat Y_d U_d=\operatorname{diag}(y_1^{(d)},y_2^{(d)},y_3^{(d)})
\]
determine the physical CKM matrix
\[
V_{\mathrm{CKM}}=U_u^\dagger U_d.
\]
Thus the original infinite-dimensional problem is reduced to a finite matrix problem.
\end{proof}

\section{Theorem II: Exact CKM CP Invariant}

\begin{theorem}[Exact Jarlskog extraction]
Assume \(\widehat Y_u\) and \(\widehat Y_d\) have simple spectra. Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}
:=
\frac{1}{3i}\operatorname{tr}\!\bigl([\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d]^3\bigr).
}
\label{eq:Jexact_def}
\end{equation}
Define also the Vandermonde products
\begin{equation}
\mathcal V_u:=\prod_{1\le i<j\le 3}(y_i^{(u)}-y_j^{(u)}),
\qquad
\mathcal V_d:=\prod_{1\le i<j\le 3}(y_i^{(d)}-y_j^{(d)}).
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{\mathrm{CKM}}
=
\frac{\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}}{2\mathcal V_u\mathcal V_d}.
}
\label{eq:exact_jarlskog_prx}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}\neq 0
\iff
J_{\mathrm{CKM}}\neq 0.
}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
For a pair of Hermitian \(3\times 3\) matrices with simple spectra, the standard Jarlskog identity gives
\[
\det([\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d])
=
2i\,J_{\mathrm{CKM}}\,
\mathcal V_u\mathcal V_d.
\]
Since the commutator is traceless \(3\times3\),
\[
\operatorname{tr}(C^3)=3\det(C),
\qquad C=[\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d].
\]
Therefore
\[
\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}
=
\frac{1}{3i}\operatorname{tr}(C^3)
=
\frac{1}{i}\det(C)
=
2J_{\mathrm{CKM}}\mathcal V_u\mathcal V_d,
\]
which immediately yields \eqref{eq:exact_jarlskog_prx}.
\end{proof}

\section{Theorem III: Microscopic Link Reduction}

The finite family matrices are not the only useful route.
One may also write the late-stage flavor data in blockwise microscopic form.

Let
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}
\end{equation}
denote the literal \(TD/DT\)-sector off-diagonal links,
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}
\end{equation}
the sectoral diagonal gaps,
and
\begin{equation}
r_{ij}^{(f)}
\end{equation}
the residual corrections.

Define the normalized links
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_{ij}^{(f)}:=\frac{\Lambda_{ij}^{(f)}+r_{ij}^{(f)}}{\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}}.
}
\label{eq:Lij_def}
\end{equation}
Define the direct relative links
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_{ij}:=L_{ij}^{(d)}-L_{ij}^{(u)}.
}
\label{eq:Sij_def}
\end{equation}
Define the chain-generated remote term
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
\frac12\,L_{12}^{(d)}L_{23}^{(d)}
+
\frac12\,L_{12}^{(u)}L_{23}^{(u)}
-
L_{12}^{(u)}L_{23}^{(d)}.
}
\label{eq:Cmic_def_prx}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Microscopic CP predictor]
The late-stage microscopic CKM CP predictor is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
\Im\!\Bigl(
S_{12}S_{23}\overline{(S_{13}+C_{\mathrm{mic}})}
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:Xi_mic_prx}
\end{equation}
Moreover, this quantity is manifestly rephasing invariant.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The adjacent sectoral misalignment channels are encoded in the relative links \(S_{12}\) and \(S_{23}\), while the remote channel is the sum of the direct relative link \(S_{13}\) and the chain term \(C_{\mathrm{mic}}\). The only rephasing-invariant cubic combination carrying an imaginary part is the three-link cycle
\[
S_{12}S_{23}\overline{(S_{13}+C_{\mathrm{mic}})}.
\]
Taking its imaginary part gives \eqref{eq:Xi_mic_prx}. Under diagonal family rephasing, the three phases cancel around the cycle, so the quantity is invariant.
\end{proof}

\section{Theorem IV: Actual Defect-Profile Overlap Formula}

Now insert the explicit kink profile
\begin{equation}
\theta(\xi)=\theta_0\tanh(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
\theta'(\xi)=\theta_0\kappa\,\sech^2(\kappa\xi),
\end{equation}
and the localized envelope
\begin{equation}
\chi_f(\xi)=\mathcal N_f\,\sech^{\nu_f}(\kappa\xi),
\qquad
\mathcal N_f^2=\frac{\kappa}{B(\tfrac12,\nu_f)}.
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Literal overlap integral]
Within the kink working ansatz, the microscopic off-diagonal links are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_{AB}^{(f)}
=
\mathcal C_{AB}^{(f)}
\mathcal G_{AB}^{(f)}
\theta_0\mathcal N_f^2
\mathcal J_{\nu_f}(s_{AB}),
}
\label{eq:literal_overlap_integral_prx}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal J_{\nu}(s)
=
\int_{-\infty}^{\infty}
du\,
\sech^\nu(u-\tfrac{s}{2})\sech^2(u)\sech^\nu(u+\tfrac{s}{2}),
}
\label{eq:Jnu_prx}
\end{equation}
and
\[
s_{AB}=\kappa R_{AB}.
\]
In the large-separation regime,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_{AB}^{(f)}
=
\mathcal A_{AB}^{(f)}
\exp\!\left[
-\nu_f\kappa R_{AB}
-\frac{1}{4\sigma_f^2}(X_{A,\perp}-X_{B,\perp})^T G_\perp (X_{A,\perp}-X_{B,\perp})
\right]
\Bigl[1+O(e^{-2\kappa R_{AB}})\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:overlap_asymptotic_prx}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The reduced \(TD/DT\) kernel contains one factor of \(\theta'(\xi)\), and the localized mode ansatz factorizes into a normal envelope, a transverse Gaussian, and an internal vector. The transverse integral produces \(\mathcal G_{AB}^{(f)}\), the internal contraction produces \(\mathcal C_{AB}^{(f)}\), and the normal-direction integral produces \(\mathcal J_{\nu_f}(s_{AB})\). The large-separation asymptotic follows by localizing the integral near the defect core and extracting the exponential tails of the two shifted \(\sech^{\nu_f}\) profiles.
\end{proof}

\section{Theorem V: Explicit Gap Formula}

Let the diagonal \(OO\)-sector operator near defect \(A\) be
\begin{equation}
\mathcal O_{OO,A}^{(f)}
=
\mu_A^{(f)}
+
a_A^{(f)}\,\theta(\xi)^2
+
b_A^{(f)}\,(\theta'(\xi))^2.
\end{equation}
Then the diagonal entries are
\begin{equation}
d_A^{(f)}
=
\mu_A^{(f)}
+
a_A^{(f)}\theta_0^2\mathcal T_{\nu_f}
+
b_A^{(f)}\theta_0^2\kappa^2\mathcal S_{\nu_f},
\end{equation}
with
\[
\mathcal T_\nu=\frac{1}{2\nu+1},
\qquad
\mathcal S_\nu=\frac{4\nu(\nu+1)}{(2\nu+1)(2\nu+3)}.
\]

\begin{theorem}[Seed diagonal gaps]
The seed gaps are

\begin{equation} 
\Delta_{ij,\mathrm{seed}}^{(f)}
\&=
\mu_j^{(f)}-\mu_i^{(f)}
+
\bigl(a_j^{(f)}-a_i^{(f)}\bigr)\theta_0^2\frac{1}{2\nu_f+1}
\nonumber\\
\&\quad
+
\bigl(b_j^{(f)}-b_i^{(f)}\bigr)\theta_0^2\kappa^2
\frac{4\nu_f(\nu_f+1)}{(2\nu_f+1)(2\nu_f+3)}.
\label{eq:seed_gap_prx}
\end{equation}

\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Insert the explicit kink profile into the diagonal \(OO\)-sector expectation value. The \(\tanh^2\) and \(\sech^4\) moments reduce to beta-function ratios, yielding the stated closed expressions for \(\mathcal T_\nu\) and \(\mathcal S_\nu\). Subtracting two diagonal entries gives \eqref{eq:seed_gap_prx}.
\end{proof}

\section{Theorem VI: Explicit Residual Formula}

Let the projected Gram matrix be
\[
S=\mathbf 1+\sigma,
\qquad
\|\sigma\|\ll 1.
\]
Write the raw projected family matrix as
\[
N^{(f)}
=
\lambda_c^{(f)}\mathbf 1
+
D^{(f)}
+
\Lambda^{(f)}
+
\rho^{(f)}.
\]
Then
\[
\widehat Y^{(f)}=S^{-1/2}N^{(f)}S^{-1/2}
=
N^{(f)}-\frac12\{\sigma,N^{(f)}\}+O(\sigma^2).
\]

\begin{theorem}[Off-diagonal remainder]
For \(i\neq j\), the off-diagonal residual is
\begin{align}
\boxed{
r_{ij}^{(f)}
\&=
\rho_{ij}^{(f)}
-
\frac12\,\sigma_{ij}\bigl(2\lambda_c^{(f)}+d_i^{(f)}+d_j^{(f)}\bigr)
}
\nonumber\\
\&\quad
-
\frac12
\sum_{k\neq i,j}
\Bigl(
\sigma_{ik}\Lambda_{kj}^{(f)}
+
\Lambda_{ik}^{(f)}\sigma_{kj}
\Bigr)
+
O(\sigma\rho,\sigma^2).
\label{eq:rij_prx}
\end{align}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Expand \(\widehat Y^{(f)}\) to first order in \(\sigma\). The off-diagonal slot receives three contributions: the raw omitted residual \(\rho_{ij}^{(f)}\), direct normalization mixing of the diagonal operator into the off-diagonal entry, and feedthrough via a third channel. Collecting terms yields \eqref{eq:rij_prx}.
\end{proof}

\section{Theorem VII: Exact--Microscopic Consistency Inequality}

Define
\begin{equation}
M:=\max\bigl(|S_{12}|,\ |S_{23}|,\ |S_{13}+C_{\mathrm{mic}}|\bigr),
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\varepsilon:=\max\bigl(|E_{12}|,\ |E_{23}|,\ |\widetilde E_{13}|\bigr),
\end{equation}
where \(E_{ij}\) and \(\widetilde E_{13}\) are the normalized residual mismatch terms.
Let \(E_{\mathrm{BCH}}\) be any valid upper bound on the neglected higher-order BCH terms.

\begin{theorem}[Final consistency inequality]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item hierarchical normalized links,
\[
|L_{ij}^{(f)}|\ll 1;
\]
\item controlled normalization corrections,
\[
\|\sigma\|,\ \|\rho\|\ll 1;
\]
\item nondegenerate gaps,
\[
\Delta_{ij}^{(f)}\neq 0.
\]
\end{enumerate}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{exact}}-\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}\right|
\le
3M^2\varepsilon
+
3M\varepsilon^2
+
\varepsilon^3
+
E_{\mathrm{BCH}}
=:E_{\mathrm{tot}}.
}
\label{eq:final_consistency_prx}
\end{equation}
In particular, if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}|>E_{\mathrm{tot}},
}
\end{equation}
then the sign of \(J_{\mathrm{CKM}}\) is fixed by \(\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}\), and the microscopic route is consistent with the exact family route.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The discrepancy between the exact CKM invariant and the microscopic predictor comes from two sources only: normalized residual mismatch and higher-order BCH corrections. Expanding the difference between the exact cubic CKM invariant and the microscopic cubic cycle produces the seven correction monomials bounded by
\[
3M^2\varepsilon+3M\varepsilon^2+\varepsilon^3.
\]
Adding the explicit BCH remainder bound yields \eqref{eq:final_consistency_prx}.
\end{proof}

\section{Final Structural Closure Theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Structural flavor closure in TECT]
Under the assumptions of the previous theorems, the TECT flavor program is structurally closed in the following precise sense:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the full CKM problem is reduced to the finite family matrices \(\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d\);
\item the exact CKM CP invariant is given by \eqref{eq:exact_jarlskog_prx};
\item the microscopic CKM predictor is given by \eqref{eq:Xi_mic_prx};
\item the microscopic links are explicitly computable from the defect profile through \eqref{eq:literal_overlap_integral_prx};
\item the seed diagonal gaps are explicitly computable through \eqref{eq:seed_gap_prx};
\item the exact and microscopic routes are tied together by the finite consistency inequality \eqref{eq:final_consistency_prx}.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the flavor problem is reduced to a finite executable audit on the intended microscopic branch.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The statement follows by composition of Theorems I--VII.
\end{proof}

\section{Honest Final Diagnosis}

The honest final status is the following.

What is structurally proved:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{TECT flavor/CKM is reduced to a finite exact route and a finite microscopic route, together with an explicit consistency inequality.}
}
\end{equation}

What is still conditional:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the actual intended microscopic branch must still be numerically executed to fill the finite input tables and verify the final inequality.}
}
\end{equation}

Thus the correct PRX-level claim is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{structural closure: yes;}
\qquad
\text{actual branch numerical closure: finite and executable, but not yet universally completed.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The TECT flavor program yields two finite computational routes:
\[
(\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d)\to J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{exact}},
\qquad
(\Lambda,\Delta,r)\to \Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}\to J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{pred}}.
\]
The exact route is controlled by the commutator invariant
\[
\mathfrak J_{\mathrm{exact}}=\frac{1}{3i}\operatorname{tr}([\widehat Y_u,\widehat Y_d]^3),
\]
while the microscopic route is controlled by the rephasing-invariant three-link cycle
\[
\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}=\Im\!\Bigl(S_{12}S_{23}\overline{(S_{13}+C_{\mathrm{mic}})}\Bigr).
\]

The microscopic links are explicitly generated by the kink-profile overlap integral
\[
\Lambda_{AB}^{(f)}
=
\mathcal C_{AB}^{(f)}
\mathcal G_{AB}^{(f)}
\theta_0\mathcal N_f^2
\mathcal J_{\nu_f}(s_{AB}),
\]
and the diagonal gaps are explicitly generated by the diagonal \(OO\)-sector moments.
The two routes are tied together by the finite consistency inequality
\[
\left|J_{\mathrm{CKM}}^{\mathrm{exact}}-\Xi_{\mathrm{mic}}\right|\le E_{\mathrm{tot}}.
\]

Hence the CKM problem in TECT is no longer an open functional mystery.
It is a finite executable microscopic audit.

(\partial_i z)^\dagger (\partial_i z)
\end{equation}

\section{Emergent Connection}

\begin{equation}
A_i
=
-i z^\dagger \partial_i z
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
D_i z = (\partial_i - i A_i)z
\end{equation}

\section{Berry Curvature}

\begin{equation}
F_{ij}
=
\partial_i A_j - \partial_j A_i
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
F_{ij}
=
-i\left[
(\partial_i z^\dagger)(\partial_j z)
-
(\partial_j z^\dagger)(\partial_i z)
\right]
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
F_{ij}
=
i\, \mathrm{Tr}
\left(
P[\partial_i P, \partial_j P]
\right)
\end{equation}

\section{Topological Charge}

\begin{equation}
Q
=
\frac{1}{2\pi}
\int F_{ij}\, dx^i \wedge dx^j
\in \mathbb{Z}
\end{equation}

\section{Holonomy from Curvature}

\end{equation}

\begin{equation}

\int_{\Sigma_{123}} F_{ij} dS^{ij}
\end{equation}

\begin{pmatrix}

w(x) \\
0
\end{pmatrix}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}

\frac{x^1 + i x^2}{R(r)}
\end{equation}

\partial_1 w \partial_2 \bar w
-
\partial_2 w \partial_1 \bar w
\right|
\end{equation}

\section{Numerical Implementation Structure}

\begin{equation}
\Psi \rightarrow X_A \rightarrow z(x) \rightarrow A_i \rightarrow F_{ij}
\rightarrow \Phi \rightarrow M,Z \rightarrow U_u,U_d \rightarrow V_{\mathrm{CKM}}
\end{equation}

\begin{verbatim}

import numpy as np
from numpy.linalg import eigh

# -------------------------
# 1. grid + field init
# -------------------------
N = 64
L = 6.0
dx = L / N
x = np.linspace(-L/2, L/2, N)
X,Y,Z = np.meshgrid(x,x,x,indexing='ij')

# 초기 field (random + small)
Psi = np.random.randn(N,N,N) + 1j*np.random.randn(N,N,N)
Psi *= 0.1

mu, Zc, Yc, lam = 1.0, -1.0, 1.0, 1.0
eps = 0.01

# -------------------------
# 2. PDE solve (simple relax)
# -------------------------
for _ in range(200):
    lap = (
        np.roll(Psi,1,0)+np.roll(Psi,-1,0)+
        np.roll(Psi,1,1)+np.roll(Psi,-1,1)+
        np.roll(Psi,1,2)+np.roll(Psi,-1,2)-6*Psi
    ) / dx**2

    lap2 = (
        np.roll(lap,1,0)+np.roll(lap,-1,0)+
        np.roll(lap,1,1)+np.roll(lap,-1,1)+
        np.roll(lap,1,2)+np.roll(lap,-1,2)-6*lap
    ) / dx**2

    dPsi = -mu**2*Psi + Zc*lap - Yc*lap2 - lam*np.abs(Psi)**2*Psi
    Psi = Psi - eps*dPsi

# -------------------------
# 3. defect centers
# -------------------------
mag = np.abs(Psi)
flat_idx = np.argsort(mag.ravel())[-3:]
coords = np.array(np.unravel_index(flat_idx, mag.shape)).T

X_A = coords * dx - L/2

# -------------------------
# 4. CP2 field
# -------------------------
z = Psi / (np.abs(Psi) + 1e-12)

# -------------------------
# 5. Berry connection (x-direction only demo)
# -------------------------
def berry_phase(a,b):
    return -np.angle(np.vdot(a,b))

# 간단 holonomy (1→2→3 loop)
Phi = 0.0
for i in range(2):
    a = Psi[tuple(coords[i])]
    b = Psi[tuple(coords[i+1])]
    Phi += berry_phase(a,b)

# -------------------------
# 6. overlap (distance model)
# -------------------------
def overlap(xi,xj,kappa=1.2):
    d = np.linalg.norm(xi-xj)
    return np.exp(-kappa*d)

M = np.zeros((3,3))
for i in range(3):
    for j in range(3):
        M[i,j] = overlap(X_A[i], X_A[j])

# -------------------------
# 7. diagonalization
# -------------------------
eigvals, U = eigh(M)

# up/down slightly perturbed
Uu = U
Ud = U @ np.diag([1, np.exp(1j*Phi), 1])

# -------------------------
# 8. CKM
# -------------------------
V = Uu.conj().T @ Ud
Vabs = np.abs(V)

print("CKM =")
print(Vabs)
    
\end{verbatim}
